Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
7 min
Invalidation of Hajj by Anal Intercourse Before Wuquf
Ruling with proof from Companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for anal intercourse before wuquf, identify the proof from Companions, and apply the conditions that trigger invalidation.

Core Idea
Anal intercourse before wuquf invalidates hajj; a sheep sacrifice and qada are wajib.

The major sin of intercourse during hajj before the standing at Arafah can invalidate the pilgrimage, even if it occurs in the back passage. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its proof from the Companions, and the conditions under which invalidation occurs, clarifying common misconceptions about gender, coercion, and barriers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognise that the act in question is sexual intercourse in the back passage (dubur) while in ihram before the standing at Arafah. The ruling is that this act invalidates the hajj (fasād al-ḥajj), requiring continuation of the current hajj and re-performance (qaḍā) in a future year.
The term 'one of the two passages' (al-sabīlayn) includes both vagina and anus.
2
Locate the Dalil
The ruling is based on reports from the Companions (Sunnah aḥad) that such intercourse invalidates hajj and obligates a sacrificial animal. These reports are accepted as proof in the Hanafi school despite being zannī al-thubūt.
No specific Companion named in the text.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalālah
The Companions' practice and statements directly indicate that anal intercourse before wuquf triggers the same consequences as vaginal intercourse: invalidation of hajj and obligation of a sheep (dam) or share in a camel.
The text emphasises 'completeness of the offence' (kamāl al-jināyah) as the rationale.
4
Note the Ikhtilāf
There is a weaker narration from Abu Hanifa that anal intercourse does not invalidate hajj, but the stronger view (and that of the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is invalidation. The muftā bihī is invalidation.
Fath al-Qādir and other authorities declare this the more correct view.
5
Detail the Scope and Conditions
The ruling applies broadly: to man and woman, free and slave, intentional or forgetful, coerced or willing. Emission is not required; insertion of the glans suffices. Use of a cloth barrier invalidates only if heat and pleasure are felt. Bestiality does not invalidate.
A woman coerced by her husband: there is ikhtilāf on whether she can claim the blood penalty from him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو أفسد حجه بجماع في أحد السبيلين قبل الوقوف بعرفة) معطوف على «قبل» أي تجب شاة لما ورد عن الصحابة من الفساد به ووجوب الهدي وأدناه شاة، ويقوم الشرك في البدنة مقامها كما صرح به في غاية البيان. وما اختاره المصنف . الفساد بالجماع في الدبر هو أصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة كقولهما لكمال الجناية كما في فتح القدير. ومراده من آدمية، وأما وطء البهيمة فلا يفسد مطلقاً لقصوره. وأطلق في الجماع فشمل ما إذا أنزل أو لم ينزل، أولج ذكره كله أو بقدر الحشفة. وفي معراج الدراية ولو استدخلت ذكر الحمار أو ذكراً مقطوعاً يفسد حجها بالإجماع، ولو لف ذكره بخرقة وأدخله إن وجد حرارة الفرج واللذة يفسد وإلا فلا .انتهى وشمل ما إذا كان عامداً أو ناسياً عالماً أو جاهلاً، مختاراً أو مكرهاً، رجلاً أو امرأة، ولا رجوع له على المكره كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وحكى في فتح خلافاً بين ابن شجاع والقاضي أبي حازم في رجوع المرأة بالدم إذا أكرهها الزوج على الجماع فقال الأول ،لا، وقال الثاني ،نعم، ولم أر قولاً في رجوعها بمؤنة حجها. وشمل الحر والعبد لكن في العبد يلزمه الهدي وقضاء الحج بعد العتق سوى حجة الإسلام، وكل ما
His statement: 'Or he invalidates his hajj by intercourse in one of the two passages before standing at Arafah' is coordinated with 'before' – meaning a sheep is required due to what is narrated from the Companions of invalidation by it and the obligation of a sacrificial animal, the minimum of which is a sheep. And a share in a camel stands in its place as clarified in Ghayat al-Bayan. And what the author chose: invalidation by intercourse in the back passage is the more correct of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, like the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the completeness of the offense, as in Fath al-Qadir. And his intent is human. As for bestiality, it does not invalidate absolutely due to its deficiency. And he made intercourse absolute, so it includes whether he emitted or not, inserted his entire penis or the amount of the glans. And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: If she inserts a donkey's penis or a severed penis, her hajj is invalidated by consensus; if he wrapped his penis in a cloth and inserted it, if he finds the heat of the vulva and pleasure, it invalidates, otherwise not. End. And it includes whether intentional or forgetful, knowing or ignorant, voluntary or coerced, man or woman, and he has no recourse against the coercer as mentioned by al-Asbajabi. And in Fath al-Qadir, a disagreement is narrated between Ibn Shuja' and Qadi Abu Hazim regarding the woman's recourse for blood if the husband coerced her to intercourse: the former said no, the latter said yes, and I have not seen a statement regarding her recourse for the expenses of her hajj. And it includes free and slave, but regarding the slave, the sacrificial animal and qada of hajj are incumbent upon him after emancipation, apart from the Hajj of Islam, and everything...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on intercourse in the back passage (dubur) during ihram before the standing at Arafah. The matn states that such an act invalidates hajj. The commentator explains that this is based on Companions' reports. The obligation is a sheep (dam), but a share in a camel suffices. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that anal intercourse invalidates hajj, which is the more correct narration from Abu Hanifa, agreeing with the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because it constitutes a complete offense. However, bestiality does not invalidate hajj. The ruling includes many details: emission is not required; the full glans or entire penis insertion suffices; even inserting an inanimate object like a donkey's penis or a severed penis invalidates the woman's hajj by consensus. If a cloth barrier is used, invalidation depends on feeling heat and pleasure. The ruling applies regardless of intent, knowledge, coercion, gender, or freedom status. For coerced sex, the woman has no recourse for the blood penalty according to one view, but there is a difference of opinion. For a slave, the sacrifice and qada are required after emancipation.

Key Terms
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (vagina) and the back (anus). Intercourse in either before wuquf invalidates hajj.
فساد الحج (fasād al-ḥajj): Invalidation of hajj, requiring continuation (imda) and completion, then qada (re-performance) in a future year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a muhrim engages in anal intercourse before the standing at Arafah?
A) Hajj is invalidated and a sheep is required
B) Hajj remains valid but a sheep is required
C) Hajj is invalidated only if emission occurs
D) No penalty because it is not vaginal intercourse

Key Takeaway
Anal intercourse before wuquf invalidates hajj in the Hanafi school, obligating a sheep sacrifice and qada, with the ruling applying broadly to all pilgrims regardless of intent or coercion.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Intercourse Spoils Hajj: Ruling, Evidence, and Sub-Cases
Commentary on the ruling of intercourse spoiling Hajj and related expiations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse spoiling Hajj before Arafat, identify the companion-based evidence, and apply the conditions and expiations for various sub-cases including bestiality, coercion, and repetition.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Arafat spoils Hajj; a sheep is obligatory and the Hajj must be repeated, with distinctions for human vs animal, minor vs adult, and single vs multiple acts.

This lesson unpacks the detailed Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse during Hajj before the stop at Arafat. Based on companion reports, the school holds that such intercourse invalidates the Hajj, requiring both completion and later repetition, along with a blood penalty. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies numerous sub-rulings including anal intercourse, bestiality, coercion, and multiple occurrences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is jima' (intercourse) before standing at Arafat. It spoils the Hajj entirely, making it wajib to complete the rites (imda') and repeat the Hajj (qada) in another year. A blood penalty (dam) of a sheep or its equivalent is also wajib.
This is the foundational ruling; all other sub-rulings build on this.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence comes from reports of the Sahabah (companions) that such intercourse spoils Hajj and requires a hady (sacrificial animal), with the minimum being a sheep. This qawl sahabi serves as the dalil.
The authority is zanni in transmission but relied upon in the school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The wording 'لما ورد عن الصحابة من الفساد به ووجوب الهدي' directly indicates that the companions established both corruption and obligation of a sacrifice. The Hanafi school accepts this as sufficient proof.
This step links the proof to the ruling.
4
Examine the conditions and scope
Define jima' as insertion of the glans (hashafah) or the entire penis into either the front or rear passage of a human. Explore conditions: occurrence before Arafat, human partner, intentional or coerced, knowing or ignorant. The act spoils Hajj regardless of emission.
Anal intercourse spoils Hajj according to the stronger narration from Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply to special cases
Apply the ruling to bestiality (does not spoil Hajj but requires blood), touching with emission (requires blood, does not spoil), minors and insane (Hajj spoiled but no blood due to harm), and repetition of intercourse (one blood if in one sitting; additional blood if in separate sittings without intention to discard the spoiled Hajj).
The intention to reject ihram by further violations results in a single blood for all.

فكفاه دم واحد ، ولهذا نص في ظاهر الرواية أن المحرم إذا جامع النساء ورفض إحرامه وأقام يصنع ما يصنعه الحلال من الجماع والطيب وقتل الصيد عليه أن يعود كما كان حراماً ويلزمه دم واحد كما ذكره في المبسوط وغيره والثاني أي الجواز عن الكرماني ثم قال : لكن بقي ما إذا استدان وهو مأذون أو مكاتب لم أر من تعرض له مع أنه أولى بالجواز من التبرع عنه قوله : (وشمل الوطء الحلال والحرام) أي الوطء لخليلته أو لأجنبية وإلا فالوطء هنا كله حرام يعارض الإحرام قوله : وبهذا ظهر ضعف ما في فتح القدير) قال في النهر : يدل على ذلك قولهم لو أفسد الصبي حجه لا قضاء عليه ولا يتأتى ذلك بغير الجماع اهـ. قال في الشرنبلالية وفيه تأمل لأن الفساد لا ينحصر في الجماع إذ يكون بفوت الوقوف بعرفة قوله : (لأنه لا يخرج عنه إلا بالأعمال قال في الشرنبلالية : ينظر فيه مع ما سنذكره من تحليل المولى أمته بنحو قص ظفر وبالجماع وإن كان لا ينبغي له فعله ابتداء ا هـ . وقد يقال : المنظور إليه هنا خصوص هذا المجامع وهو لا يخرج إلا بالأعمال قوله : (لكن لما كانت المخظورات الخ) يعني أنه وإن أخطأ في تأويله يرتفع عنه الضمان لما ذكر فإن التأويل الفاسد معتبر في رفع الضمان كالباغي إذا أتلف مال العادل فإنه لا يضمن لأنه أتلف عن تأويل كما في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي قوله (ولهذا نص في ظاهر الرواية الخ) قال في اللباب : اعلم أن المحرم إذا نوى رفض الإحرام فجعل يصنع ما يصنعه الحلال من لبس الثياب والتطيب والحلق والجماع وقتل الصيد فإنه لا يخرج بذلك من الإحرام وعليه أن يعود كما كان محرماً، ويجب دم واحد لجميع ما ارتكب ولو كل المحظورات وإنما يتعدد الجزاء بتعدد الجنايات إذا لم ينو الرفض، ثم نية الرفض إنما تعتبر ممن زعم
Or if he spoils his Hajj by intercourse in one of the two passages before standing at Arafat, he proceeds and makes up and they do not separate. It has been said: The obligation of blood is only because he committed what is forbidden due to ihram alone, and mentioning intercourse in the presence of women is not prohibited only for ihram but is absolutely prohibited, though more severe in ihram. By this, the preference of the book's absolute statement is shown, because the [؟] are forbidden for ihram absolutely, so blood is obligatory absolutely. The Hajj is not spoiled by [؟] with emission as fasting is spoiled by them, because its corruption is connected to actual intercourse by the text, and intercourse is a different meaning so it was not annexed to it. As for the corruption of fasting, it is dependent on fulfillment of desire, and it occurred. In al-Muhit: A muhrim who plays with his penis has nothing on him, and if he emits, he owes blood because he fulfilled desire by touch, as if he touched a woman and emitted. If he copulated with an animal and emitted, his Hajj is not spoiled and he owes blood, as if he had intercourse below the glans. If he does not emit, nothing on him. Because from his saying: (Or if he spoils his Hajj by intercourse in one of the two passages before standing at Arafat) is conjunct to 'before', i.e., a sheep is obligatory due to what was reported from the Companions about corruption by it and the obligation of a sacrificial animal, the least of which is a sheep. The share in a camel stands in its place, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. What the author chose—corruption by anal intercourse—is the more correct of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, like the two of them, due to the completeness of the offense, as in Fath al-Qadir. He means from a human; as for bestiality, it does not corrupt absolutely due to its deficiency. He gave absolute license in intercourse, so it includes whether he emitted or not, inserted his entire penis or to the extent of the glans. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: If she inserted a donkey's penis or a severed penis, her Hajj is corrupted by consensus. If he wrapped his penis in a cloth and inserted, if he found the heat of the vulva and pleasure, it corrupts; otherwise not. It includes whether intentional or forgetful, knowing or ignorant, voluntary or coerced, man or woman. He has no recourse against the one who coerced him, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. In Fath, a dispute is reported between Ibn Shuja' and al-Qadi Abu Hazim regarding the woman's recourse for the blood if the husband coerced her to intercourse: the first said no, the second said yes. I have not seen a statement about her recourse for the expenses of her Hajj. It includes free and slave, but for the slave, he must give a sacrificial animal and make up the Hajj after manumission, apart from the Hajj of Islam. Everything that requires monetary payment is exacted after his manumission, unlike what requires fasting, which is exacted immediately. It is not permissible for the master to feed on his behalf except in the case of ihsar, where the master sends on his behalf so that he may become halal; then if he is freed, he owes a Hajj and an Umrah. It includes lawful and unlawful intercourse, and intercourse of the legally responsible and others, as stated in al-Muhit. Al-Walwaliji stated that the boy and the insane person corrupt their Hajj by intercourse, but no blood is due on them. In Manasik Ibn al-Dhiya: If a boy has intercourse such that his Hajj is spoiled, nothing is required of him. By this, the weakness of what is in Fath al-Qadir is shown: 'If the husband is a boy who is capable of intercourse, her Hajj is spoiled but not his; if the wife is a young girl or insane, the ruling is reversed.' This is a ruling connected to the essence of intercourse and to an excuse; intercourse is not absent, so the ruling connected to it is not absent. They are not held to the ruling of corruption due to the harm in it. It is supported by the fact that the corruptor of prayer and fasting does not differ between the legally responsible and others, so too Hajj. It includes when intercourse is repeated; he owes one blood if the gathering is single, whether with one woman or multiple women. If the gathering is multiple and he did not intend by it to reject the spoiled Hajj, he owes another blood according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. If he intended by the second intercourse to reject the corrupted one, nothing is due for the second, as in Fatawa Qadikhan, even though the intention of rejection is invalid because he does not exit except through actions. But since the prohibitions are based on a single intention—namely, hastening release—they are unified, so one blood suffices him. For this reason, it is stated in Zahir al-Riwayah that if a muhrim has intercourse with women and rejects his ihram and proceeds to do what a halal person does—intercourse, perfume, hunting—he must return to being prohibited, and one blood is owed, as mentioned in al-Mabsut and others. The second (meaning the permissibility from al-Kirmani) then said: But remaining is if he borrows while being authorized or a mukatib—I have not seen anyone address it, though it is more deserving of permissibility than donating on his behalf. His saying: (It includes lawful and unlawful intercourse) means intercourse with his sweetheart or a foreign woman; otherwise, intercourse here is all unlawful, conflicting with ihram. His saying: By this the weakness of what is in Fath al-Qadir is shown. In al-Nahr: This is indicated by their statement: If a boy spoils his Hajj, no make-up is required, and that is not attained except by intercourse. In al-Shurnublaliyya: There is contemplation because corruption is not confined to intercourse; it can also occur by missing the stop at Arafat. His saying: (Because he does not exit except through actions). In al-Shurnublaliyya: It requires consideration with what we will mention of the master's analytical statement of his slave girl by cutting a nail and by intercourse, even if he should not do it initially. It may be said: The consideration here is specifically this person who has intercourse; he does not exit except through actions. His saying: (But since the prohibitions...) means that even if he erred in his interpretation, the liability is lifted due to what was mentioned, for an invalid interpretation is considered in removing liability, like a rebel who destroys the property of a just person—he does not compensate because he destroyed based on an interpretation, as in al-Shurnublaliyya from al-Kafi. His saying (For this reason it is stated in Zahir al-Riwayah...) In al-Lubab: Know that if a muhrim intends to reject ihram and begins to do what a halal person does—wearing clothes, applying perfume, shaving, intercourse, hunting—he does not exit ihram by that, and he must return to being prohibited. One blood is owed for all he committed, even if all prohibitions. The penalty is multiplied only by multiple offenses if he did not intend rejection. The intention of rejection is only considered from one who claims...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the ruling on sexual intercourse (jima') during Hajj before standing at Arafat, which spoils the Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The author first establishes that the obligation of blood (dam) is due because the act is prohibited by virtue of ihram. He contrasts with other prohibitions like talking about intercourse, which are not specifically tied to ihram. The passage then clarifies that while desire (dawa'i) alone with emission does not spoil Hajj unlike fasting, because the corruption of Hajj is textually linked to actual intercourse. The text then covers various sub-rulings: touching with desire ( 'abath bi-dhakarihi ) requires blood if emission occurs; bestiality does not spoil Hajj but requires blood; the definition of intercourse includes full insertion or insertion to the glans, regardless of emission. The commentator also discusses the case of anal intercourse (jima' fi al-dubur), stating that the chosen position is that it spoils Hajj, as per the stronger narration from Abu Hanifa, akin to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage further addresses issues of coercion, ignorance, and the status of slaves, minors, and the insane. For a slave, the blood and make-up Hajj are required after manumission. For a minor, the Hajj is spoiled but no blood is due, differing from the statement in Fath al-Qadir which is criticized as weak. The commentary also covers repetition of intercourse: if multiple acts occur in one sitting, one blood suffices; if in separate sittings without intention to reject the spoiled Hajj, additional blood is required. If the muhrim intends to reject ihram by his acts, a single blood is due for all prohibitions according to Zahir al-Riwayah. The overall aim is to provide detailed guidance on the expiation for sexual offenses during Hajj.

Key Terms
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse, specifically insertion of the glans into the front or rear private part of a human. Includes both vaginal and anal intercourse.
دم (dam): A penalty blood (a sheep or equivalent) owed for committing a prohibited act during Ihram that does not invalidate the Hajj entirely, or as expiation for invalidating the Hajj.
فساد الحج (fasad al-hajj): Invalidation of the Hajj due to a major violation, requiring its completion (imda') and later repetition (qada) in another year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person copulates with an animal during Hajj and emits?
A) His Hajj is spoiled and he owes an animal sacrifice.
B) His Hajj is not spoiled, but he owes a blood penalty.
C) His Hajj is spoiled, but no further penalty is required.
D) Nothing is required if he did not intend to violate ihram.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before Arafat spoils Hajj; a sheep is wajib; the pilgrim must complete the spoiled Hajj and repeat it.

Multiple Acts of Intercourse in Ihram: When One Dam Suffices
Explaining the ruling on multiple acts of intercourse in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules to determine the number of dams required for multiple acts of intercourse in ihram, considering whether they occur in one sitting or separate sittings, and whether the intent was to nullify ihram.

Core Idea
Multiple violations in ihram are treated as one if they share a single intent to hasten tahlil, reducing the penalty to one dam.

This lesson examines the detailed rulings on repeated intercourse during ihram. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a single sitting (majlis wahid) and separate sittings, and considers the intention behind the actions. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying the penalty (dam) system in hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the number of sittings
Determine if the acts occurred in one sitting (e.g., same tent, continuous session) or multiple separate sittings (e.g., different days, different locations).
A single sitting may include multiple acts with one or multiple women.
2
Assess the intent
If in multiple sittings, check if the muhrim intended to nullify his ihram with the later acts. This intent, though invalid in itself (since ihram cannot be exited by intention alone), changes the penalty.
The intent to nullify indicates the goal of hastening tahlil.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
If one sitting → one dam for all acts. If multiple sittings without nullification intent → one dam per sitting (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). If multiple sittings with nullification intent → one dam for all acts.
Regardless of the number of women.
4
Understand the rationale (istihsan)
The prohibited acts are considered unified because they stem from a single goal of hastening tahlil. This istihsan overrides the general rule that each violation requires a separate penalty.
This principle is supported by the ruling in Zahir al-Riwaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل الوطء الحلال والحرام ووطء المكلف وغيره كما صرح به في المحيط، وصرح الولوالجي بأن الصبي والمعتوه يفسد حجهما بالجماع لكن لا دم عليهما، وفي مناسك ابن الضياء : وإذا جامع الصبي حتى فسد حجه لا يلزمه شيء انتهى. وبهذا ظهر ضعف ما في فتح القدير من قوله : ولو كان الزوج صبياً يجامع مثله فسد حجها دونه، ولو كانت صبية أو مجنونة انعكس الحكم انتهى. فإن هذا حكم تعلق بعين الجماع وبالعذر لا ينعدم الجماع فلا ينعدم الحكم المتعلق به، وإنما لم يلزمهما حكم الفساد لما فيه من الضرر، ويؤيده أن المفسد للصلاة والصوم لا فرق فيه بين المكلف وغيره فكذلك الحج. وشمل ما إذا تعدد الجماع فإنه يلزمه دم واحد إن كان المجلس متحداً، يصنع ما يصنعه الحلال من الجماع والطيب وقتل الصيد عليه أن يعود كما كان حراماً ويلزمه دم واحد كما ذكره في المبسوط . وغيره والثاني أي الجواز عن الكرماني ثم قال : لكن بقي ما إذا استدان وهو مأذون أو مكاتب لم أر من تعرض له مع أنه أولى بالجواز من التبرع عنه قوله : (وشمل الوطء الحلال والحرام) أي الوطء لخليلته أو لأجنبية وإلا فالوطء هنا كله حرام يعارض الإحرام قوله : وبهذا ظهر ضعف ما في فتح القدير) قال في النهر : يدل على ذلك قولهم لو أفسد الصبي حجه لا قضاء عليه ولا يتأتى ذلك بغير الجماع اهـ. قال في الشرنبلالية وفيه تأمل لأن الفساد لا ينحصر في الجماع إذ يكون بفوت الوقوف بعرفة قوله : (لأنه لا يخرج عنه إلا بالأعمال قال في الشرنبلالية : ينظر فيه مع ما سنذكره من تحليل المولى أمته بنحو قص ظفر وبالجماع وإن كان لا ينبغي له فعله ابتداء ا هـ . وقد يقال : المنظور إليه هنا خصوص هذا المجامع وهو لا يخرج إلا بالأعمال قوله : (لكن لما كانت المخظورات الخ) يعني أنه وإن أخطأ في تأويله يرتفع . عنه الضمان لما ذكر فإن التأويل الفاسد معتبر في رفع الضمان كالباغي إذا أتلف مال العادل فإنه لا يضمن لأنه أتلف عن تأويل كما في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي قوله (ولهذا نص في ظاهر الرواية الخ) قال في اللباب : اعلم أن المحرم إذا نوى رفض الإحرام فجعل يصنع ما يصنعه الحلال من لبس الثياب والتطيب والحلق والجماع وقتل الصيد فإنه لا يخرج بذلك من الإحرام وعليه أن يعود كما كان محرماً، ويجب دم واحد لجميع ما ارتكب ولو كل المحظورات وإنما يتعدد الجزاء بتعدد الجنايات إذا لم ينو الرفض، ثم نية الرفض إنما تعتبر ممن زعم أنه خرج منه بهذا And it includes lawful and unlawful intercourse, and intercourse of the legally responsible and others, as stated in al-Muhit. And al-Walwaliji stated that the child and the insane person invalidate their hajj by intercourse, but no dam is required of them. And in Manasik of Ibn al-Dhiya: If a child had intercourse such that his hajj became invalid, nothing is required of him. End. And by this the weakness of what is in Fath al-Qadir is apparent, from his statement: If the husband was a boy who could engage in intercourse, her hajj becomes invalid without him, and if she was a girl or insane, the ruling is reversed. End. For this ruling is connected to the act of intercourse itself and to the excuse; the intercourse is not absent, so the ruling connected to it is not absent. Rather, the ruling of invalidity was not required of them due to harm. And it is supported by the fact that the invalidator of prayer and fasting does not differentiate between the legally responsible and others, so too for hajj. And it includes if intercourse is repeated: one dam is required if the sitting is one, whether with one woman or multiple women. But if the sitting is multiple and he did not intend by it to nullify the corrupt hajj, another dam is required according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And if he intended by the second intercourse to nullify the corrupt one, nothing is required of him by the second. This is in Fatawa Qadikhan, even though the intention to nullify is invalid because he cannot exit except through actions. But because the prohibited acts are based on a single intent, which is hastening tahlil, they are unified, so one dam suffices him. And for this reason it is stated in Zahir al-Riwayah that if a muhrim had intercourse with women and nullified his ihram and began doing what a halal person does, such as intercourse, perfume, and hunting, then he must return as he was in ihram, and one dam is required of him, as mentioned in al-Mabsut and others. And the second: permission from al-Kirmani. Then he said: But what remains is if he borrowed while being a ma'dhun or mukatab, I have not seen anyone address it, though it is more deserving of permission than donating on his behalf. His statement: (And it includes lawful and unlawful intercourse) i.e., intercourse with his concubine or a foreign woman; otherwise, intercourse here is all unlawful opposing ihram. His statement: And by this the weakness of what is in Fath al-Qadir is apparent. Al-Nahr said: That indicates their statement: If a child corrupted his hajj, no make-up is required of him, and that is not possible without intercourse. End. Al-Shurnubulali said: There is reflection in it because corruption is not limited to intercourse, as it can occur by missing the standing at Arafat. His statement: (Because he cannot exit except through actions). Al-Shurnubulali said: It should be considered with what we will mention of the master tahlil of his slave girl by cutting a nail and by intercourse, even if he should not do it initially. End. It may be said: The focus here is specifically on this person who engaged in intercourse, and he cannot exit except through actions. His statement: (But because the prohibited acts are based on a single intent) means that even if he erred in his interpretation, liability is removed from him for what was mentioned, for erroneous interpretation is considered in removing liability, like the transgressor if he destroys the property of a just person, he does not guarantee because he destroyed based on interpretation, as in al-Shurnubulali from al-Kafi. His statement: (And for this reason it is stated in Zahir al-Riwayah). Al-Lubab said: Know that if a muhrim intends to nullify ihram and begins doing what a halal person does, like wearing clothes, applying perfume, shaving, intercourse, and hunting, he does not thereby exit from ihram, and he must return as he was in ihram, and one dam is required for all he committed, even if all prohibited acts. And the penalty only multiplies with multiple violations if he did not intend nullification. Then the intention of nullification is only considered from one who claims that he exited by this intention due to ignorance of the issue of non-exit. But one who knows that he does not exit by this intention, it is not considered from him. End. And his commentator said: Likewise, it should not be considered from him if he is doubtful about the issue or forgetful of it.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically dealing with the chapter on violations in hajj (bab al-jinayat). The author, Ibn Nujaym, clarifies several rulings regarding intercourse in ihram. First, he states that the term 'wati' (intercourse) in the matn includes both lawful (with one's wife) and unlawful (with a stranger) intercourse, and applies to both the legally responsible (mukallaf) and others like children and the insane. However, children and insane persons are not required to pay a dam because of harm, though their hajj is still invalidated. This is supported by analogy to prayer and fasting where invalidation applies to all. Next, the author addresses multiple acts of intercourse: if they occur in a single sitting, only one dam is required, regardless of the number of women. But if they occur in separate sittings without the intent to nullify the corrupt hajj, a separate dam is required for each sitting according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. If the muhrim intends by the second intercourse to nullify the corrupt hajj, no additional dam is required, even though the intention to nullify is invalid because one cannot exit ihram merely by intention but only by completing the rituals. Nevertheless, since all prohibited acts stem from the single goal of hastening tahlil, they are considered unified, and one dam suffices. The passage then discusses the ruling when someone actually acts on the intention to nullify ihram by wearing clothes, applying perfume, etc. According to Zahir al-Riwaya, he does not exit ihram and must return to ihram, and only one dam is required for all violations. The intention of nullification is only considered from someone who is ignorant that it does not work; if he knows, it is not considered. Likewise, if he is doubtful or forgetful, it is not considered.

Key Terms
وطء (wati'): Sexual intercourse, whether lawful (with spouse) or unlawful.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as penalty for certain ihram violations.
رفض الإحرام (rafḍ al-iḥrām): The intention to nullify ihram and acting accordingly, though it does not actually exit one from ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a muhrim has intercourse twice in one sitting (majlis wahid), how many dams are required?
A) Two dams, one for each act
B) One dam
C) No dam
D) It depends on the number of women

Key Takeaway
The number of dams for multiple acts of intercourse in ihram depends on whether they occur in one sitting and whether the intent is to nullify ihram; a single sitting or a unified intent results in one dam.

Children and the Insane in Ihram: Invalidation Without Dam
Explaining the ruling on children/insane persons in ihram and critique of a contrary view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a child or insane person's intercourse invalidates their hajj but does not require a dam, using the Hanafi qiyas to prayer and fasting.

Core Idea
Legal responsibility is required for penalty, not for invalidation — children and insane persons invalidate their hajj but owe no dam.

This lesson addresses a specific case: if a child or an insane person engages in intercourse while in ihram, their hajj is invalidated, but no dam is required. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) to prayer and fasting, where invalidation applies to all but penalty only to the legally responsible. We also examine a critique of a contrary view found in Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The act of intercourse invalidates the hajj of a child or insane person, but no dam is required of them.
This is stated by al-Walwaliji and in Manasik of Ibn al-Dhiya'.
2
Understand the exception
The invalidation is attached to the act itself, not to the person's legal responsibility. However, the penalty (dam) is waived due to the harm (lack of liability) that would be caused by requiring it.
The ruling in Fath al-Qadir that a child's intercourse only invalidates the wife's hajj is rejected.
3
Apply the qiyas
Analogize to prayer and fasting: if a child or insane person commits an invalidating act (e.g., eating during fasting), the act invalidates but no penalty (kafarah) is required. Similarly for hajj, intercourse invalidates but no dam.
The illa (effective cause) is the lack of legal responsibility, which removes penalty but not invalidation.
4
Critique the opposing view
The author points out the weakness in Fath al-Qadir's claim that a child's intercourse only invalidates his wife's hajj. The correct view is that both the child and the wife have their hajj invalidated, but the child owes no dam.
The invalidation is connected to the act of intercourse itself, unaffected by the excuse.

Al-Shurnubulali said: It should be considered with what we will mention of the master tahlil of his slave girl by cutting a nail and by intercourse, even if he should not do it initially. End. It may be said: The focus here is specifically on this person who engaged in intercourse, and he cannot exit except through actions. His statement: (But because the prohibited acts are based on a single intent) means that even if he erred in his interpretation, liability is removed from him for what was mentioned, for erroneous interpretation is considered in removing liability, like the transgressor if he destroys the property of a just person, he does not guarantee because he destroyed based on interpretation, as in al-Shurnubulali from al-Kafi. His statement: (And for this reason it is stated in Zahir al-Riwayah). Al-Lubab said: Know that if a muhrim intends to nullify ihram and begins doing what a halal person does, like wearing clothes, applying perfume, shaving, intercourse, and hunting, he does not thereby exit from ihram, and he must return as he was in ihram, and one dam is required for all he committed, even if all prohibited acts. And the penalty only multiplies with multiple violations if he did not intend nullification. Then the intention of nullification is only considered from one who claims that he exited by this intention due to ignorance of the issue of non-exit. But one who knows that he does not exit by this intention, it is not considered from him. End. And his commentator said: Likewise, it should not be considered from him if he is doubtful about the issue or forgetful of it.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically dealing with the chapter on violations in hajj (bab al-jinayat). The author, Ibn Nujaym, clarifies several rulings regarding intercourse in ihram. First, he states that the term 'wati' (intercourse) in the matn includes both lawful (with one's wife) and unlawful (with a stranger) intercourse, and applies to both the legally responsible (mukallaf) and others like children and the insane. However, children and insane persons are not required to pay a dam because of harm, though their hajj is still invalidated. This is supported by analogy to prayer and fasting where invalidation applies to all. Next, the author addresses multiple acts of intercourse: if they occur in a single sitting, only one dam is required, regardless of the number of women. But if they occur in separate sittings without the intent to nullify the corrupt hajj, a separate dam is required for each sitting according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. If the muhrim intends by the second intercourse to nullify the corrupt hajj, no additional dam is required, even though the intention to nullify is invalid because one cannot exit ihram merely by intention but only by completing the rituals. Nevertheless, since all prohibited acts stem from the single goal of hastening tahlil, they are considered unified, and one dam suffices. The passage then discusses the ruling when someone actually acts on the intention to nullify ihram by wearing clothes, applying perfume, etc. According to Zahir al-Riwaya, he does not exit ihram and must return to ihram, and only one dam is required for all violations. The intention of nullification is only considered from someone who is ignorant that it does not work; if he knows, it is not considered. Likewise, if he is doubtful or forgetful, it is not considered.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabī): A child who has not reached puberty (ghayr baligh).
معتوه (ma'tūh): An insane or mentally deficient person who lacks legal responsibility.
فسد (fasada): Becomes invalid (fasad) — the hajj is corrupted and must be made up later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a child in ihram has intercourse, what is the ruling on his hajj and the penalty?
A) Hajj valid, no penalty
B) Hajj invalid, no penalty
C) Hajj invalid, penalty of dam required
D) Hajj valid, penalty of dam required

Key Takeaway
A child or insane person's intercourse invalidates their hajj but does not require a dam, because invalidation attaches to the act while penalty requires legal responsibility.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Completing and Making Up a Corrupted Hajj
Explaining that one must continue in a corrupted hajj and then make it up the following year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on continuing in a corrupted hajj and explain why the make-up hajj is considered 'ada (performance) rather than qada.

Core Idea
A corrupted hajj does not void the obligation; complete the rites and the 'make-up' is actually the obligatory hajj itself.

When a pilgrim corrupts their hajj, confusion often arises about whether to stop or continue. The Hanafi school provides a clear framework: one must persist in the remaining rites and then repeat the hajj in a valid form. This lesson unpacks that ruling and explores the subtle distinction between qada (make-up) and 'ada (performance) in the context of hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a corrupted hajj (hajj fasid). According to the matn, the ruling is that one must continue in the rites and then make it up the following year. Determine the hukm level (wajib).
The ruling applies whether it is the obligatory hajj or a supererogatory one that became obligatory to complete.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage uses qiyas to the prayer (salah) analogy: if one corrupts the dhuhr prayer in its time, performing it again fulfills the obligation without a separate qada. Similarly for hajj, the repeated hajj is not a new debt but the original obligation performed correctly.
The dalil is a rational analogy (qiyas), not a direct text, but it is firmly grounded in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In prayer, the time for dhuhr is limited, so repeating it within the same time is 'ada (performance). For hajj, one's entire lifetime is the time of obligation, so performing hajj again after corruption is also 'ada, not qada.
This hinges on the Hanafi principle that hajj is obligatory immediately (fawr) but can be delayed within one's lifetime.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) may consider the repeated hajj as qada because it replaces a deficient performance. The Hanafi school rejects this, as the corruption does not create a new obligation.
The practical difference: if the make-up hajj is also corrupted, Hanafis say only one hajj is owed (the original). Others may require another make-up.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi), supported by later authorities like al-Kamal ibn al-Humam. The correct view is that the repeated hajj is the obligatory hajj itself, performed correctly.
This resolves the student's question: no additional hajj is required beyond the original obligation.

يبطله كما في المضمرات. قال المصنف - يعني صاحب اللباب - فأفاد أن المراد من الفساد النقص الفاحش لا البطلان، وهو قيد حسن يزيل بعض الإشكالات قلت من جملتها في الأفعال لكن في عدم الإبطال أيضاً نوع من His statement: (And he continues and makes it up, and they are not different in it) i.e., it is obligatory to continue in the acts of hajj after corrupting it, just as he continues in it while it is valid, and he is required to make it up the following year, whether it was the hajj of Islam or not, because he performed the acts with the description of corruption, while what is due on him is performance with the description of validity. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: He avoids in the corrupt hajj what he avoids in the acceptable hajj. And some of our contemporaries thought that if hajj becomes corrupt, the ihram does not become corrupt, and for this reason they said that the ihram remains, so he performs qada in it, but it is not as they thought; rather, it became corrupt. Ramadan that he exited by this intention due to ignorance of the issue of non-exit. But one who knows that he does not exit by this intention, it is not considered from him. End. His commentator said: Likewise, it should not be considered from him if he is doubtful about the issue or forgetful of it. His statement: (And he is required to make it up the following year). Al-Nahr said: Some students at al-Azhar Mosque asked me about if the make-up also becomes corrupt, must he also make it up? I said: I have not seen the issue, and by analogy, since he only commenced it as a means of discharge, not as a binding obligation, the intended meaning of 'qada' is its linguistic meaning, and the intended meaning is 'i'ada' (repetition), as is apparent. End. The conclusion is that only one hajj is required of him for the one he first corrupted, and a second hajj is not required for the one he corrupted second. His statement is clear in terms of ruling, and Sheikh Ismail transmitted it from al-Mubtagha, saying: The wording of al-Mubtagha: If a person missed hajj and then performed hajj the following year intending to make up that hajj, and then corrupted that hajj, he only needs to make up one hajj, just as if he corrupted the make-up of fasting. End. As for his statement that the intended meaning of 'qada' is... there is ambiguity in it. If he meant that the intended meaning of 'qada' is perfection and precision, it is not suitable here. And if he meant by it performance, as one says 'qadaytu al-dayn' meaning I paid the debt, then his statement 'and the intended meaning is i'ada' contradicts it, unless the waw is in the sense of 'aw' (or). But there is in it that i'ada is doing something similar to the obligatory in its time due to a defect other than corruption and lack of validity of commencement, and it does not occur here. Yes, it is possible according to the well-known definition of the Shafi'is, which is doing something a second time in the time of performance due to a defect in its first performance. So the correct thing is to delete his statement 'and the intended meaning is i'ada' and restrict to explaining that the intended meaning of 'qada' is performance, as indicated by the statement of al-Kamal in al-Tahrir: 'Calling the valid hajj after the corrupt hajj 'qada' is metaphorical.' Al-Halabi said in his commentary: Because it is in its time, which is one's lifetime, so it is performance according to the view of our scholars. End. Since it is performance according to us, the question falls entirely, because the first hajj is void; if he performs it correctly, he fulfills the obligation, otherwise not. So he must perform it a second time, third time, and so on until he performs it correctly. What he does after the corrupt is not a non-obligatory hajj, but rather it is the obligatory hajj if it is valid, and the previous one does not require qada at all. For if, for example, he performed dhuhr prayer in its time and corrupted it, then performed it a second time, he fulfills the obligation, and no one imagines that another prayer is owed as qada for the one he commenced and corrupted. Similarly, what we presented from al-Mubtagha of making it analogous to corrupting the make-up of Ramadan fasting, i.e., only one day is required. His statement: (And he thought...) It is mentioned in Sharh al-Lubab what supports this assumption. He said: In Sharh al-Niqaya of al-Shams al-Samarqandi at his statement 'he corrupted his hajj', i.e., he diminished it excessively and did not nullify it, as in al-Mudmarat. The author (i.e., the author of al-Lubab) said: So it indicates that the intended meaning of corruption is excessive diminishment, not nullification. This is a good qualification that removes some problems. I say: Among them is [the problem] in the acts, but in not nullifying there is also a type of problem, which is the qada, but it can be repelled by saying that it is performed in a complete manner. End. His statement: (He made it absolute so it includes...) And likewise it includes if he engages in intercourse intentionally or forgetfully, in both cases a badanah is required, as in the general [books].
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the rules of corrupted hajj. The matn states 'He continues and makes it up, and they are not different in it' meaning that even after corrupting hajj, the pilgrim must continue performing the remaining rites just as he would in a valid hajj, and then he is obligated to make it up the following year. This applies whether it was his obligatory hajj (hajjat al-Islam) or not, because he performed the acts in a corrupted state, whereas the obligation is to perform them correctly. The author then addresses a misconception: some thought that corruption of hajj does not corrupt ihram, but the correct view is that ihram is also corrupted and he must continue as a muhrim. Then he discusses a question: if the make-up hajj itself becomes corrupted, must he make it up again? By analogy, since the make-up is only a means to discharge the original obligation, if it is corrupted, he only needs to make up the original one, not an additional one. This is like if someone misses a day of Ramadan fasting and then makes it up, but corrupts the make-up; he only owes one make-up. The commentary then delves into the meaning of 'qada' vs 'i'ada', explaining that in Hanafi terminology, performing the hajj again within one's lifetime is considered 'ada' (performance) not qada, because it is still within the time of obligation (one's lifetime). Therefore, the repeated hajj is actually the obligatory hajj itself if performed correctly; the corrupted one is void. The author cites al-Kamal ibn al-Humam that calling it qada is metaphorical. Finally, he notes that the ruling applies whether intercourse was intentional or forgetful, requiring a badanah (camel) as penalty.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Linguistically, performance or completion; technically in this context, it is used metaphorically for repeating the hajj after corruption, but in Hanafi view it is actually 'ada.
إعادة (i'āda): Repeating an act due to a defect; here it is not applicable because the corruption does not create a new obligation.
بدنة (badana): A camel (or large animal) required as a penalty for certain ihram violations, e.g., intentional or forgetful intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person corrupts his obligatory hajj, what must he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Stop and not continue; only pay a penalty.
B) Continue the rites, then make it up the following year.
C) Only make it up without continuing.
D) Pay a fine and do nothing else.

Key Takeaway
A corrupted hajj must be completed, and the subsequent valid hajj fulfills the original obligation; it is 'ada, not qada.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Continuing and Making Up a Corrupted Hajj
Ruling statement with refutation of a mistaken view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on continuing a corrupted Hajj, explain the obligation of make-up, and refute the mistaken view that the ihram remains uncorrupted.

Core Idea
A corrupted Hajj must be completed and repeated next year; the make-up is the original obligation itself.

What happens if your Hajj becomes corrupted partway through? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling: you must continue the remaining rituals even in the corrupted state, then perform Hajj again the following year. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the obligation, the nature of corruption as severe deficiency (naqs fahish), and corrects a common misconception about the state of ihram. It also addresses an advanced question: what if the make-up Hajj itself is also corrupted?

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Basis
From the matn 'And he continues and makes up, and they do not separate', identify that both continuing in the corrupted Hajj and making it up next year are wajib. The basis is that the obligation must be performed with soundness (sahih), but the corrupted Hajj was performed with corruption (fasid).
2
Understand the Nature of Corruption (Fasad)
The passage defines fasad as 'severe deficiency' (naqs fahish), not total nullification (butlan). This means the pilgrim's actions are deficient but the state of ihram is still considered; the pilgrim must still avoid prohibitions.
This nuance resolves why the pilgrim must continue in the corrupted state.
3
Refute the Mistaken View
Some contemporaries thought that corruption of Hajj does not corrupt the ihram, so one could continue in the same ihram for the make-up. The passage firmly rejects this: the ihram is also corrupted.
The make-up Hajj requires a new ihram.
4
Apply the Ruling to a Corrupted Make-up
The text discusses a query: if the make-up Hajj is also corrupted, must one make it up again? The answer: no, only one make-up is required. This is because the make-up is actually the performance of the original obligation itself (ada'), not a separate qada' in the technical sense.
Analogous to praying Dhuhr in its time, corrupting it, then repeating it; no further make-up is needed.
5
Recognize the Linguistic Nuance of Qada'
The commentator clarifies that 'qada'' in this context means 'ada'' (performance) according to the Hanafi usage. Calling the subsequent Hajj 'qada'' is a metaphor; it is actually the original obligation.
This avoids the confusion of requiring multiple make-ups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بوصف الصحة. وفي فتاوى قاضي خان: ويجتنب في الفاسدة ما يجتنب في الجائزة، وقد ظن بعض أهل عصرنا أن الحج إذا فسد لا يفسد الإحرام ولهذا قالوا إن الإحرام باقٍ فيقضي فيه وليس كما ظن بل فسد [؟] رمضان أنه خرج بالقضاء الإحكام والإتقان فغير مناسب هنا، وإن أراد به الأداء كما يقال قضيت الدين أي أديته فقوله «والمراد الإعادة» يخالفه إلا أن يكون الواو بمعنى (أو) لكن فيه أن الإعادة فعل مثل الواجب في وقته لخلل غير بالقضاء الأداء كما يدل عليه قول الكمال في التحرير إن تسمية الحج الصحيح بعد الحج الفاسد قضاء مجاز. قال الحلبي في شرحه لأنه في وقته وهو العمر فهو أداء على قول مشايخنا ا هـ. وحيث كان أداء عندنا سقط قبله لا يلزمه قضاؤه أصلاً إذ لو صلى الظهر مثلاً في وقتها وأفسدها ثم أداها ثانياً خرج عن العهدة ولا يتوهم أحد لزوم صلاة أخرى قضاء عن التي شرع فيها وأفسدها، وكذا ما قدمناه عن المبتغى من جعله نظير ما لو أفسد قضاء صوم رمضان أي فإنه لا يلزمه إلا قضاء يوم واحد
قوله: (وقد ظن الخ) ذكر في شرح اللباب ما يقوي هذا الظن حيث قال: وفي شرح النقاية للشمس السمرقندي عند قوله «أفسد حجه» أي نقصه نقصاناً فاحشاً ولم يبطله كما في المضمرات. قال المصنف - يعني صاحب اللباب - فأفاد أن المراد من الفساد النقص الفاحش لا البطلان، وهو قيد حسن يزيل بعض الإشكالات قلت من جملتها في الأفعال لكن في عدم الإبطال أيضاً نوع من الإشكال وهو القضاء إلا أنه يمكن دفعه بأنه يؤدى على وجه الكمال ا هـ
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses. His saying: (And he continues and makes up, and they do not separate in it) meaning: It is obligatory to continue in the actions of Hajj after its corruption just as he continues in it while it is valid, and he is obliged to make it up the following year, whether it was the Hajj of Islam or not, because he performed the actions with the description of corruption while what is due upon him is to perform them with the description of soundness. And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: He avoids in the corrupted Hajj what he avoids in the valid one. And some of our contemporaries thought that if Hajj is corrupted, the ihram is not corrupted, and therefore they said the ihram remains, so he makes up in it, but it is not as they thought; rather it is corrupted... [unclear] Ramadhan: that he leaves it with this intention, the ignorant person is the issue of not leaving. But as for one who knows that he does not leave it with this intention, it is not considered from him. He said: Its commentator said: Likewise, it should not be considered from him if he is doubtful about the matter or forgetful of it. His saying: (And he is obliged to make it up the next year). He said in al-Nahr: Some students at al-Azhar Mosque asked me: If the make-up is also corrupted, must he make it up as well? I said: I have not seen the issue, and by analogy, since he entered into it as a means of discharging the obligation, not as a new obligation, the intended meaning of 'qada' is the linguistic meaning, and the intended meaning is 'i'ada' (repetition), as is apparent. In summary, he is only obliged to one Hajj for the one he corrupted first, and he is not obliged to a second Hajj for the one he corrupted second. His words regarding the ruling are apparent, and Sheikh Ismail transmitted it from al-Mubtagha, saying: The wording of al-Mubtagha: If he missed the Hajj, then he performed Hajj the following year intending to make up that Hajj, but he corrupted the Hajj, he is only obliged to make up one Hajj, just as if he had corrupted the make-up of fasting. As for his saying that the intended meaning of qada'... then there is obscurity. Because if he intended that the meaning of qada' is 'ihkam' and 'itqan' (perfection), it is not appropriate here. And if he intended 'ada' (performance) as one says 'qadaytu al-dayn' meaning I paid it, then his saying 'and the intended meaning is i'ada' contradicts it, unless the waw is in the sense of 'aw' (or). But in that, there is the issue that i'ada is doing something like the obligatory in its time due to a defect other than corruption and lack of soundness of initiation, and it is not applicable here. Yes, it is applicable according to the famous definition among the Shafi'is: that it is doing something a second time in the time of performance due to a defect in its first doing. So the correct thing is to delete his statement 'and the intended meaning is i'ada' and limit to clarifying that the intended meaning of qada' is ada', as indicated by the saying of al-Kamal in al-Tahrir: 'Calling the valid Hajj after the corrupted Hajj 'qada'' is a metaphor.' Al-Halabi said in his commentary: Because it is in its time, which is one's lifetime, so it is ada' according to our mashayikh. End quote. And since it is ada' in our school, the question falls entirely, because the first Hajj is void. If he performs it validly, he has discharged the obligation, otherwise not. So he must perform it a second, third, etc., until he performs it validly. What he does after the corrupted Hajj is not a Hajj other than the obligatory; rather it is the obligatory if valid, and what came before does not require him to make it up at all. For if he prayed Dhuhr, for example, in its time and corrupted it, then he performed it a second time, he has discharged the obligation, and no one would imagine he has to perform another prayer as a make-up for the one he began and corrupted. Similarly, what we presented from al-Mubtagha of making it analogous to if he corrupted the make-up of Ramadan fast, i.e., he is only obliged to make up one day. His saying: (And he thought, etc.) He mentioned in Sharh al-Lubab what strengthens this thought, where he said: In Sharh al-Niqaya of al-Shams al-Samarqandi, regarding his saying 'he corrupted his Hajj', meaning: he diminished it severely and did not nullify it, as in al-Mudmarat. The author, i.e., the author of al-Lubab, said: So he indicated that the meaning of fasad is severe deficiency, not nullification. This is a good restriction that removes some difficulties. I say: Among them are the actions, but in not nullifying there is also a kind of difficulty, which is the make-up, except that it can be repelled by saying that it is performed to perfection. End quote.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq in the chapter of Hajj, section on offenses. It begins by explaining the matn's phrase 'And he continues and makes up, and they do not separate in it.' The ruling is that once a Hajj is corrupted (whether it is the obligatory Hajj or a voluntary one), the pilgrim must continue the remaining actions of the Hajj in its corrupted state, just as he would have continued if it were valid. Then he must make up that Hajj the following year. The reason given is that he has performed the actions but with the attribute of corruption, whereas what was required of him was performance with the attribute of soundness. The commentator then quotes Qadi Khan's Fatawa stating that in a corrupted Hajj, he must avoid the same prohibitions as in a valid Hajj. Next, the passage addresses a mistaken view held by some contemporaries: that corruption of Hajj does not corrupt the ihram, so the ihram remains intact and he can continue in it for the make-up. The commentator firmly refutes this, stating that the ihram is indeed corrupted. Then the discussion moves to a subtle point: if the make-up Hajj itself is also corrupted, does it require yet another make-up? The commentator relates a query from a student at al-Azhar. The answer, based on al-Nahr and al-Mubtagha, is that only one make-up is required, not two. The reasoning is that the make-up is actually an 'ada' (performance) of the same obligation, not a separate 'qada' in the technical sense. Since the first Hajj was void, what he performs subsequently is the original obligatory Hajj itself, so if he corrupts that, he must repeat it, but a second make-up is not required. The analogy is made to a prayer corrupted during its time: if he repeats it, that suffices; no one would demand a make-up for the corrupted prayer. The commentator also clarifies the linguistic meaning of 'qada'' as 'ada' (performance) according to Hanafi terminology, supported by al-Kamal and al-Halabi. Finally, the passage cites Sharh al-Lubab, which quotes al-Samarqandi's definition of 'ifsad' as severe deficiency rather than nullification (batlan), a nuance that resolves some issues. This defines the nature of corruption in Hajj: it is severe deficiency, not total nullification, yet it still requires a make-up. The commentator notes the remaining difficulty of the make-up but resolves it by saying the make-up is performed to perfection.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): Corruption of Hajj: a severe deficiency (naqs fahish) that requires make-up but does not nullify the ihram completely; it is not total nullification (butlan).
قضاء (qada'): In this context, qada' means 'ada' (performance) of the original obligation at a later time, not a separate compensatory act; it is a linguistic usage.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah; the passage argues it is corrupted (fasid) when the Hajj is corrupted, contrary to the mistaken view that it remains intact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a pilgrim corrupts his make-up Hajj (the one performed the year after a first corruption), how many additional make-up Hajjs are required?
A) Two: one for each corruption.
B) One: only for the first corruption; the second corruption does not trigger a separate make-up.
C) None: the second corruption absolves him of any further obligation.
D) He must slaughter a badanah for each corruption.

Key Takeaway
A corrupted Hajj obligates the pilgrim to complete the rituals and repeat Hajj the following year; if the make-up is also corrupted, it is treated as the same obligation, requiring repetition but not an additional make-up.

Core Ruling: Badanah Before Shaving, Shah After
Penalty details for jima' after standing at Arafat, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required penalty for jima' after standing at Arafat and explain why the Hajj remains valid.

Core Idea
After Arafat, jima' does not invalidate Hajj; penalty: badanah before shaving, shah after.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for a major Haij offense—sexual intercourse after the key pillar of standing at Arafat. The text clarifies that the Hajj is not invalidated, but a wajib sacrificial penalty applies, and the amount depends on whether shaving has occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is jima' after standing at Arafat. The ruling is that a penalty (badanah or shah) is wajib, but the Hajj is not invalidated (la fasad).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat has perfected his Hajj' is cited, and the athar from Ibn Abbas establishing the penalty.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'tamma hajjuhu' indicates that the Hajj is secure from corruption because the second pillar (tawaf) remains. The penalty is derived from the athar.
4
Note the distinction based on shaving
Before shaving: badanah. After shaving (before tawaf): shah. This is the position of the matn and most early Hanafis.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later mashayikh (al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i) hold that a badanah is absolutely required regardless of timing.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference, explored in the next lesson.

صرحوا بفساده في مواضع عديدة في هذا الفصل. ومعنى بقائه عدم الخروج عنه بغير الأفعال ومعنى الافتراق الذي ليس بواجب أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما في طريق غير طريق صاحبه، وإنما لم يجب لأن الجامع بينهما وهو النكاح قائم فلا معنى للافتراق قبل الإحرام لإباحة الوقوع، ولا بعده لأنهما يتذاكران ما لحقهما من المشقة الشديدة لذة صغيرة فيزدادان ندماً وتحرزا لكنه مستحب إذا خاف الوقاع كما في المحيط وغيره. قوله: (وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد) أي يجب بدنة لو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق ولا يفسد حجه للحديث "من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه" أي أمن من فساده لبقاء الركن الثاني وهو الطواف. ووجوب البدنة مروي عن ابن عباس والأثر فيه كالخبر. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا جامع مرة أو مراراً إن اتحد المجلس، وأما إذا اختلف فبدنة للأوّل وشاة للثاني في قولهما. وقال محمد: إن ذبح للأوّل فيجب للثاني شاة وإلا فلا ذكره الأسبيجابي، وعلل له المبسوط بأنه دخل إحرامه نقصان بالجماع الأوّل وبالجماع الثاني صادف إحراماً ناقصاً فيكفيه شاة. في قوله: (أو جامع بعد الحلق) معطوف على قوله أول الفصل «قبل» أي يجب شاة إن جامع بعد الحلق قبل الطواف لقصور الجناية لوجود الحل الأوّل بالحلق. ثم اعلم أن أصحاب المتون على ما ذكره المصنف من التفصيل فيما إذا جامع بعد الوقوف، فإن كان قبل الحلق فالواجب بدنة، وإن كان بعده فالواجب شاة. ومشى جماعة من المشايخ كصاحب المبسوط والبدائع والأسبيجابي على وجوب البدنة مطلقاً. وقال في فتح القدير: إنه الأوجه لأن إيجابها ليس إلا بقول ابن عباس والمروي عنه ظاهره فيما بعد الحلق. ثم المعنى يساعده وذلك لأن وجوبها قبل الحلق ليس إلا للجناية على الإحرام، ومعلوم أن الوطء ليس جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لاعتبار تحريمه لغيره فليس الطيب جناية على الإحرام باعتبار تحريمه الجماع أو الحلق بل باعتبار تحريمه للطيب وكذا كل جناية على الإحرام ليست جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لها لا لغيرها فيجب أن يستوي ما قبل الحلق وما بعده في حق الوطء لأن الذي به كان جناية قبله بعينه ثابت بعده والزائل لم يكن الوطء جناية باعتباره لا أن المذكور في ظاهر الرواية إطلاق لزوم البدنة بعد الوقوف من غير تفصيل بين كونه قبل الحلق أو بعده [؟] عامداً أو ناسياً. وذكر الحدادي في شرح القدوري ناقلاً عن الوجيز أنه إنما تجب البدنة إذا جامع عامداً، أما إذا جامع ناسياً فعليه شاة ا هـ. وهو خلاف ما في المشاهر من الروايات حيث لا فرق بين العامد والناسي في سائر الجنايات، وقد صرح به قاضيخان بقوله: ولو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة فلا يفسد حجه وعليه جزور جامع عامداً أو ناسياً ا هـ. كذا في شرح اللباب وسيذكر المصنف أن جماع الناسي كالعامد قوله: (وإن كان بعده) أي بعد الحلق وقبل طواف الزيارة [؟] كما هو ظاهر وصرح به في شرحه
His saying: (He made it absolute, so it includes, etc.) Likewise, it includes if he had intercourse deliberately or forgetfully, then a badanah is obligatory in both cases as in most books. And a badanah is due if after it and no corruption, or if he had intercourse after shaving or in Umrah before performing tawaf for it, the majority [say] due to ihram like Hajj, and they have stated its corruption in many places in this chapter. The meaning of its remaining is not leaving it except by actions, and the meaning of separation that is not obligatory is that each takes a path different from his companion's. It is not obligatory because the bond between them, namely marriage, remains, so there is no meaning to separation before ihram to permit occurrence, nor after because they recall what befell them of severe hardship [for] a small pleasure, so they increase in regret and caution. But it is recommended if he fears intercourse as in al-Muhit and others. His saying: (And a badanah if after it and no corruption) meaning: A badanah is obligatory if he had intercourse after standing at Arafat before shaving, and his Hajj is not corrupted because of the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat has perfected his Hajj', i.e., it is safe from corruption due to the remaining of the second pillar, which is tawaf. The obligation of a badanah is narrated from Ibn Abbas, and the athar is like a hadith. He made it absolute, so it includes if he had intercourse once or repeatedly if the same session. But if different sessions, then a badanah for the first and a shah for the second according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: If he sacrificed for the first, then a shah is due for the second; otherwise not. Mentioned by al-Asbijabi. Al-Mabsut gave the reason: his ihram entered a deficiency by the first intercourse, and by the second intercourse it encountered a deficient ihram, so a shah is sufficient. Regarding his saying: (Or if he had intercourse after shaving) is coordinated with his saying at the beginning of the chapter 'before', meaning a shah is obligatory if he had intercourse after shaving before tawaf due to the deficiency of the offense because of the first release by shaving. Then know that the authors of the texts, according to what the author mentioned, have the detail: if he had intercourse after standing, if before shaving the obligation is a badanah, and if after shaving the obligation is a shah. And a group of mashayikh like the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i, and al-Asbijabi adopted the obligation of a badanah absolutely. And it is said in Fath al-Qadir: It is the more appropriate because its obligation is only by the saying of Ibn Abbas, and what is narrated from him apparently is regarding after shaving. Then the meaning supports it: because its obligation before shaving is only due to the offense against ihram, and it is known that intercourse is an offense against it only by virtue of its prohibition, not by virtue of its prohibition of something else. Hence perfume is not an offense against ihram by virtue of its prohibition of intercourse or shaving, but by virtue of its prohibition of perfume. Similarly, every offense against ihram is not an offense against it except by virtue of its prohibition of that thing, not for other things. So it must be the same before shaving and after regarding intercourse, because that which made it an offense before is exactly the same after, and what was removed was not that intercourse was an offense by virtue of it. But what is mentioned in the apparent riwaya is the absolute obligation of a badanah after standing without distinction between before shaving or after [?] deliberately or forgetfully. And al-Hadadi mentioned in Sharh al-Quduri transmitting from al-Wajiz that a badanah is only obligatory if he had intercourse deliberately; if he had intercourse forgetfully, then a shah is due. End quote. This is contrary to what is in the well-known narrations where there is no distinction between deliberate and forgetful in all offenses, and Qadikhan explicitly stated: 'If he had intercourse after standing at Arafat, his Hajj is not corrupted, and a jazur is due, whether he had intercourse deliberately or forgetfully.' End quote. Similarly in Sharh al-Lubab, and the author will mention that intercourse of the forgetful is like the deliberate. His saying: (And if after it) meaning after shaving and before tawaf al-ziyara [?] as is apparent and stated in his commentary.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, focusing on penalties for sexual intercourse (jima') during Hajj after standing at Arafat. The commentator first explains the generality of the matn: the ruling applies whether the person acted deliberately or forgetfully, as found in most books. Then he introduces the key ruling: if a person has intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving (halq), a badanah (a camel) is required, and the Hajj is not invalidated. This is based on the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat has perfected his Hajj', meaning the Hajj is safe from corruption because the second pillar (tawaf al-ziyara) remains. The obligation of a badanah is also traced to the Companion Ibn Abbas. The commentator notes that the matn is absolute regarding the number of times: if intercourse occurs once or multiple times in the same session, only one badanah is due. If in separate sessions, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a badanah is due for the first and a shah (sheep) for the second. Imam Muhammad has an additional condition: if he already sacrificed for the first, a shah is due for the second; otherwise not. Al-Mabsut explains that the first intercourse introduces a deficiency into the ihram, so the second intercourse encounters an already deficient ihram, making a shah sufficient. The passage then addresses the case of intercourse after shaving (but before tawaf al-ziyara). Here, due to the first release (al-hall al-awwal) achieved by shaving, the offense is considered lesser, and only a shah is required. The commentator notes that the authors of the main texts (asbab al-mutun) adhere to this distinction: before shaving – badanah; after shaving – shah. However, a group of later mashayikh (such as the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i, and al-Asbijabi) held that a badanah is absolutely required in both cases. Fath al-Qadir supports this, arguing that the narration from Ibn Abbas apparently refers to after shaving, and the reasoning (ma'na) supports it: the prohibition of intercourse is based on the prohibition itself, not on the timing of shaving. The passage then discusses the difference regarding intent. Al-Hadadi, in his commentary on al-Quduri, transmits from al-Wajiz that a badanah is only due for deliberate intercourse; for forgetful, a shah is due. But this contradicts the well-known narrations in the school, as Qadikhan explicitly says there is no difference between deliberate and forgetful. The commentator confirms that the author will later state that intercourse of the forgetful is like the deliberate. The passage ends with a brief note on the ruling after shaving before tawaf al-ziyara, as is apparent.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A large sacrificial animal (camel/cow) required as penalty for jima' before shaving after Arafat.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat, required as a lesser penalty for jima' after shaving.
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse, a hajj violation incurring penalty.
فساد (fasad): Corruption; here, the Hajj is not corrupted after standing at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required sacrifice for jima' after standing at Arafat but before shaving?
A) A shah (sheep)
B) A badanah (camel)
C) No sacrifice
D) The Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
Jima' after Arafat before shaving requires a badanah, but the Hajj remains valid.
