Intra-Hanafi Disputes: Absolute Badanah vs Distinction, and Intent
Intra-Hanafi disagreements on penalty amount and intent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the main Hanafi position from that of later mashayikh regarding penalty amount, and evaluate the dispute on intent.

Core Idea
Later mashayikh require badanah absolutely; also, forgetfulness may reduce penalty to shah according to a minority view.

Within the Hanafi school, there are important differences regarding the penalty for jima' after Arafat. While the matn distinguishes between before and after shaving, a group of later scholars holds that a badanah is required in all cases. Additionally, the role of intent (deliberate vs forgetful) is contested. This lesson explores these disputes and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the main Hanafi position
The matn and early scholars: badana for jima' before shaving, shah after shaving.
2
Identify the opposing view
Later mashayikh (al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i, al-Asbijabi) require a badanah absolutely, regardless of timing.
They argue based on the generality of Ibn Abbas's athar and the illa of the act itself.
3
Analyze the proofs
The matn uses qiyas: shaving reduces severity. The mashayikh use the literal meaning of the athar.
Fath al-Qadir supports the absolute view as 'more appropriate'.
4
Examine the dispute on intent
Al-Hadadi reports a view that a badanah is only for deliberate; for forgetful, a shah. But the majority (Qadikhan) say no difference.
The author of the text sides with the majority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If jima' occurs after shaving, the matn requires shah; the mashayikh require badanah (more expensive). Also, if forgetful, minority requires shah instead of badanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (أطلقه فشمل الخ) وكذا شمل ما لو جامع عامداً أو ناسياً فتلزمه فيهما بدنة كما في عامة الكتب. وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد أو جامع بعد الحلق أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر بسبب الإحرام كالحج وقد صرحوا بفساده في مواضع عديدة في هذا الفصل. ومعنى بقائه عدم الخروج عنه بغير الأفعال ومعنى الافتراق الذي ليس بواجب أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما في طريق غير طريق صاحبه، وإنما لم يجب لأن الجامع بينهما وهو النكاح قائم فلا معنى للافتراق قبل الإحرام لإباحة الوقوع، ولا بعده لأنهما يتذاكران ما لحقهما من المشقة الشديدة لذة صغيرة فيزدادان ندماً وتحرزا لكنه مستحب إذا خاف الوقاع كما في المحيط وغيره. قوله: (وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد) أي يجب بدنة لو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق ولا يفسد حجه للحديث "من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه" أي أمن من فساده لبقاء الركن الثاني وهو الطواف. ووجوب البدنة مروي عن ابن عباس والأثر فيه كالخبر. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا جامع مرة أو مراراً إن اتحد المجلس، وأما إذا اختلف فبدنة للأوّل وشاة للثاني في قولهما. وقال محمد: إن ذبح للأوّل فيجب للثاني شاة وإلا فلا ذكره الأسبيجابي، وعلل له المبسوط بأنه دخل إحرامه نقصان بالجماع الأوّل وبالجماع الثاني صادف إحراماً ناقصاً فيكفيه شاة. في قوله: (أو جامع بعد الحلق) معطوف على قوله أول الفصل «قبل» أي يجب شاة إن جامع بعد الحلق قبل الطواف لقصور الجناية لوجود الحل الأوّل بالحلق. ثم اعلم أن أصحاب المتون على ما ذكره المصنف من التفصيل فيما إذا جامع بعد الوقوف، فإن كان قبل الحلق فالواجب بدنة، وإن كان بعده فالواجب شاة. ومشى جماعة من المشايخ كصاحب المبسوط والبدائع والأسبيجابي على وجوب البدنة مطلقاً. وقال في فتح القدير: إنه الأوجه لأن إيجابها ليس إلا بقول ابن عباس والمروي عنه ظاهره فيما بعد الحلق. ثم المعنى يساعده وذلك لأن وجوبها قبل الحلق ليس إلا للجناية على الإحرام، ومعلوم أن الوطء ليس جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لاعتبار تحريمه لغيره فليس الطيب جناية على الإحرام باعتبار تحريمه الجماع أو الحلق بل باعتبار تحريمه للطيب وكذا كل جناية على الإحرام ليست جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لها لا لغيرها فيجب أن يستوي ما قبل الحلق وما بعده في حق الوطء لأن الذي به كان جناية قبله بعينه ثابت بعده والزائل لم يكن الوطء جناية باعتباره لا أن المذكور في ظاهر الرواية إطلاق لزوم البدنة بعد الوقوف من غير تفصيل بين كونه قبل الحلق أو بعده [؟] عامداً أو ناسياً. وذكر الحدادي في شرح القدوري ناقلاً عن الوجيز أنه إنما تجب البدنة إذا جامع عامداً، أما إذا جامع ناسياً فعليه شاة ا هـ. وهو خلاف ما في المشاهر من الروايات حيث لا فرق بين العامد والناسي في سائر الجنايات، وقد صرح به قاضيخان بقوله: ولو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة فلا يفسد حجه وعليه جزور جامع عامداً أو ناسياً ا هـ. كذا في شرح اللباب وسيذكر المصنف أن جماع الناسي كالعامد قوله: (وإن كان بعده) أي بعد الحلق وقبل طواف الزيارة [؟] كما هو ظاهر وصرح به في شرحه
His saying: (He made it absolute, so it includes, etc.) Likewise, it includes if he had intercourse deliberately or forgetfully, then a badanah is obligatory in both cases as in most books. And a badanah is due if after it and no corruption, or if he had intercourse after shaving or in Umrah before performing tawaf for it, the majority [say] due to ihram like Hajj, and they have stated its corruption in many places in this chapter. The meaning of its remaining is not leaving it except by actions, and the meaning of separation that is not obligatory is that each takes a path different from his companion's. It is not obligatory because the bond between them, namely marriage, remains, so there is no meaning to separation before ihram to permit occurrence, nor after because they recall what befell them of severe hardship [for] a small pleasure, so they increase in regret and caution. But it is recommended if he fears intercourse as in al-Muhit and others. His saying: (And a badanah if after it and no corruption) meaning: A badanah is obligatory if he had intercourse after standing at Arafat before shaving, and his Hajj is not corrupted because of the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat has perfected his Hajj', i.e., it is safe from corruption due to the remaining of the second pillar, which is tawaf. The obligation of a badanah is narrated from Ibn Abbas, and the athar is like a hadith. He made it absolute, so it includes if he had intercourse once or repeatedly if the same session. But if different sessions, then a badanah for the first and a shah for the second according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: If he sacrificed for the first, then a shah is due for the second; otherwise not. Mentioned by al-Asbijabi. Al-Mabsut gave the reason: his ihram entered a deficiency by the first intercourse, and by the second intercourse it encountered a deficient ihram, so a shah is sufficient. Regarding his saying: (Or if he had intercourse after shaving) is coordinated with his saying at the beginning of the chapter 'before', meaning a shah is obligatory if he had intercourse after shaving before tawaf due to the deficiency of the offense because of the first release by shaving. Then know that the authors of the texts, according to what the author mentioned, have the detail: if he had intercourse after standing, if before shaving the obligation is a badanah, and if after shaving the obligation is a shah. And a group of mashayikh like the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i, and al-Asbijabi adopted the obligation of a badanah absolutely. And it is said in Fath al-Qadir: It is the more appropriate because its obligation is only by the saying of Ibn Abbas, and what is narrated from him apparently is regarding after shaving. Then the meaning supports it: because its obligation before shaving is only due to the offense against ihram, and it is known that intercourse is an offense against it only by virtue of its prohibition, not by virtue of its prohibition of something else. Hence perfume is not an offense against ihram by virtue of its prohibition of intercourse or shaving, but by virtue of its prohibition of perfume. Similarly, every offense against ihram is not an offense against it except by virtue of its prohibition of that thing, not for other things. So it must be the same before shaving and after regarding intercourse, because that which made it an offense before is exactly the same after, and what was removed was not that intercourse was an offense by virtue of it. But what is mentioned in the apparent riwaya is the absolute obligation of a badanah after standing without distinction between before shaving or after [?] deliberately or forgetfully. And al-Hadadi mentioned in Sharh al-Quduri transmitting from al-Wajiz that a badanah is only obligatory if he had intercourse deliberately; if he had intercourse forgetfully, then a shah is due. End quote. This is contrary to what is in the well-known narrations where there is no distinction between deliberate and forgetful in all offenses, and Qadikhan explicitly stated: 'If he had intercourse after standing at Arafat, his Hajj is not corrupted, and a jazur is due, whether he had intercourse deliberately or forgetfully.' End quote. Similarly in Sharh al-Lubab, and the author will mention that intercourse of the forgetful is like the deliberate. His saying: (And if after it) meaning after shaving and before tawaf al-ziyara [?] as is apparent and stated in his commentary.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, focusing on penalties for sexual intercourse (jima') during Hajj after standing at Arafat. The commentator first explains the generality of the matn: the ruling applies whether the person acted deliberately or forgetfully, as found in most books. Then he introduces the key ruling: if a person has intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving (halq), a badanah (a camel) is required, and the Hajj is not invalidated. This is based on the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat has perfected his Hajj', meaning the Hajj is safe from corruption because the second pillar (tawaf al-ziyara) remains. The obligation of a badanah is also traced to the Companion Ibn Abbas. The commentator notes that the matn is absolute regarding the number of times: if intercourse occurs once or multiple times in the same session, only one badanah is due. If in separate sessions, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a badanah is due for the first and a shah (sheep) for the second. Imam Muhammad has an additional condition: if he already sacrificed for the first, a shah is due for the second; otherwise not. Al-Mabsut explains that the first intercourse introduces a deficiency into the ihram, so the second intercourse encounters an already deficient ihram, making a shah sufficient. The passage then addresses the case of intercourse after shaving (but before tawaf al-ziyara). Here, due to the first release (al-hall al-awwal) achieved by shaving, the offense is considered lesser, and only a shah is required. The commentator notes that the authors of the main texts (asbab al-mutun) adhere to this distinction: before shaving – badanah; after shaving – shah. However, a group of later mashayikh (such as the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i, and al-Asbijabi) held that a badanah is absolutely required in both cases. Fath al-Qadir supports this, arguing that the narration from Ibn Abbas apparently refers to after shaving, and the reasoning (ma'na) supports it: the prohibition of intercourse is based on the prohibition itself, not on the timing of shaving. The passage then discusses the difference regarding intent. Al-Hadadi, in his commentary on al-Quduri, transmits from al-Wajiz that a badanah is only due for deliberate intercourse; for forgetful, a shah is due. But this contradicts the well-known narrations in the school, as Qadikhan explicitly says there is no difference between deliberate and forgetful. The commentator confirms that the author will later state that intercourse of the forgetful is like the deliberate. The passage ends with a brief note on the ruling after shaving before tawaf al-ziyara, as is apparent.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): Large sacrificial animal for penalty.
شاة (shah): Small sacrificial animal (sheep/goat).
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known narrations (Zahir al-Riwaya), is there a difference in penalty between deliberate and forgetful jima' after Arafat?
A) Yes, deliberate requires badanah, forgetful requires shah
B) No, both require the same penalty
C) No penalty for forgetful
D) It depends on the number of times

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi disputes exist on penalty amount and intent; the mufta bihi remains the distinction based on shaving and no differentiation for intent.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

6 min
Ruling on Intercourse After Wuquf and After Halq
Explains the matn ruling on intercourse after Arafah and after shaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation (badanah or sheep) required for intercourse at different stages of Hajj and explain why the Hajj is not invalidated based on the hadith and Hanafi reasoning.

Core Idea
Intercourse after wuquf does not nullify Hajj but requires a badanah; after halq, requires a sheep.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elaborates on the matn's ruling regarding intercourse during Hajj. It distinguishes between two scenarios: after standing at Arafah but before shaving, and after shaving but before tawaf. The key point is that in the first scenario, the Hajj remains valid, but a substantial expiation (badanah) is obligatory; in the second, a lesser expiation (sheep) suffices. The commentary also addresses multiple occurrences and intra-Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the two timeframes mentioned: after wuquf before halq, and after halq before tawaf. The expiation differs based on the level of prohibition remaining.
The first scenario involves a greater violation (ihram still fully in effect), the second a lesser one (first release by shaving).
2
State the required expiation for each
For intercourse after wuquf before halq: a badanah (camel/cow). For after halq before tawaf: a sheep (shāh).
Badaneh is an adult camel or cow; shāh is a sheep or goat.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah has completed his Hajj' shows that the Hajj is not invalidated because the main pillar (standing at Arafah) has been performed. The expiation is based on an athar from Ibn Abbas.
The hadith is cited as proof for non-invalidation, not for the expiation amount.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on multiple occurrences
If intercourse occurs multiple times in separate sittings, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a badanah for the first and a sheep for the second. Muhammad has an alternative view: if the badanah is slaughtered for the first, a sheep is due for the second; otherwise no additional expiation.
The reasoning: first intercourse weakens the ihram, so the second encounters a deficient ihram.
5
Determine the practical outcome
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn (badaneh for first, sheep for second). This affects a pilgrim who commits multiple acts of intercourse without having slaughtered the expiation for the first.
If one does not slaughter the badanah for the first, Muhammad's view would not require anything extra for the second, while the Sahibayn still would.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيه وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد أو جامع بعد الحلق أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر بسبب الإحرام كالحج وقد صرحوا بفساده في مواضع عديدة في هذا الفصل. ومعنى بقائه عدم الخروج عنه بغير الأفعال ومعنى الافتراق الذي ليس بواجب أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما في طريق غير طريق صاحبه، وإنما لم يجب لأن الجامع بينهما وهو النكاح قائم فلا معنى للافتراق قبل الإحرام لإباحة الوقوع ، ولا بعده لأنهما يتذاكران ما لحقهما من المشقة الشديدة لذة صغيرة فيزدادان ندماً وتحرزا لكنة مستحب إذا خاف الوقاع كما في المحيط وغيره قوله : ( وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد أي يجب بدنة لو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق ولا يفسد حجه للحديث من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه أي أمن من فساده لبقاء الركن الثاني وهو الطواف . ووجوب البدنة مروي عن ابن عباس والأثر فيه كالخبر . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا جامع مرة أو مراراً إن اتحد المجلس، وأما إذا اختلف فبدنة للأوّل وشاة للثاني في قولهما. وقال محمد: إن ذبح للأوّل فيجب للثاني شاة وإلا فلا ذكره الأسبيجابي، وعلل له المبسوط بأنه دخل إحرامه نقصان بالجماع الأوّل وبالجماع الثاني صادف إحراماً ناقصاً فيكفيه شاة . في قوله : ( أو جامع بعد الحلق) معطوف على قوله أول الفصل «قبل» أي يجب شاة إن جامع بعد الحلق قبل الطواف لقصور الجناية لوجود الحل الأوّل بالحلق.
In it: a badanah if after it and no corruption, or if he has intercourse after shaving or in Umrah before he performs most of its tawaf. Due to the ihram like Hajj, and they declared it corrupt in many places in this chapter. The meaning of its remaining is not leaving it except by actions, and the meaning of separation which is not obligatory is that each of them takes a path other than the path of his companion. It is not obligatory because the bond between them, which is marriage, remains, so there is no meaning for separation before ihram to permit occurrence, nor after it because they will remember the severe hardship they faced [and] small pleasure, so they increase in regret and caution, but it is recommended if they fear intercourse as in al-Muhit and others. His statement: (and a badanah if after it and no corruption) means a badanah is obligatory if he has intercourse after standing at Arafah before shaving, and his Hajj is not corrupted because of the hadith: 'Whoever stands at Arafah has completed his Hajj,' meaning he is safe from its corruption due to the remaining of the second pillar which is tawaf. The obligation of the badanah is narrated from Ibn Abbas, and the effect is like the report. He gave it absolutely, so it includes if he has intercourse once or multiple times if in one sitting. But if separated, then a badanah for the first and a sheep for the second according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: If he slaughtered for the first, then a sheep is obligatory for the second, otherwise no, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. Al-Mabsut explained for him: Because his ihram entered a deficiency by the first intercourse, and the second intercourse encountered a deficient ihram, so a sheep suffices him. In his statement: (or if he has intercourse after shaving) is conjoined to his statement at the beginning of the chapter 'before', meaning a sheep is obligatory if he has intercourse after shaving before tawaf due to the deficiency of the offense because of the existence of the first release (halal) by shaving.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling regarding intercourse during Hajj. The author explains the matn's phrase 'فيه وبدنة لو بعده ولا فساد' meaning that if a person has intercourse after standing at Arafah but before shaving his head (halq), he must offer a badanah (a camel or cow) but his Hajj is not invalidated. The basis is the hadith 'من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه' which indicates that the Hajj is preserved from corruption by the remaining pillar of tawaf. The obligation of badanah is traced to Ibn Abbas as an athar. The author then details that if one has intercourse multiple times in the same sitting, one badanah suffices. If in separate sittings, then according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), a badanah is due for the first and a sheep for the second. Muhammad has an alternative view: if he slaughtered the badanah for the first, a sheep is due for the second; otherwise not. Al-Mabsut's reasoning is that the first intercourse weakens the ihram, so the second finds a deficient ihram, thus only a sheep is needed. The passage then covers the second part of the matn: 'أو جامع بعد الحلق', explaining that if intercourse occurs after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah, only a sheep is obligatory because the first release (from the prohibition of not wearing sewn clothes, etc.) has occurred with shaving, making the offense lighter.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as expiation for violating ihram.
شاة (shāh): A sheep or goat offered as expiation for a lesser violation.
جماع (jimā‘): Sexual intercourse between a man and woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence of having intercourse after standing at Arafah but before shaving the head?
A) Hajj is invalidated and a badanah is required
B) Hajj is not invalidated and a badanah is required
C) Hajj is invalidated and a sheep is required
D) Hajj is not invalidated and a sheep is required

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after wuquf before halq requires a badanah but does not invalidate Hajj; after halq before tawaf, only a sheep is needed.

Dispute Over Badanah After Wuquf: Detailed vs Absolute View
Intra-Hanafi dispute with talil and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether badanah is required for intercourse after wuquf, identify the evidence for each, and explain why the detailed view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Badanah is required only if the violation coincides with a complete ihram; after halq, ihram is deficient, so only a sheep is due.

The authors of the matns (e.g., al-Quduri, al-Kanz) distinguish between intercourse before and after shaving: before requires a badanah, after requires a sheep. However, several later Hanafi authorities, such as the author of al-Mabsut, hold that badanah is required absolutely after wuquf. In this passage, the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq weighs the arguments and upholds the matn view, providing a detailed talil based on the completeness of ihram. We will walk through the dispute and the reasoning that leads to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the matn position
Identify the ruling given in the base texts: if intercourse occurs after wuquf but before halq, a badanah is wajib; if after halq (but before tawaf al-ziyarah), only a sheep is wajib. This is the starting point of the dispute.
This is the position of the author of al-Hidayah and similar matn works.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that a group of later shuyukh (al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', al-Asbijabi) hold that a badanah is wajib absolutely, whether before or after halq. They argue from the general statement of Ibn Abbas and a rational analysis that the prohibition of intercourse remains until tawaf.
This view is found in Fath al-Qadeer as 'al-awjah' according to some.
3
Analyze the evidence for the absolute view
The absolute view relies on: (a) the literal appearance of Ibn Abbas's statement, and (b) the argument that the prohibition of intercourse is the same before and after halq. According to this reasoning, if the act is prohibited, the penalty should be uniform.
The text says: 'لأن إيجابها ليس إلا بقول ابن عباس والمروي عنه ظاهره فيما بعد الحلق'
4
Present the Hanafi response and counter-evidence
The text refutes the absolute view by pointing to the consensus (ittifaq) that a second intercourse before halq requires only a sheep. This shows that the severity of the penalty depends on the completeness of ihram. After halq, ihram is deficient (since the muhrim has exited from one restriction), so the penalty is lighter. The same logic applies to other violations like perfume or sewn garments, where the completeness of ihram affects the amount of dam.
This is the key talil: 'فإنه لا يجب بدنة وإنما تجب شاة مع أن وجوبها للجماع الأول ليس إلا باعتبار حرمته عليه...فالجماع في المرة الثانية صادف إحراماً ناقصاً'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Having weighed the arguments, the commentator declares the matn view 'al-awjah' (most appropriate) and thus the relied-upon position. The absolute view is considered marjuh.
Secondary: the dispute about forgetfulness is also resolved in favor of equality—intentional and forgetful are the same, per Qadikhan and the well-known narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن أصحاب المتون على ما ذكره المصنف من التفصيل فيما إذا جامع بعد الوقوف، فإن كان قبل الحلق فالواجب بدنة، وإن كان بعده فالواجب شاة. ومشى جماعة من المشايخ كصاحب المبسوط والبدائع والأسبيجابي على وجوب البدنة مطلقاً. وقال في فتح القدير: إنه الأوجه لأن إيجابها ليس إلا بقول ابن عباس والمروي عنه ظاهره فيما بعد الحلق. ثم المعنى يساعده وذلك لأن وجوبها قبل الحلق ليس إلا للجناية على الإحرام، ومعلوم أن الوطء ليس جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لاعتبار تحريمه لغيره فليس الطيب جناية على الإحرام باعتبار تحريمه الجماع أو الحلق بل باعتبار تحريمه للطيب وكذا كل جناية على الإحرام ليست جناية عليه إلا باعتبار تحريمه لها لا لغيرها فيجب أن يستوي ما قبل الحلق وما بعده في حق الوطء لأن الذي به كان جناية قبله بعينه ثابت بعده والزائل لم يكن الوطء جناية باعتباره لا أن المذكور في ظاهر الرواية إطلاق لزوم البدنة بعد الوقوف من غير تفصيل بين كونه قبل الحلق أو بعده جرم العامد الكتب. وذكر الحدادي في شرح القدوري ناقلاً عن الوجيز أنه إنما تجب البدنة إذا جامع عامداً، أما إذا جامع ناسياً فعليه شاة ا هـ. وهو خلاف ما في المشاهر من الروايات حيث لا فرق بين والناسي في سائر الجنايات، وقد صرح به قاضيخان بقوله : ولو جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة فلا يفسد حجه وعليه جزور جامع عامداً أو ناسياً ! هـ. كذا في شرح اللباب وسيذكر المصنف أن جماع الناسي كالعامد قوله : ( وإن كان بعده أي بعد الحلق وقبل طواف الزيارة كـ ظاهر وصرح به في ... ثم يرد عليه أنهم اتفقوا أنه لو جامع مرة ثانية بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق فإنه لا يجب بدنة وإنما تجب شاة مع أن وجوبها للجماع الأول ليس إلا باعتبار حرمته عليه وهو بعينه موجود في كل جماع أتى به قبل الطواف فتعين أن ينظر إلى أن البدنة لا تجب إلا إذا كملت الجناية وكمالها بمصادفتها إحراماً كاملاً. فالجماع في المرة الثانية صادف إحراماً ناقصاً فلم تجب البدنة، وكذا الجماع بعد الحلق صادف إحراماً ناقصاً لخروجه عنه في حق غير النساء. وهذا الباب - أعني باب الجنايات على الإحرام - ينظر فيه إلى كمال الجناية وقصورها ليجب الجزاء تقدم من تطييب العضو وما دونه ومن لبس المخيط يوماً أو أقل إلى غير ذلك لا إلى تحريم الفعل فقط . فالحاصل أن مسائلهم شاهدة بأن الجناية إن كملت تغلظ الجزاء كما في لبس المخيط يوماً أو أقل إلى غير ذلك لا إلى تحريم الفعل فقط وإن قصرت خف الجزاء، فالأوجه ما في المتون والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Then know that the authors of the matns follow the detail mentioned by the author regarding intercourse after standing: if it is before shaving, the obligatory is a badanah; if after, the obligatory is a sheep. And a group of shaykhs, such as the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', and al-Asbijabi, adopted the obligation of a badanah absolutely. And in Fath al-Qadeer it is said: It is more appropriate because its obligation is only from the statement of Ibn Abbas, and what is narrated from him apparently concerns after shaving. Then the meaning supports it: because its obligation before shaving is only for the violation against ihram, and it is known that sexual intercourse is not a violation against it except by virtue of its prohibition for other than itself; so perfume is not a violation against ihram by virtue of its prohibition for intercourse or shaving, but by virtue of its prohibition for perfume. Similarly, every violation against ihram is not a violation except by virtue of its prohibition for itself, not for something else. So it must be that before shaving and after are equal regarding intercourse, because what made it a violation before is exactly what remains after, and what has ceased was not the basis of the violation. But what is mentioned in the apparent narration is the absolute imposition of badanah after standing without distinguishing between before or after shaving. ... And al-Hadadi in his commentary on al-Quduri, quoting from al-Wajeez, said that badanah is only obligatory if one does it intentionally; if forgetful, then a sheep. This contradicts the well-known narrations which make no distinction between intentional and forgetful in all violations. Qadikhan explicitly stated: 'If he has intercourse after standing at Arafah, his Hajj is not corrupted and he owes a badanah, whether intentional or forgetful.' That is in Sharh al-Lubab, and the author will mention that intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional. ... Then it is objected that they agreed that if he has intercourse a second time after standing before shaving, no badanah is required, only a sheep, while the obligation for the first intercourse is only due to its prohibition on him, which is exactly present in every intercourse performed before tawaf. So it must be considered that badanah is not obligatory unless the violation is complete, and its completion is by coinciding with a complete ihram. The second intercourse coincided with a deficient ihram, so badanah was not obligatory. Similarly, intercourse after shaving coincided with a deficient ihram because he has exited it with respect to other than women. This chapter—the chapter of violations against ihram—considers the completeness or deficiency of the violation to determine the compensation, as previously in the case of applying perfume to a limb or less, and wearing sewn garments for a day or less, etc., not merely the prohibition of the act. Therefore, their cases show that if the violation is complete, the compensation is severe; if deficient, the compensation is light. So the most appropriate is what is in the matns, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of badanah for intercourse after standing at Arafah. The matn authors maintain a distinction: if before shaving, badanah; if after shaving, sheep. However, a group of later Hanafi scholars (e.g., author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', al-Asbijabi) hold that badanah is obligatory absolutely, regardless of whether before or after shaving. The author of Fath al-Qadeer claims this absolute view is more appropriate because the authority (Ibn Abbas's statement) appears to apply even after shaling. He uses rational argument: the violation is due to the prohibition of intercourse, which persists until tawaf, so whether before or after shaving should not matter. The text then mentions a secondary dispute about forgetfulness: al-Hadadi reports from al-Wajeez that badanah is only for intentional, sheep for forgetful. But the established view (from Qadikhan and the well-known narrations) is that there is no distinction—intentional and forgetful are the same. The passage then refutes the absolute view by pointing to a consensus that a second intercourse before shaving only requires a sheep, not a badanah, showing that the severity depends on the completeness of the ihram. The conclusion is that the mu'tamad position is the detailed one in the matns (badaanah before halq, sheep after).

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): A violation of the prohibitions of ihram that requires expiation (dam, badanah, etc.).
ناسي (nāsī): One who commits a violation forgetfully, i.e., unintentionally.
جزاء (jazā’): Compensation for a violation, such as a badanah or sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what evidence is used to refute the absolute view that badanah is required even after halq?
A) The statement of Ibn Abbas explicitly limits badanah to before halq.
B) The consensus that a second intercourse before halq requires only a sheep.
C) The view of al-Wajeez that forgetful persons only owe a sheep.
D) The argument that perfume and sewn garments do not require badanah.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that badanah is wajib only for intercourse before halq; after halq, only a sheep is due, and this grading is based on the completeness of ihram.

Ruling on Intercourse in Umrah Before Most Tawaf
Explains the consequence of intercourse during Umrah ihram before most tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when intercourse occurs during Umrah before completing most tawaf, and identify the required expiation and consequence.

Core Idea
Intercourse in Umrah before four tawaf circuits invalidates the Umrah and requires a sheep.

This lesson clarifies a specific ruling regarding sexual intercourse during the state of ihram for Umrah. The key threshold is whether the pilgrim has completed most of the tawaf (four out of seven circuits) before the act. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary invalidation and ensures proper expiation if needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the ruling concerns a person in ihram for Umrah who engages in intercourse. Determine at what point in the tawaf this occurs.
The ihram is still intact at the time of the act.
2
Define 'most of tawaf' (akthar al-tawaf)
The text specifies that 'most' means four circuits (ashwaṭ). This is the benchmark: before four circuits is before most, after four circuits is after most.
Tawaf has seven circuits; four is the majority.
3
State the consequence if before four circuits
If intercourse occurs before completing four circuits, the Umrah becomes invalid (fasid). The pilgrim must continue the remaining rituals of the invalidated Umrah, then perform a new Umrah as qada (make-up), and also slaughter one sheep (shah) as expiation.
The Umrah is fasid, not batil; it must still be completed.
4
State the consequence if after four circuits
If intercourse occurs after completing four or more circuits, the Umrah remains valid and no expiation is required. The act is still sinful but does not affect the validity of the Umrah.
The threshold of 'most' protects the validity after four.
5
Note the analogous ruling in Hajj
The text compares this to a similar ruling in Hajj (referred to as 'al-Fath'), establishing consistency: before the majority of the essential acts, intercourse invalidates and requires expiation.
Analogous reasoning (qiyas) across the two rituals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر وتفسد ويمضي ويقضي) أي لو جامع في إحرام العمرة قبل أن يطوف أربعة أشواط لزمه شاة وفسدت عمرته كما لو جامع في الفتح .
His statement: (or in Umrah before he performs most of its tawaf, and it is invalidated, and he continues and makes it up) meaning that if he has intercourse in the ihram of Umrah before he has performed four circuits, a sheep is required and his Umrah is invalidated, just as if he had intercourse in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the matn phrase 'أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر وتفسد ويمضي ويقضي'. It clarifies that if someone in ihram for Umrah engages in intercourse before completing most of the tawaf (i.e., before four circuits out of seven), his Umrah becomes invalid (fasid). He must continue the invalidated Umrah (by completing the remaining actions) and then make it up later with a new Umrah. Additionally, he owes one sheep (shah) as expiation. The ruling is analogous to that of intercourse in Hajj: before the majority of the essential acts, the rite is invalidated. 'الأكثر' here refers to four circuits because the tawaf is seven; most is four. The reference to 'كما لو جامع في الفتح' likely means the same ruling applies as mentioned in another text or section (perhaps Fath al-Qadeer).

Key Terms
طواف (tawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah, a pillar of Umrah and Hajj.
أكثر الطواف (akthar al-tawāf): Most of the tawaf, defined here as four circuits out of seven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One circuit
B) Three circuits
C) Four circuits
D) Seven circuits

Key Takeaway
In Umrah, intercourse before completing four circuits of tawaf invalidates the Umrah and requires a sheep; after four circuits it does not.

Ruling for the Qarin Who Has Intercourse
Rulings for Qarin's intercourse at various stages and an intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for a Qarin who commits intercourse at different stages of Hajj and Umrah, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute after halq regarding the sheep penalty for Umrah.

Core Idea
When a Qarin commits intercourse, penalties vary by timing; after shaving, whether Umrah's ihram is fully dissolved is disputed.

The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not explicitly address the case of a Qarin who has intercourse. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq fills that gap, detailing how the ruling depends critically on the stage of Hajj and Umrah. It also presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a sheep is still due for Umrah after shaving (halq), with the preferred view being that no penalty remains because Umrah's ihram is completely terminated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stages and their default rulings
The passage divides intercourse into three main timings: before standing at Arafah and Umrah tawaf, after Umrah tawaf but before standing, and after tawaf and standing but before tawaf al-ziyarah. For each, note whether Hajj, Umrah, or both are invalidated and what penalties are due.
The dam of qiran is dropped in the first two cases because the pilgrimage becomes invalid.
2
Recognize the agreed-upon ruling before halq
If intercourse occurs after tawaf and standing but before tawaf al-ziyarah and before shaving, there is consensus: neither pilgrimage is invalidated, and the pilgrim owes a badanah for Hajj and a sheep for Umrah.
This is the baseline ruling before the dispute.
3
Locate the two disputes after halq
The text mentions two disagreements after shaving: one about the penalty for Hajj (already settled), and the current dispute about whether a sheep is still due for Umrah. Identify the two positions: majority (Mabsut, Bada'i', Asbajabi) say yes; al-Obari says no.
The first dispute is referenced but not detailed here.
4
Analyze the proofs behind each position
The majority analogize to Hajj, where after halq one remains in ihram regarding women, so Umrah should similarly have a partial ihram. Al-Obari counters that Umrah's ihram is not known to have partial dissolution; shaving ends it completely.
The commentator initially objects but Fath al-Qadir refutes the objection.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Fath al-Qadir declares al-Obari's view as correct because Umrah's ihram is entirely folded up by shaving. Hence no sheep is due for Umrah after halq.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف حكم القارن إذا جامع وحكمه أنه إن كان قبل الوقوف بعرفة وطواف العمرة فسد حجه وعمرته ولزمه دمان وقضاؤهما وسقط عنه دم القرآن وإن كان بعد طواف العمرة أو أكثره قبل الوقوف فسد الحج فقط ولزمه دمان أيضاً وقضاء الحج فقط وسقط عنه دم القرآن، وإن كان بعد الطواف والوقوف قبل طواف الزيارة لم يفسدا وعليه بدنة للحج وشاة للعمرة إن كان قبل الحلق اتفاقاً. واختلفوا فيما إذا كان بعد الحلق في موضعين : الأول في وجوب البدنة للحج أو الشاة وقدمناه والثاني في وجوب شاة للعمرة، فالذي اختاره صاحب المبسوط والبدائع والأسبيجابي أنه يجب شاة للعمرة، والذي اختاره الوبري أنه لا يجب شيء لأجل العمرة لأنه خرج من إحرامها بالحلق وبقي إحرام الحج في حق النساء واستشكله الشارح بأنه إذا بقي محرماً بالحج فكذا في العمرة ورده في فتح القدير بأن إحرام العمرة لم يعهد بحيث يتحلل منه بالحلق من غير النساء ويبقى في حقهن، بل إذا حلق بعد أفعالها حل بالنسبة إلى كل ما حرم عليه وإنما عهد ذلك في إحرام الحج. فإذا ضم إحرام الحج إلى إحرام العمرة استمر كل على ما عهد له في الشرع فينطوي بالحلق إحرام العمرة بالكلية فالصواب ما عن الوبري ا هـ
And the author did not mention the ruling of the Qarin if he has intercourse. His ruling is that if it is before standing at Arafah and the tawaf of Umrah, then his Hajj and Umrah are corrupted, and he owes two penalties (daman) and their qada, and the dam of qiran is dropped. If it is after the tawaf of Umrah or most of it before standing, then only the Hajj is corrupted, and he also owes two penalties and only qada of Hajj, and the dam of qiran is dropped. If it is after tawaf and standing before tawaf al-ziyarah, then neither is corrupted, and he owes a badanah for Hajj and a sheep for Umrah if it is before halq by agreement. They differed regarding when it is after halq in two places: first, regarding the obligation of a badanah for Hajj or a sheep, which we have already presented; second, regarding the obligation of a sheep for Umrah. What the author of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', and al-Asbajabi chose is that a sheep is obligatory for Umrah. What al-Obari chose is that nothing is obligatory for Umrah because he has exited its ihram by shaving and remains in ihram of Hajj regarding women. The commentator objected because if he remains in ihram for Hajj, then likewise for Umrah. This was refuted in Fath al-Qadir because ihram of Umrah is not known to be partially dissolved by shaving while remaining in effect regarding women; rather, when he shaves after its acts, he becomes halal with respect to everything that was forbidden, and that is only known in ihram of Hajj. So when ihram of Hajj is joined to ihram of Umrah, each continues according to what is known in sharia, and by shaving the ihram of Umrah is completely folded up. So the correct view is that of al-Obari.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute. It addresses the case of a pilgrim performing Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) who commits intercourse during ihram. The ruling depends on the timing. Before standing at Arafah and before completing most of Umrah's tawaf, both Hajj and Umrah are invalidated, requiring two penalties and qada of both, and the dam of qiran is dropped. After Umrah's tawaf but before standing, only Hajj is invalidated, still two penalties. After tawaf and standing but before tawaf al-ziyarah, neither is invalidated; he owes a badanah for Hajj and a sheep for Umrah if before shaving. After shaving, there is a dispute: the majority (Mabsut, Bada'i', Asbajabi) hold a sheep is still due for Umrah, but al-Obari says nothing due because shaving completely ends Umrah's ihram, as supported by Fath al-Qadir. The relied-upon view is that of al-Obari.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim performing Hajj and Umrah together with one ihram.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as a penalty for certain ihram violations.
شاة (shāh): A sheep or goat offered as a penalty.
حلقة (halq): Shaving the head (or trimming) to exit the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A sheep is obligatory for Umrah according to the majority.
B) A sheep is not obligatory for Umrah according to al-Obari.
C) A badanah is obligatory for both Hajj and Umrah.
D) No penalty is due at all.

Key Takeaway
For a Qarin who has intercourse after shaving, the mufta bihi is that no sheep is due for Umrah because shaving completely ends its ihram.

Intercourse Before Four Tawaf Circuits Invalidates Umrah
Ruling with qiyas on intercourse before four tawaf circuits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for intercourse in Umrah before completing four tawaf circuits and explain the qiyas with Hajj before Arafah.

Core Idea
Intercourse before four tawaf circuits invalidates Umrah, requiring a sheep and qada, by analogy to Hajj before Arafah.

This passage establishes a clear ruling: if a person in Umrah ihram has intercourse before completing the majority of tawaf (four circuits), the Umrah becomes invalid. The penalty is one sheep, and the person must continue in the invalid state and later perform qada (make-up). The ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy) to the same situation in Hajj, where intercourse before standing at Arafah invalidates Hajj. Understanding this analogy will help you grasp how Hanafi jurists extend rulings from one act of worship to another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intercourse during Umrah ihram before completing four circuits of tawaf. The ruling: the Umrah becomes invalid (fasid/batil), and a sheep (wajib) must be sacrificed, and qada must be performed.
Note that after completing four circuits, intercourse would not invalidate the Umrah.
2
Recognize the analogy (qiyas)
The text explicitly compares this to intercourse in Hajj before standing at Arafah. The common cause (illah) is that the violation occurs before the essential pillar (rukn) is performed. In Hajj, the rukn is standing at Arafah; in Umrah, the rukn is four circuits of tawaf.
The qiyas is jali (clear) because the ruling is directly transferred from Hajj to Umrah based on the same illah.
3
Understand the consequences
The invalid Umrah must still be completed (the person continues in the state of ihram and performs tawaf etc.), and then qada must be performed at a later time. The sheep is a penalty for the violation of ihram.
This is similar to the rule for invalidated Hajj.
4
Differentiate the threshold
The key threshold is 'most of tawaf' which is defined as four circuits (since the rukn of tawaf is four). Before four circuits, the Umrah is invalid; after four, it remains valid (though a penalty may still apply).
This distinction is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر وتفسد ويمضي ويقضي) أي لو جامع في إحرام العمرة قبل أن يطوف أربعة أشواط لزمه شاة وفسدت عمرته كما لو جامع في الحج قبل الوقوف بجامع حصوله قبل إدراك الركن فيهما ويمضي في فاسدها كما يمضي في صحيحها ويلزمه قضاؤها
His statement: '(or in Umrah before he has performed most of its tawaf, and it becomes invalid, and he must continue and perform qada)' meaning: if he has intercourse in the ihram of Umrah before he has performed four circuits, a sheep is incumbent upon him and his Umrah becomes invalid, just as if he had intercourse in Hajj before standing (at Arafah) due to the commonality of its occurrence before attaining the rukn in both, and he continues in his invalid Umrah as he would in a valid one, and he is obligated to perform its qada.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with implicit qiyas. The text explains the ruling for intercourse during Umrah before completing the majority of tawaf (four circuits). The penalty is one sheep, and the Umrah becomes invalid, requiring him to continue in the invalid state (as if valid) and later make it up (qada). The reasoning is analogy with Hajj: just as intercourse before standing at Arafah invalidates Hajj, similarly intercourse before reaching the rukn of Umrah (which is the tawaf, at least four circuits) invalidates Umrah. The key point is that the violation occurs before the essential pillar (rukn) is performed, thus the act is invalidated.

Key Terms
طواف الأكثر (ṭawāf al-akthar): The majority of tawaf, i.e., four out of seven circuits.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up an invalidated act of worship after its time.
ركن (rukn): Essential pillar of an act; without it the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the penalty for intercourse in Umrah before completing four tawaf circuits?
A) A badanah and the Umrah is invalid.
B) A sheep and the Umrah becomes invalid, requiring qada.
C) No penalty, only the Umrah is invalid.
D) Two sheep and qada of both Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before the rukn (four tawaf circuits) in Umrah invalidates it and necessitates a sheep and qada, by qiyas to Hajj before Arafah.

Forgetful Intercourse in Ihram: Same Penalty as Intentional
Ruling with usuli reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that forgetful intercourse during ihram invalidates Hajj and requires a penalty, and explain the usuli principle that forgetfulness does not negate obligation.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness in ihram does not exempt from penalty — the act is still a violation.

In Hajj, certain acts invalidate the pilgrimage and require a penalty (dam or qada). What if the pilgrim forgets they are in ihram and commits intercourse? Does forgetfulness excuse them? The Hanafi school rules that forgetfulness does not remove the penalty or the invalidation, though it may remove sin. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sexual intercourse performed forgetfully before standing at Arafah during Hajj. The ruling: the Hajj becomes invalid (fasid/batil) and a penalty (dam) is wajib, just like intentional intercourse.
The text explicitly equates forgetful and intentional in 'جماع الناسي كالعامد'.
2
Understand the usuli principle
The principle 'al-nisyān lā yunāfī al-wujūb' means forgetfulness does not negate obligation. The person retains full intellect, so the obligation to avoid the act remains. However, forgetfulness may remove sin in matters purely between man and Allah (like fasting). In rights of servants (like Hajj invalidating), forgetfulness does not excuse the penalty.
This distinction explains why forgetful eating breaks prayer but not fast.
3
Apply the principle to analogous cases
The text compares: (a) eating while praying: forgetfulness does not excuse because prayer is a right of Allah with no motive; (b) saying salam in the wrong sitting: forgetfulness does excuse because there is a motive (to end prayer) and no reminder; (c) eating while fasting: forgetfulness excuses because fasting tolerates forgetfulness; (d) leaving takbir by slaughterer: forgetfulness excuses by greater reason.
These analogies help delineate when forgetfulness drops the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وجماع الناسي كالعامد) يعني في جميع ما ذكرنا من أحكام الجنايات فيفسد حجه لو جامع ناسياً قبل الوقوف وحاصل ما ذكره الأصوليون أن النسيان لا ينافي الوجوب لكمال العقل وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوق الله تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي وجناية المحرم لم يسقط بتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة، وإن كان ليس مع مذكر مع داع إليه سقط كأكل الصائم، وإن لم يكن معهما فكذلك بالأولى كترك الذابح التسمية .انتهى. وقد قدمنا أن الجاهل والعالم والمختار والمكره والنائم والمستيقظ سواء الحصول الارتفاق
His statement: '(and the intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional)' meaning in all the rulings of violations that we have mentioned, so his Hajj becomes invalid if he has intercourse forgetfully before standing. The gist of what the usuliyyun have mentioned is that forgetfulness does not negate obligation due to completeness of intellect, and it is not an excuse in the rights of servants, and in the rights of Allah it is an excuse for the dropping of sin. As for the ruling: with a reminder and no motive, like eating of the praying person and the violation of the muhrim is not dropped due to his negligence, unlike his salam in the qa'dah. If there is no reminder but there is a motive, it is dropped like the eating of the fasting person. If neither exists, then all the more so, like leaving the takbir by the slaughterer. End. And we have already stated that the ignorant and the knowledgeable, the one who chooses and the one who is compelled, the sleeper and the awake are equal in the ruling of the violation.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with usul reasoning. It establishes that forgetfulness does not exempt one from the obligation of penalty for ihram violations. The Hajj is invalidated even if intercourse is done forgetfully before standing. The usuli principle: forgetfulness does not negate the obligation because the person is still of sound mind; however, it may remove sin. But for the penal consequences (dam, qada), it is the same as intentional. The text analogizes to other cases: eating while praying nullifies prayer even if forgetful, but saying salam in the wrong place does not nullify if forgetful. For fasting, eating forgetfully does not break the fast. For ihram violations, forgetfulness does not remove the penalty because the person is responsible for maintaining the state of ihram. The ruling also includes the ignorant, compelled, sleeper, etc. as equal in incurring the penalty.

Key Terms
الناسي (al-nāsī): One who forgets that they are in ihram.
النسيان لا ينافي الوجوب (al-nisyān lā yunāfī al-wujūb): Principle that forgetfulness does not negate the obligation of the act or its replacement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a forgetful person who has intercourse during ihram before standing at Arafah?
A) No penalty and Hajj remains valid.
B) The Hajj becomes invalid but no qada is due.
C) The Hajj becomes invalid and a penalty is due, just like an intentional act.
D) Only sin is removed, but no penalty.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness does not negate the obligation or penalty for ihram violations; the Hanafi ruling equates forgetful intercourse with intentional in all consequences.

Tawaf without Wudu Obligates a Sheep: The Verbal Dispute
Ruling with proof and clarification of verbal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for tawaf performed without wudu and explain why the internal Hanafi dispute is considered verbal (khilaf lafzi).

Core Idea
Purity for tawaf is wajib; omitting it requires a sheep, and the dispute between wajib and sunnah is merely verbal.

In this passage, the author clarifies a key ruling in Hajj: performing tawaf without wudu (in a state of hadath) obligates a sacrificial sheep. More importantly, he reveals that an apparent disagreement among Hanafis about whether purity is obligatory (wajib) or merely recommended (sunnah) has no practical effect because both positions require the same penalty. This is a classic example of ikhtilaf lafzi (verbal dispute). We will examine the proof from the Sunnah and understand the legal reasoning behind the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the penalty
The act is performing tawaf for the rukn while in a state of hadath (without wudu). The penalty is a sheep (dam) for leaving purity.
The author states 'يلزمه شاة' (a sheep is incumbent upon him).
2
Understand the internal Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafis consider purity for tawaf as wajib; others as sunnah. However, both agree that a dam is due for omission. This is proven by the statement that even the view calling it sunnah still requires expiation, citing Muhammad's ruling on departing Arafat early.
The text says 'الخلف لفظي لا ثمرة له' – the dispute is verbal with no practical consequence.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The dalil is the hadith from Aisha (ra) where the Prophet (saw) told her: 'اقضي ما يقضي الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي بالبيت' – 'Perform what the pilgrim performs except do not circumambulate the House.' The prohibition of tawaf is linked to the absence of purity, indicating purity is a condition.
The hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
4
Recognize the verbal nature of the dispute
The dispute is only about terminology: whether to call purity 'wajib' or 'sunnah'. The practical ruling (dam for omission) is agreed upon. Thus, the dispute is lafzi.
Be careful not to misunderstand; both opinions require the same action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو طاف للركن محدثاً) أي يلزمه شاة لترك الطهارة لأنه أدخل نقصاً في الركن فصار كترك شوط منه وظاهر كلام غاية البيان أن الدم واجب اتفاقاً، أما على القول بوجوبها وهو الأصح فظاهر، وأما على القول بسنيتها فلأنه لا أن تكون سنة ويجب بتركها الكفارة ولهذا قال محمد فيمن أفاض من عرفة قبل الإمام لأنه ترك سنة الدفع ا هـ . وبهذا علم أن الخلف لفظي لا ثمرة له. وإنما كانت الطهارة واجبة لما ثبت في الصحيحين عن عائشة أنها حاضت فقال لها عليه السلام: اقضي ما يقضي الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي بالبيت رتب منع الطواف على انتفاء الطهارة وهذا حكم وسبب، وظاهره أن الحكم يتعلق بالسبب فيكون المنع لعدم الطهارة لا لعدم دخول المسجد. إذا ثم ترك الواجب أشد اهـ. اللهم إلا أن يقال : مراده الثمرة في وجوب الدم وعدمه. يمتنع يجب عليه دم
His statement: '(or he performed tawaf of the rukn while in a state of hadath)' meaning: a sheep is incumbent upon him for leaving purity because he introduced a deficiency in the rukn, so it is like leaving a circuit from it. The apparent wording of Ghayat al-Bayan is that the dam is agreed upon. As for the view that purity is obligatory (and that is the correct view), it is apparent; as for the view that it is a sunnah, it is because it cannot be a sunnah while it is obligatory to offer expiation for leaving it, which is why Muhammad said regarding one who departed from Arafah before the imam that he left the sunnah of departure. From this it is known that the dispute is verbal (lafzi) with no practical consequence. Purity is wajib because it is established in the two Sahihs from Aisha that she menstruated, and he ﷺ said: 'Perform what the pilgrim performs except do not circumambulate the House.' He linked the prohibition of tawaf to the absence of purity. This is a ruling and a cause, and its apparent meaning is that the ruling is attached to the cause, so the prohibition is due to lack of purity, not due to not entering the mosque. Therefore, leaving the wajib is severe. Unless it is said that he meant the consequence in terms of the obligation of dam or not. It is prevented, a dam is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and a note on the nature of a dispute. It states that performing tawaf for the rukn (four circuits) while in a state of hadath (without wudu) obligates a sheep. This is because purity (tahara) is a wajib condition for tawaf, and omitting it introduces a deficiency in the rukn itself, akin to omitting one circuit. The text clarifies that there is a dispute among Hanafis about whether purity is obligatory (wajib) or recommended (sunnah) for tawaf. It argues that this dispute is purely verbal: even those who call it sunnah agree that leaving it requires expiation, as seen in the case of departing from Arafah before the imam. The proof for the obligation is the hadith of Aisha (ra) where the Prophet (saw) told her to do everything except tawaf, which indicates that the prohibition of tawaf is because of impurity, not because of entering the mosque. Thus, purity is a wajib condition.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-ḥadath): State of ritual impurity (minor or major) that invalidates wudu.
الخلف لفظي (al-khilāf lafẓī): A verbal dispute with no practical difference; both sides agree on the outcome (dam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of the dispute about whether purity for tawaf is wajib or sunnah?
A) One view requires a sheep, the other does not.
B) Both views require a sheep for omission.
C) One view invalidates Hajj, the other does not.
D) There is no penalty in either view.

Key Takeaway
Purity for tawaf is wajib; omitting it requires a dam, and any internal dispute about its classification is purely verbal.

Repeating Tawaf with Impurity: Recommendation vs Obligation
Critical refinement on the ruling of repeating tawaf with impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings for repeating tawaf with minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah), and state the consequence of delaying the repetition.

Core Idea
Repetition of tawaf is recommended for minor impurity but obligatory for major impurity; delay requires a dam.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a lacuna in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author notes that the matn did not specify the ruling for repeating tawaf when performed with impurity. The commentator al-Nahr, citing al-Asbajabi, provides the critical refinement: the ruling depends on the type of impurity. This distinction is essential for understanding the legal consequences and potential required sacrifice (dam).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is repeating tawaf that was performed while the pilgrim was in a state of impurity. Two types of impurity are distinguished: minor (hadath, e.g., breaking wudu) and major (janabah, requiring ghusl).
Minor impurity refers to anything that invalidates wudu; major impurity is janabah.
2
Extract the ruling for each impurity
For minor impurity (hadath), repetition of tawaf is recommended (nadb). For major impurity (janabah), repetition is obligatory (wajib).
Nadb means it is meritorious but not sinful to omit; wajib means omission incurs a penalty.
3
Understand the timing consequence
If the pilgrim repeats the tawaf within the days of sacrifice (11th–13th Dhul Hijjah), no additional dam is required. If repetition is delayed beyond these days, a dam becomes wajib due to the delay.
The dam is a type of penalty, not for the original impure tawaf, but for delaying the required repetition.
4
Note the authority
al-Nahr and al-Asbajabi state this as the most correct view (al-ashah), based on the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa. This is a later fatwa (fatawa mutakhkhirin) not found in the earlier matn.
The term 'al-ashah' indicates a preferred view among later Hanafi jurists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يذكر صفة الإعادة الخ قال في النهر : والأصح ندبها مع الحدث وجوبها مع الجنابة فإن أعاده في أيام النحر فلا ذبح وإلا وجب عليه دم عند الإمام للتأخير . قاله الأسبيجابي قوله: (فلا
His statement: '(and he did not mention the description of repetition...). Al-Nahr said: The most correct view is that it is recommended with hadath and obligatory with janabah. If he repeats it within the days of sacrifice, then no slaughter; otherwise, a dam becomes obligatory upon him according to Imam Abu Hanifa due to delay. Al-Asbajabi said this. His statement: (so not...)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from a hashya. It addresses a lacuna in the matn regarding the description of repeating tawaf when performed with impurity. The super-commentator (from al-Nahr) clarifies that if tawaf was performed without wudu (minor impurity), repeating it is recommended (nadb), but if it was done without ghusl (major impurity, janabah), repetition is obligatory. If the repetition is done within the days of sacrifice, no additional dam is needed; if delayed beyond them, a dam is due for delaying. This is based on the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
الندب (an-nadb): Recommended but not obligatory.
الجنابة (al-janābah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nahr, what is the ruling for someone who performed tawaf with janabah and then repeats it?
A) The repetition is recommended, and no dam is needed.
B) The repetition is obligatory, and if delayed beyond days of sacrifice, a dam is due.
C) The repetition is obligatory but no dam is ever needed.
D) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated with no additional penalty.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on repeating tawaf after impurity depends on the type: nadb for minor, wajib for major; a dam for delay applies if repetition is done after the days of sacrifice.

Intercourse After Four Tawafs in Umrah: Ruling and Penalty
Explains ruling on intercourse after four tawafs in Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse after four tawafs in Umrah and explain the reason for the distinction between Hajj and Umrah.

Core Idea
After four tawafs in Umrah, the Umrah remains valid but a sheep is due to show the difference between obligatory Hajj and sunnah Umrah.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced Hanafi ruling: what happens if someone has intercourse after completing most of the tawaf in Umrah? The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that the Umrah is not invalidated, but a penalty of a sheep is required. We'll explore the reasoning and compare it with Hajj, where a camel is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is sexual intercourse during Umrah while in ihram. The key context is that it occurs after the majority of tawaf (four circuits).
The majority of tawaf (tawaf al-akthar) means four out of seven circuits.
2
State the ruling and penalty
According to the Hanafi school, if intercourse occurs after four tawafs, the Umrah is still valid, but a sheep (shah) must be sacrificed as a penalty. This is based on the author's statement 'لزمه شاة ولا تفسد عمرته'.
If intercourse occurs before completing four tawafs, the Umrah is invalidated and a camel is due.
3
Understand the reason for the distinction from Hajj
In Hajj, after standing at Arafat, if one has intercourse, a camel is due because the remaining pillar (tawaf) is still to be performed, so the offense is more severe. In Umrah, after four tawafs, the pillar (tawaf) is complete, so only obligations remain, resulting in a lighter penalty.
The difference in penalty (sheep vs. camel) highlights the distinction between fard (obligatory) and sunnah (recommended) acts.
4
Note the intra-madhhab disagreement
Some Hanafi scholars argue that this distinction applies only to the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam), not to supererogatory Hajj or Umrah, because both are supererogatory before starting. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the distinction is general.
The author references Al-Hidayah as support for the general application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج قبل الوقوف بجامع حصوله قبل إدراك الركن فيهما ويمضي في فاسدها كما يمضي في صحيحها ويلزمه قضاؤها قوله : (أو بعد طواف الأكثر ولا فساد أي لو جامع بعد ما طاف أربعة أشواط لزمه شاة ولا تفسد عمرته لأنه أتى بالركن فصار كالجماع بعد الوقوف. وإنما لم تجب بدنة كما في الحج إظهاراً للتفاوت بين الفرض والسنة. كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وقد يقال : إنه يتم في حجة الإسلام أما في غيرها فلا فرق بين الحج والعمرة لأن كلاً منهما نفل قبل الشروع واجب بعده اللهم إلا أن يقال: نفل الحج أقوى من نفل العمرة. والفرق بينهما بأن الجماع في الحج بعد الوقوف يكون قبل أداء بقية أركان الحج لأنه بقي الطواف وهو ركن فتغلظت الجناية فتغلظ الجزاء بخلافه بعد طواف الأكثر في العمرة فإنه لم يبق عليه إلا الواجبات لا أنه يقتضي وجوب البدنة لو جامع قبل طواف الأكثر وليس كذلك. يصح فإن كان وشمل قوله بعد طواف الأكثر ما إذا طاف الباقي وسعى بين الصفا والمروة أولاً لكن بشرط أن يكون قبل الحلق وتركه للعلم به لأن بالحلق يخرج عن إحرامها بالكلية بخلاف إحرام الحج، ولما بين المصنف حكم المفرد بالحج والمفرد بالعمرة علم منه حكم القارن والمتمتع قوله: (وجماع الناسي كالعامد) يعني في جميع ما ذكرنا من أحكام الجنايات فيفسد حجه لو جامع ناسياً قبل الوقوف وحاصل ما ذكره الأصوليون أن النسيان لا ينافي الوجوب لكمال العقل وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوق الله تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي وجناية المحرم لم يسقط بتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة، وإن كان ليس مع مذكر مع داع إليه سقط كأكل الصائم، وإن لم يكن معهما فكذلك بالأولى كترك الذابح التسمية .انتهى. وقد قدمنا أن الجاهل والعالم والمختار والمكره والنائم والمستيقظ سواء الحصول الارتفاق
Hajj before standing (at Arafat) is similar to [intercourse] before performing the pillar in both, and one proceeds in the invalid [Hajj] as one proceeds in the valid one, and its make-up is obligatory. His statement: 'Or after the majority of tawaf, and no invalidation' meaning: if one has intercourse after performing four circuits, a sheep is incumbent upon him, and his Umrah is not invalid because he performed the pillar, so it becomes like intercourse after standing. A camel was not required as in Hajj to show the difference between the obligatory and the sunnah. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. And it may be said: it applies to the Hajj of Islam; otherwise there is no difference between Hajj and Umrah because each is supererogatory before beginning and obligatory after it. Unless it is said: the supererogatory Hajj is stronger than the supererogatory Umrah. And the difference between them is that intercourse in Hajj after standing occurs before performing the remaining pillars of Hajj because tawaf remains and it is a pillar, so the offense is aggravated and the penalty is aggravated, unlike after the majority of tawaf in Umrah because nothing remains except obligations. It does not necessitate the obligation of a camel if one had intercourse before the majority of tawaf, and it is not like that. It is valid? And his statement 'after the majority of tawaf' includes the case where one performed the remaining [circuits] and the sa'y between Safa and Marwa first, but on condition that it be before shaving the head, and leaving it is due to knowledge of it because by shaving one exits from the ihram of Umrah entirely, unlike the ihram of Hajj. And since the author explained the ruling of the individual for Hajj and the individual for Umrah, from it one knows the ruling of the qarin and mutamatti'. His statement: 'Intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional' means in all the rulings of offenses we mentioned, so his Hajj is invalid if he forgetfully has intercourse before standing. And the conclusion of what the usuliyyun mentioned is that forgetfulness does not negate obligation due to completeness of intellect and is not an excuse in the rights of people, and in the rights of Allah it is an excuse in dropping sin. As for the ruling when there is a reminder and no need, like the eating of the praying person and the offense of the muhrim, it is not dropped due to his negligence, unlike his salam in the sitting. And if there is no reminder with a need, it drops like the eating of the fasting person. And if there is neither, then by greater priority it is so, like the slaughterer leaving the basmalah. End. And we have already stated that the ignorant and the knowledgeable, the willing and the coerced, the sleeping and the awake are equal in [whether] attainment of facilitation?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling on sexual intercourse during Umrah after performing the majority of tawaf (four circuits). The author clarifies that if one has intercourse after completing four tawafs, the Umrah remains valid, but a sheep (shah) must be sacrificed as a penalty. This is contrasted with Hajj, where intercourse after standing at Arafat requires a camel (badanah) and does not invalidate the Hajj but imposes a heavier penalty. The reason for the distinction is to show the difference between the obligatory Hajj (fard) and the sunnah Umrah. However, some scholars argue this only applies to the obligatory Hajj; for supererogatory pilgrimage, there is no difference. The passage also addresses the forgetful person (nasi): if one forgetfully has intercourse before standing, the Hajj is invalidated, and the penalty is the same as intentional. The usuliyyun explain that forgetfulness does not remove the obligation of compensation, though it may remove sin. The rule is that forgetfulness is not an excuse in matters of worship (huquq Allah) for dropping the ruling, but it is an excuse for sin. The author then mentions that the ignorant, the knowledgeable, the willing, the coerced, the sleeping, and the awake are all equal in that the penalty is obligatory, though the text here is somewhat unclear.

Key Terms
طواف الأكثر (tawaf al-akthar): The majority of tawaf, defined as four out of seven circuits.
شاة (shah): A sheep, as a penalty (dam) for certain ihram offenses.
بدنة (badanah): A camel, required as a penalty for more severe ihram offenses, e.g., intercourse before the pillar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Umrah is invalid and a camel is due.
B) The Umrah is valid and a sheep is due.
C) The Umrah is valid and no penalty is due.
D) The Umrah is invalid and a sheep is due.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after four tawafs in Umrah does not invalidate the Umrah, but a sheep penalty is due, in contrast to Hajj where a camel is required.
