Forgetfulness in Ihram: Sin vs. Compensation
Explains forgetfulness in ihram and its effect on sin and compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that forgetfulness in ihram offenses removes sin but not the obligation of compensation.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness in ihram offenses does not cancel the requirement for compensation, but it lifts the sin.

In this lesson, we extract a key usul principle from the passage: the forgetful person (nasi) is treated like the intentional one regarding the obligation of compensation (dam) but differs regarding sin. The Hanafi school maintains that in rights of Allah (huquq Allah), forgetfulness is an excuse for sin but not for dropping the required compensation. We'll examine how this applies to the muhrim's offense of intercourse and other examples.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between sin (ithm) and compensation (jaza)
In Islamic law, some offenses have both a spiritual consequence (sin) and a material consequence (penalty). Forgetfulness can affect the former but not necessarily the latter.
The source text states: 'النسيان لا ينافي الوجوب لكمال العقل' (forgetfulness does not negate obligation due to completeness of intellect).
2
Apply to the muhrim's intercourse
If a muhrim forgetfully has intercourse before standing at Arafat, the Hajj is invalidated and a camel is due, just as if intentional. However, the person is not sinful for the forgetfulness.
The text says: 'يفسد حجه لو جامع ناسياً قبل الوقوف' (his Hajj is invalid if he forgetfully has intercourse before standing).
3
Understand the usul principle behind it
The usuliyyun (methodologists) state: forgetfulness is not an excuse in rights of Allah for dropping the ruling (hukm taklifi), but it is an excuse for dropping sin (ithm). This is due to the completeness of intellect; the obligation remains because the person is legally responsible.
The text contrasts this with rights of people (huquq al-'ibad) where forgetfulness may be an excuse.
4
Note the exceptions and comparisons
The text compares with other acts: a praying person who eats forgetfully (sin drops but compensation? they mention a difference), a fasting person who eats forgetfully (no penalty), a slaughterer who forgets basmalah (ruling differs). The key factor is whether there is a reminder (mudhakkir) and need (dai').
This part is somewhat complex and may require further study; focus on the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج قبل الوقوف بجامع حصوله قبل إدراك الركن فيهما ويمضي في فاسدها كما يمضي في صحيحها ويلزمه قضاؤها قوله : (أو بعد طواف الأكثر ولا فساد أي لو جامع بعد ما طاف أربعة أشواط لزمه شاة ولا تفسد عمرته لأنه أتى بالركن فصار كالجماع بعد الوقوف. وإنما لم تجب بدنة كما في الحج إظهاراً للتفاوت بين الفرض والسنة. كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وقد يقال : إنه يتم في حجة الإسلام أما في غيرها فلا فرق بين الحج والعمرة لأن كلاً منهما نفل قبل الشروع واجب بعده اللهم إلا أن يقال: نفل الحج أقوى من نفل العمرة. والفرق بينهما بأن الجماع في الحج بعد الوقوف يكون قبل أداء بقية أركان الحج لأنه بقي الطواف وهو ركن فتغلظت الجناية فتغلظ الجزاء بخلافه بعد طواف الأكثر في العمرة فإنه لم يبق عليه إلا الواجبات لا أنه يقتضي وجوب البدنة لو جامع قبل طواف الأكثر وليس كذلك. يصح فإن كان وشمل قوله بعد طواف الأكثر ما إذا طاف الباقي وسعى بين الصفا والمروة أولاً لكن بشرط أن يكون قبل الحلق وتركه للعلم به لأن بالحلق يخرج عن إحرامها بالكلية بخلاف إحرام الحج، ولما بين المصنف حكم المفرد بالحج والمفرد بالعمرة علم منه حكم القارن والمتمتع قوله: (وجماع الناسي كالعامد) يعني في جميع ما ذكرنا من أحكام الجنايات فيفسد حجه لو جامع ناسياً قبل الوقوف وحاصل ما ذكره الأصوليون أن النسيان لا ينافي الوجوب لكمال العقل وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوق الله تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي وجناية المحرم لم يسقط بتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة، وإن كان ليس مع مذكر مع داع إليه سقط كأكل الصائم، وإن لم يكن معهما فكذلك بالأولى كترك الذابح التسمية .انتهى. وقد قدمنا أن الجاهل والعالم والمختار والمكره والنائم والمستيقظ سواء الحصول الارتفاق
Hajj before standing (at Arafat) is similar to [intercourse] before performing the pillar in both, and one proceeds in the invalid [Hajj] as one proceeds in the valid one, and its make-up is obligatory. His statement: 'Or after the majority of tawaf, and no invalidation' meaning: if one has intercourse after performing four circuits, a sheep is incumbent upon him, and his Umrah is not invalid because he performed the pillar, so it becomes like intercourse after standing. A camel was not required as in Hajj to show the difference between the obligatory and the sunnah. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. And it may be said: it applies to the Hajj of Islam; otherwise there is no difference between Hajj and Umrah because each is supererogatory before beginning and obligatory after it. Unless it is said: the supererogatory Hajj is stronger than the supererogatory Umrah. And the difference between them is that intercourse in Hajj after standing occurs before performing the remaining pillars of Hajj because tawaf remains and it is a pillar, so the offense is aggravated and the penalty is aggravated, unlike after the majority of tawaf in Umrah because nothing remains except obligations. It does not necessitate the obligation of a camel if one had intercourse before the majority of tawaf, and it is not like that. It is valid? And his statement 'after the majority of tawaf' includes the case where one performed the remaining [circuits] and the sa'y between Safa and Marwa first, but on condition that it be before shaving the head, and leaving it is due to knowledge of it because by shaving one exits from the ihram of Umrah entirely, unlike the ihram of Hajj. And since the author explained the ruling of the individual for Hajj and the individual for Umrah, from it one knows the ruling of the qarin and mutamatti'. His statement: 'Intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional' means in all the rulings of offenses we mentioned, so his Hajj is invalid if he forgetfully has intercourse before standing. And the conclusion of what the usuliyyun mentioned is that forgetfulness does not negate obligation due to completeness of intellect and is not an excuse in the rights of people, and in the rights of Allah it is an excuse in dropping sin. As for the ruling when there is a reminder and no need, like the eating of the praying person and the offense of the muhrim, it is not dropped due to his negligence, unlike his salam in the sitting. And if there is no reminder with a need, it drops like the eating of the fasting person. And if there is neither, then by greater priority it is so, like the slaughterer leaving the basmalah. End. And we have already stated that the ignorant and the knowledgeable, the willing and the coerced, the sleeping and the awake are equal in [whether] attainment of facilitation?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling on sexual intercourse during Umrah after performing the majority of tawaf (four circuits). The author clarifies that if one has intercourse after completing four tawafs, the Umrah remains valid, but a sheep (shah) must be sacrificed as a penalty. This is contrasted with Hajj, where intercourse after standing at Arafat requires a camel (badanah) and does not invalidate the Hajj but imposes a heavier penalty. The reason for the distinction is to show the difference between the obligatory Hajj (fard) and the sunnah Umrah. However, some scholars argue this only applies to the obligatory Hajj; for supererogatory pilgrimage, there is no difference. The passage also addresses the forgetful person (nasi): if one forgetfully has intercourse before standing, the Hajj is invalidated, and the penalty is the same as intentional. The usuliyyun explain that forgetfulness does not remove the obligation of compensation, though it may remove sin. The rule is that forgetfulness is not an excuse in matters of worship (huquq Allah) for dropping the ruling, but it is an excuse for sin. The author then mentions that the ignorant, the knowledgeable, the willing, the coerced, the sleeping, and the awake are all equal in that the penalty is obligatory, though the text here is somewhat unclear.

Key Terms
ناسي (nasi): A forgetful person; one who inadvertently commits an act.
إثم (ithm): Sin, moral culpability.
مذكر (mudhakkir): A reminder; something that should prompt the person to remember the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of forgetfulness on the penalty (dam) for intercourse in ihram?
A) The penalty is completely waived.
B) The penalty is reduced (e.g., from camel to sheep).
C) The penalty remains the same as for intentional.
D) The penalty is replaced by a verbal repentance.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness in ihram offenses removes sin but does not remove the obligation of compensation; the muhrim must still pay the due penalty.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Ruling on Tawaf While Impure
Explains compensations for tawaf with impurity with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf performed with minor and major impurity, explain why purity is considered wajib rather than a condition, and identify the required compensations.

Core Idea
Tawaf while impure is valid but requires compensation: a sheep for hadath, a camel for janaba.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq details the Hanafi position on performing the essential tawaf (tawaf al-rukun) while in a state of impurity. The author distinguishes between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janaba), specifying the required compensation and the ruling on repetition. The proof is from the authentic hadith of Aisha (ra), which the Hanafis interpret as establishing purity as a wajib, not a condition. Understanding this distinction clarifies why tawaf remains valid yet incurs a penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tawaf al-rukun (essential tawaf) performed with impurity. The Hanafi ruling is that such tawaf is valid but requires compensation: a sheep for hadath, a camel for janaba, and repetition is wajib for janaba, mustahabb for hadath.
Note the distinction between hadath and janaba.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'Do what the pilgrims do, except do not perform tawaf of the House.' This is a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) with zanni thubut and dalala.
The Hanafis use this to argue that purity is a wajib, not a shart.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet prohibited tawaf when purity is absent. This indicates a connection (ta'liq) between the ruling and the cause. The Hanafis interpret this as making purity a wajib, omission of which requires compensation, not invalidation.
Shafi'is see the same hadith as making purity a condition (shart) for validity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that purity is a condition for tawaf; tawaf without it is invalid and must be repeated without compensation. The Hanafi response is that making it a condition would require restricting the Quranic command (Surah al-Hajj 29) with this solitary hadith, which constitutes abrogation and is impermissible.
The dispute is based on usul al-fiqh principles regarding the use of solitary hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says valid with compensation (sheep/camel), Shafi'i says invalid must be repeated. Also, within Hanafi, repetition is wajib for janaba and mustahabb for hadath.
The mufta bihi position: sheep for hadath, camel for janaba, repetition wajib for janaba, mustahabb for hadath.

راجع إلى الطواف محدثاً أو جنباً، ولم يذكر صفة الإعادة للاختلاف، وصحح في الهداية أنها واجبة في الطواف جنباً مستحبة في الطواف محدثاً للفحش في الأول والقصور في الثاني، فإن أعاده فلا عليه فيهما مطلقاً أيام النحر لزمه الدم عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله بالتأخير ا.هـ. هذا وسيذكر المصنف أنه لو طاف للركن جنباً وللصدر طاهراً أن عليه دمين أي وتسقط البدنة لوقوع طواف الصدر عن طواف الركن فعليه دم لتأخيره ودم لترك الصدر إن
His statement: 'Or if he performed tawaf for the pillar while in a state of hadath' meaning: a sheep is incumbent upon him for leaving purity because he introduced a deficiency into the pillar, so it becomes like leaving a circuit of it. The apparent meaning of Ghayat al-Bayan is that the blood (penalty) is obligatory by agreement. As for the opinion of its obligation, which is the most correct, it is apparent. As for the opinion of its being sunnah, it is because [purity] cannot be sunnah and require expiation for leaving it; hence Muhammad said concerning one who departed from Arafat before the imam because he left the sunnah of the departure. From this it is known that the dispute is verbal with no consequence. Purity was only obligatory because it is established in the Two Sahihs from Aisha that she menstruated and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to her: 'Do what the pilgrims do, except do not perform tawaf of the House.' He made the prohibition of tawaf conditional on the absence of purity, and this is a ruling and a cause. Its apparent meaning is that the ruling is connected to the cause, so the prohibition is due to the lack of purity, not due to not entering the mosque. Then leaving the obligatory is more severe. End. Unless it is said: his intention is the consequence in the obligation of blood or not. He refrains? A blood penalty is obligatory upon him. His statement: 'And he did not mention the description of repetition.' Al-Nahr said: The correct view is that it is recommended with hadath and obligatory with janaba. If he repeats it during the Days of Nahr, then no slaughter; otherwise, a blood penalty is obligatory upon him according to Imam Abu Hanifa due to delay, as stated by al-Asbajabi. His statement: 'So if he performed tawaf for the pillar while in hadath, and a camel if junub, and he repeats, and charity if in hadath for the tawaf of arrival and departure, or leaves less.' It was not made a condition as al-Shafi'i said because it would necessitate restricting the absolute definitive [verse] 'let them perform tawaf' [Surah al-Hajj 29] with a solitary hadith, which is abrogation according to us, so it is not permissible as known in usul. As for his statement (peace be upon him) 'Tawaf around the House is prayer,' what is meant is resemblance in reward. He restricted it to hadath because if he performed tawaf while his garment has najasa more than the size of a dirham, then nothing is incumbent upon him, but it is disliked due to bringing najasa into the mosque. Nothing was stated in Zahir al-Riwayah except about the garment, and the reasoning indicates no distinction between garment and body. What is in al-Zahiriyya that impurity of the entire garment requires blood has no basis in the riwaya, so it is not relied upon. He indicated that if he performed tawaf with his awrah uncovered to the extent that prayer is not valid with it, then a blood penalty is incumbent upon him due to leaving the obligatory, which is covering the awrah, as stated in al-Zahiriyya. The evidence for obligation is his statement: 'Let no polytheist perform Hajj after this year, and let no one perform tawaf around the House naked,' based on the fact that a solitary hadith indicates obligation according to us. He restricted it to the pillar, i.e., the majority, because if he performed its minimum while in hadath and did not repeat, he is obligated for each circuit half a sa' of wheat, unless its value reaches a blood penalty, then he may reduce from it as he wishes. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. His statement: 'And a camel if junub, and he repeats' meaning: a camel is obligatory if he performed tawaf for the pillar while junub. Thus narrated from Ibn Abbas. And because the offense is more severe, so compensation for its deficiency must be with a camel to show the difference between them. Menstruation and postnatal bleeding are like janaba. He restricted it to the pillar, i.e., the majority, because if he performed the minimum while junub and did not repeat, a sheep is obligatory upon him. If he repeats it, charity (sadaqa) is obligatory upon him due to delaying the minimum of tawaf al-ziyarah: for each circuit half a sa'. His statement 'and he repeats' refers to tawaf while in hadath or janaba. He did not mention the description of repetition due to difference of opinion. It was corrected in al-Hidayah that it is obligatory in tawaf while junub and recommended in tawaf while in hadath due to the severity in the former and lightness in the latter. If he repeats, then nothing is upon him in both cases absolutely because the deficiency is compensated by repetition, except that if he repeats and had... blood upon him in both. His statement 'absolutely' apparently means during the Days of Nahr or after them, but it is specific to tawaf while in hadath, evidenced by what follows. The phrase of al-Hidayah: 'Then if he repeats after having performed tawaf while in hadath, there is no slaughter upon him even if he repeats after the Days of Nahr because after repetition, only the semblance of deficiency remains. If he repeats after having performed tawaf while junub during the Days of Nahr, then nothing is upon him because he repeated in its proper time. If he repeats after the Days of Nahr, a blood penalty is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa due to delay.' End. This, and the author will mention that if he performed tawaf for the pillar while junub and for the departure while pure, then two blood penalties are upon him, meaning: the camel is dropped because the tawaf of departure takes the place of the tawaf of the pillar, so he owes blood for delay and blood for leaving the departure if...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq details the penalties for performing the essential tawaf (tawaf al-rukun, i.e., tawaf al-ifadah) while in a state of impurity. The author distinguishes between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janaba, including menstruation and postnatal bleeding). For minor impurity, one must slaughter a sheep (shah) and repeat the tawaf; for major impurity, one must slaughter a camel (badanah) and repeat. The evidence is from the hadith of Aisha (ra) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed her not to perform tawaf while menstruating, indicating that purity is a condition. The author also addresses the Shafi'i view that purity is a prerequisite for the validity of tawaf, arguing that this would require abrogating the Quranic command (Surah al-Hajj 29) with a solitary hadith, which is impermissible according to Hanafi usul. Instead, purity is considered an obligatory (wajib) element, the omission of which requires compensation but does not invalidate the tawaf. The passage further discusses the details of repetition: if one repeats during the Days of Nahr, no further penalty is needed; otherwise, a penalty for delay may be due according to Abu Hanifa. The author also notes that tawaf with impurity on the garment (less than a dirham) does not require a penalty but is disliked, and tawaf with uncovered awrah requires a blood penalty.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that nullifies wudu; requires a sheep if tawaf performed in this state.
جنابة (janaba): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl; tawaf in this state requires a camel and repetition.
طواف الركن (tawaf al-rukun): The essential tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah) that is one of the pillars of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the penalty for performing the essential tawaf while in a state of janaba (major impurity)?
A) A sheep and repetition.
B) A camel and repetition.
C) Only a sheep, no repetition.
D) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated without penalty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tawaf while impure is valid but requires compensation: a sheep for hadath, a camel for janaba; repetition is wajib for janaba and mustahabb for hadath.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling for Tawaf al-Rukn in Hadath and Janabah
States ruling, proof, and refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing tawaf al-rukn while in a state of minor or major impurity and explain why taharah is not a condition according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Tawaf in impurity is valid but deficient — compensation is wajib, but taharah is not a condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common question: if a pilgrim performs the obligatory tawaf al-rukn while in a state of minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (janabah), what is the ruling? The Hanafi school holds that the tawaf remains valid, but the pilgrim must compensate with sadaqah (for hadath) or a camel (for janabah) and should repeat the tawaf. This ruling contrasts with the Shafi'i view that taharah is a condition. The passage provides the Quranic and usul proof for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tawaf al-rukn performed while in a state of hadath (minor impurity) or janabah (major impurity). The ruling is that the tawaf remains valid, but compensation is required: sadaqah for hadath, a camel (badanah) for janabah, and repetition is recommended.
Tawaf al-rukn is a fard act of Hajj; the compensation is wajib.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The proof is the Quranic command 'wal yattawwafu' (Quran 22:29), which is an absolute (mutlaq) command. The Hanafi usul holds that an absolute command cannot be restricted (takhsis) by a solitary report (khabar wahid) because that would constitute naskh (abrogation), which is impermissible.
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith 'tawaf is prayer' to require taharah, but Hanafis interpret it as resemblance in reward only.
3
Refute the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers taharah a condition for tawaf. The Hanafi response is that this would require restricting the definitive Quranic text with a solitary report, which is not allowed. The hadith 'tawaf is prayer' is only about reward, not legal rulings.
The passage explicitly refutes the Shafi'i position.
4
Note the exception for garment impurity
If the impurity is on the garment (exceeding a dirham) and not on the body, no compensation is required, though it is disliked (makruh). The reasoning extends to the body as well, but the transmitted text only mentions the garment.
Claims in al-Zahiriyyah that require blood for garment impurity are baseless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طاف للركن محدثاً . وبدنة لو جنباً ويعيد وصدقة لو محدثاً للقدوم والصدر أو ترك أقل وإنما لم يكن شرطاً كما قال الشافعي لأنه يلزمه تقييد مطلق القطعي وهو وليطوفوا [ الحج : : ٢٩] بخبر الواحد وهو نسخ عندنا فلا يجوز كما عرف في الأصول. وأما قوله عليه السلام الطواف بالبيت صلاة (١) فالمراد به التشبيه في الثواب . قيد بالحدث لأنه لو طاف وعلى ثوبه نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم فإنه لا يلزمه شيء لكنه يكره لإدخال النجاسة المسجد، ولم ينص في ظاهر الرواية إلا على الثوب والتعليل يفيد عدم الفرق بين الثوب والبدن. وما في الظهيرية من أن نجاسة الثوب كله فيه الدم لا أصل له في الرواية فلا يعول عليه.
He performed tawaf for the Corner (rukn) while in a state of minor impurity. And a camel if he was in major impurity, and he repeats, and charity if he was in minor impurity for the arrival and departure tawaf or he omitted the minimum. And it is not a condition as al-Shafi'i said because it would require restricting an absolute definitive [text] which is 'and let them circumambulate' (Quran 22:29) with a solitary report, and that is abrogation in our view, so it is not permissible as known in usul. As for his statement (peace be upon him): 'Circumambulation of the House is prayer,' what is meant is resemblance in reward. It is restricted to hadath because if he circumambulated while his garment had impurity more than a dirham's worth, nothing is incumbent upon him, but it is disliked because of bringing impurity into the mosque. And in the apparent riwayah only the garment is mentioned, but the reasoning indicates no difference between garment and body. And what is in al-Zahiriyyah that impurity on the entire garment requires blood has no basis in transmission, so it is not relied upon.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a sharh expounding the ruling of tawaf under impurity. The author first states the core ruling: one who performs tawaf al-rukn while in minor impurity (hadath asghar) must give sadaqah (charity) for tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-sadr if he omitted the minimum, and must repeat. For major impurity (janabah), he must sacrifice a camel (badanah) and repeat. The author then refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's view that taharah is a condition for tawaf, arguing that accepting a solitary report to restrict an absolute definitive Quranic command would constitute naskh (abrogation), which is not permitted by our usul. He then clarifies the hadith 'tawaf is prayer' means only in reward, not in legal rulings. Finally, he addresses impurity on the garment: if the impurity exceeds a dirham, no blood sacrifice is required, only karahah; the apparent riwayah only mentions the garment, but by reasoning (ta'lil) it extends to the body. Claims from al-Zahiriyyah requiring blood for full garment impurity are baseless.

Key Terms
محدثاً (muhdithan): In a state of minor impurity (hadath asghar) requiring wudu
بدنة (badanah): A camel sacrificed as expiation
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity given as expiation; in this context, the minimum is sadaqat al-fitr

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A sheep (shah)
B) A camel (badanah)
C) Charity (sadaqah) for each shawt
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-rukn performed in any state of impurity remains valid in the Hanafi school, but compensation (sadaqah or badanah) and repetition are wajib.

Covering Awrah in Tawaf: Wajib, Not Shart
Explains the ruling on covering awrah in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that covering the awrah in tawaf is wajib and explain the consequence of its omission, citing the hadith and the Hanafi usul principle that a solitary report indicates obligation.

Core Idea
Covering awrah in tawaf is wajib; omission requires a blood sacrifice (dam).

This lesson examines a specific ruling for tawaf: covering the awrah. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that covering is a wajib, not a shart, meaning tawaf remains valid without it but a dam is owed. The proof is a hadith, interpreted via Hanafi usul as indicating obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the missing element
What is the person doing? Performing tawaf with awrah exposed. What element is missing? Covering the awrah.
The text specifies exposure 'to an extent that prayer is not valid with it' – for men, more than a quarter of a limb.
2
State the ruling and its basis
A blood sacrifice (dam) is required. The basis is that covering the awrah is a wajib, and abandoning a wajib in hajj requires a dam.
This is explicit: 'yalzamuhu dam'.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'La yatufanna bi'l-bayti 'uryan' (No one shall circumambulate the House naked). This is a solitary report (khabar wahid).
The hadith is cited as the proof for wujub.
4
Understand the usul connection
In Hanafi usul, a solitary report from the Prophet (ﷺ) indicates wujub (obligation) when it commands or prohibits. The prohibition here implies that covering is obligatory.
Other schools may interpret this differently; the passage notes 'at our school'.
5
Distinguish shart vs wajib
Covering awrah is not a condition (shart) for tawaf; it is a wajib. Thus, tawaf performed without it is still valid (sahih) but incurs a compensatory dam.
This nuance is key: if it were a shart, tawaf would be invalid and require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى أنه لو طاف منكشف العورة قدر ما لا تجوز الصلاة معه فإنه يلزمه دم لترك الواجب وهو ستر العورة كما صرح به في الظهيرية، ودليل الوجوب قوله عليه السلام إلا لا يحج بعد العام مشرك ولا يطوف بالبيت عريان (٢) بناء على أن خبر الواحد يفيد الوجوب عندنا.
And he indicated that if he circumambulated while his ‘awrah was uncovered to an extent that prayer is not valid with it, then a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory for him due to abandoning the wajib, which is covering the ‘awrah, as stated in al-Zahiriyyah. And the proof of obligation is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Indeed, no polytheist shall perform Hajj after this year, and no one shall circumambulate the House naked,' based on the fact that a solitary report indicates obligation in our view.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from the sharh addresses the ruling for one who performs tawaf with ‘awrah exposed to the extent that would invalidate prayer (i.e., more than a quarter of the limb for men, the whole body for women). The author explains that this omission of a wajib (covering ‘awrah) necessitates a blood sacrifice (dam). The proof is the hadith prohibiting circumambulation naked, which is a solitary report (khabar wahid) that, in the Hanafi school, indicates obligation (wujub). The ruling is consistent with the principle that covering ‘awrah is wajib in tawaf, and not doing so requires compensation.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and tawaf (for men: navel to knee; for women: whole body except face and hands)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
B) A blood sacrifice (dam) is required
C) Nothing, it is permissible
D) They must repeat only the rounds where awrah was exposed

Key Takeaway
Covering awrah in tawaf is a wajib, not a shart; omission requires a dam, not a repetition of tawaf.

Obligation of I'adah and Expiation for Tawaf in Janabah
Ruling with proof on i'adah after impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'adah (repetition) for tawaf in janabah vs hadath, identify the expiation required, and apply the timing condition regarding the days of sacrifice.

Core Idea
Repetition of tawaf is wajib for janabah, mustahabb for hadath; blood sacrifice is due if delay occurs after the days of sacrifice.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position on what to do if one performs tawaf while in a state of major or minor impurity. The core ruling distinguishes between janabah and hadath, and the expiation varies accordingly. We will also see how timing matters: repeating within the days of sacrifice has different consequences than repeating after them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of impurity
The text distinguishes between hadath (minor impurity) and janabah (major impurity). Determine which type occurred, as the ruling on i'adah and expiation differs.
Janabah includes post-coital impurity and, according to the text, menstruation and post-natal bleeding.
2
Determine the hukm of i'adah
According to al-Hidayah, i'adah is wajib for janabah and mustahabb for hadath. Understand the rationale: janabah is a more severe violation, so compensation is obligatory.
If the tawaf was the rukn (obligatory) tawaf, the rule applies; if it was a lesser tawaf (e.g., for umra), a sheep is due instead of a camel.
3
Check the timing of i'adah
If the repetition is done within the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr), no other compensation is needed. If it is done after those days, Abu Hanifa rules that a blood sacrifice (dam) is required for the delay.
This is a point of ikhtilaf within the school; some later scholars hold that no blood is needed for delay in the case of hadath, only for janabah.
4
Identify the expiation for non-repetition
If one does not repeat the tawaf performed in janabah, the expiation is a camel (badanah) for the rukn tawaf, or a sheep for a lesser tawaf. For hadath, if not repeated, no expiation is mentioned but repeating is recommended.
The text also mentions a minority view that if one repeats after the days, charity (sadaqah) per shawt is due.
5
Apply the preferred view (mufta bihi)
The preferred view in later Hanafi practice is that repetition is wajib for janabah and mustahabb for hadath; delay after the days of sacrifice requires a blood sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa, but some scholars like those in al-Hidayah hold that i'adah itself is sufficient and no extra blood is needed.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq sides with al-Karkhi's view that the first tawaf remains valid, which affects whether the delay is counted.

And if he returns for the first, he returns with a new ihram based on the fact that he became permitted with regard to women by the visitation tawaf in janabah, and he is an afaqi wanting Mecca, so he must assume ihram for Hajj or Umra. If he assumes ihram for Umra, he begins with it; when he completes it, he performs tawaf for visitation, and a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory for delaying the visitation tawaf from its time. Al-Razi understood from this that the second tawaf is valid and that the first has been dissolved. Al-Karkhi held that the first is considered in the chapter of violation just as in the chapter of hadath by agreement; the author of al-Idah affirmed this since there is no doubt that the first occurred validly such that women became permissible by it. Commentary
This passage is a critical discourse on the nature of repetition (i'adah) when one performs tawaf in a state of impurity. The author explains that the base text's 'wa ya'id' (and he repeats) implies an alternative: either the blood sacrifice or the repetition. The repetition is recommended for minor impurity and obligatory for major impurity according to al-Hidayah. If one repeats within the days of sacrifice, no further compensation is needed. However, if one repeats after the days of sacrifice, Abu Hanifa rules that a blood sacrifice is required for the delay. The passage then delves into a famous ikhtilaf between al-Razi and al-Karkhi: al-Razi held that the second tawaf (the repetition) completely replaces the first, while al-Karkhi argued that the first tawaf remains valid and the repetition is merely a supplement. The author sides with al-Karkhi, noting that the first tawaf has already permitted intercourse with women, so it cannot be invalidated. Supporting arguments from al-Idah and others are cited. The discussion concludes with a note about a different opinion requiring charity per shawt.

Key Terms
إعادة (i‘adah): Repeating the tawaf after having performed it in a state of impurity
شاة (shah): A sheep as expiation for tawaf in janabah if not repeated
بدنة (badanah): A camel as expiation for tawaf al-rukn in janabah if not repeated

Repetition of tawaf is required for janabah (wajib) and recommended for hadath; if delayed after the days of sacrifice, a blood sacrifice is due according to the strongest Hanafi view.

Ikhtilaf al-Razi and al-Karkhi on the Validity of the First Tawaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of i'adah on original tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the internal Hanafi dispute between al-Razi and al-Karkhi regarding which tawaf is considered valid after i'adah, and evaluate the preferred view with supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Al-Karkhi: first tawaf remains valid; al-Razi: second tawaf replaces it — a key dispute affecting expiation.

This lesson delves into a subtle but consequential ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school. When a person repeats tawaf performed in janabah, does the original tawaf become invalid, or does it remain valid and the repetition is merely a supplement? Al-Razi and al-Karkhi took opposing positions, and the preferred view has significant implications for what expiation is due and whether a new ihram is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in dispute
The ikhtilaf centers on whether the first tawaf performed in janabah, when repeated (i'adah), is still considered valid or is dissolved and replaced by the second tawaf.
This affects whether the repetition is compensatory or substitutive.
2
State al-Razi's position and his evidence
Al-Razi held that the second tawaf is the valid one and the first is dissolved. His evidence: when a person returns to perform the repetition, they must assume a new ihram, which indicates that the first tawaf's effect (tahlil) is undone and a fresh start is needed.
The new ihram is required because the person had become halal (permitted for women) after the first tawaf, but to return to Mecca for tawaf, a new ihram is necessary.
3
State al-Karkhi's position and his evidence
Al-Karkhi held that the first tawaf remains valid and is considered in the chapter of violation (janabah). His evidence: the first tawaf already permitted intercourse with women (halla bi al-nisa'), which is a strong indication of its validity. It cannot be invalidated retroactively.
He also argues that the need for a new ihram is because of the journey to Mecca, not because the first tawaf is invalid.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq prefers al-Karkhi's view, citing al-Idah and the argument that there is no doubt the first tawaf occurred validly. The practical implication is that the repetition is complementary, and no extra expiation beyond what is required for the delay is needed.
If al-Razi's view were taken, the repetition would be the main tawaf, and the delay would be counted from the original tawaf, potentially requiring additional blood.
5
Apply the preferred view to a scenario
Consider a pilgrim who performed tawaf in janabah and repeated it after the days of sacrifice. According to al-Karkhi, the first tawaf is valid, so the delay is measured from the first tawaf to the repetition. The repetition itself compensates the deficiency, but the delay triggers a blood sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa. If al-Razi's view were followed, the second tawaf would be the valid one, so the delay would be measured from the repetition to… actually, the delay would be from the original time to the second, but the original is void, so the pilgrim would need to perform tawaf as if for the first time, and any delay after the days would require blood.
In practice, the preferred view (al-Karkhi) simplifies the ruling: the first tawaf is valid, so only the delay requires blood if applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبدنة لو جنباً ويعيد أي يجب بدنة لو طاف للركن جنباً. كذا روي عن ابن عباس. ولأن الجناية أغلظ فيجب جبر نقصانها في البدنة إظهاراً للتفاوت بينهما والحيض والنفاس كالجنابة قيد بالركن وهو الأكثر لأنه لو طاف الأقل جنباً ولم يعد وجب عليه شاة، فإن أعاده وجبت عليه صدقة لتأخير الأقل من طواف الزيارة لكل شوط نصف صاع. وقوله ويعيد» راجع إلى الطواف محدثاً أو جنباً، ولم يذكر صفة الإعادة للاختلاف، وصحح في الهداية أنها واجبة في الطواف جنباً مستحبة في الطواف محدثاً للفحش في الأول والقصور في الثاني، فإن أعاده فلا عليه فيهما مطلقاً لجبر النقصان الحاصل بالإعادة إلا أنه إن أعاده وقد طاف جنباً بعد أيام النحر لزمه دم للتأخير عند أبي حنيفة. وبهذا علم أن الواو في قوله بمعنى «أو» لأن الواجب بمعنى شيئين إما لزوم الشاة أو الإعادة والإعادة هي الأصل ما دام بمكة ليكون الجابر من جنس المجبور فهي أفضل من الدم، وأما إذا رجع إلى أهله ففي الحدث الأصغر اتفقوا أن بعث الشاة أفضل من الرجوع واختلفوا في الحدث الأكبر فاختار في الهداية أن العود إلى الإعادة أفضل لماذكرنا ، واختار في المحيط أن بعث الدم أفضل لأن الطواف الأول معتداً . وقع به وفيه منفعة للفقراء، وإذا عاد للأول يرجع بإحرام جديد بناء على أنه حل في حق النساء بطواف الزيارة جنباً وهو آفاقي يريد مكة فلا بد له من إحرام بحج أو عمرة، فإذا أحرم بعمرة يبدأ بها، فإذا فرغ منها يطوف للزيارة ويلزمه دم لتأخير طواف الزيارة عن وقته وفهم الرازي من ذلك أن الطواف الثاني معتد به وأن الأول قد انفسخ، وذهب الكرخي إلى أن الأول معتبر في فصل الجناية كما في فصل الحدث اتفاقاً، وصححه صاحب الإيضاح إذ لا شك في وقع الأول معتداً به حتى حل به النساء، واستدل له بما في لم يعده كما سيشرحه المؤلف قوله وقد طاف جنباً جملة حالية معترضة بين الظرف ومتعلقة فإن قوله بعد أيام النحر» متعلق بإعاده، وقيد بذلك لأنه لو كان طاف محدثاً وأعاده سقط عنه الدم، سواء أعاده في أيام النحر أو بعدها ولا شيء عليه للتأخير كما في اللباب وعزاه شارحه إلى الهداية والكافي وغيرهما . قال : وفي البحر الزاخر هو الصحيح ثم قال في اللباب : وقيل يجب عليه للتأخير دم . قال شارحه قال قوام الدين ما في الهداية سهو لأن تأخير النسك عن وقته يوجب الدم عند أبي حنيفة على أن الرواية مصرحة بخلاف ذلك، ولذا قال في شرح الطحاوي : إذا أعاد طواف الزيارة بعد أيام النحر يجب عليه الدم، سواء كانت إعادته بسبب الحدث أو الجنابة. وبه جزم في البدائع وصحح في السراج ما في الهداية قال في المطلب : إنه الأظهر ا.هـ. ووجهه أن طوافه الأول معتد به بلا خلاف والإعادة لتكميل العبادة وتمامه فيه. ثم قال في اللباب وقيل صدقة لكل شوط وعزاه شارحه إلى الخلاصة وشرح الجامع لقاضيخان وسيذكر المؤلف ذلك بعد ورقتين
His statement: 'And a camel if in major impurity and he repeats' i.e., a camel is obligatory if he performed tawaf al-rukn in janabah. Thus it is narrated from Ibn Abbas. And because the violation is more severe, it is obligatory to compensate its deficiency with a camel, showing the difference between the two. Menstruation and post-natal bleeding are like janabah. It is restricted to the corner (rukn) because it is the majority; if he performed the lesser tawaf (the minimum) in janabah and did not repeat, a sheep becomes obligatory; if he repeats, charity becomes obligatory due to delaying the lesser of the visitation tawaf: for each shawt, half a sa' of wheat. His statement 'and he repeats' refers to tawaf in minor or major impurity, and he did not mention the description of repetition due to difference of opinion. In al-Hidayah it is affirmed that it is obligatory for tawaf in janabah and recommended for tawaf in minor impurity because of the severity in the former and the deficiency in the latter. If he repeats, then nothing is upon him in either case absolutely due to the compensation of deficiency achieved by repetition, except that if he repeats after having performed tawaf in janabah after the days of sacrifice, a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory due to delay according to Abu Hanifa. By this it is known that the waw in his statement means 'or' because the obligatory is one of two things: either the obligation of the sheep or the repetition; and repetition is the original as long as he is in Mecca so that the compensator is of the same type as the compensated, so it is better than blood. As for when he returns to his family, regarding minor impurity they all agreed that sending a sheep is better than returning; regarding major impurity they differed: in al-Hidayah he chose that returning for repetition is better for the reason we mentioned; in al-Muhit he chose that sending blood is better because the first tawaf is valid; it occurred and there is benefit for the poor. And if he returns for the first, he returns with a new ihram based on the fact that he became permitted with regard to women by the visitation tawaf in janabah, and he is an afaqi wanting Mecca, so he must assume ihram for Hajj or Umra. If he assumes ihram for Umra, he begins with it; when he completes it, he performs tawaf for visitation, and a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory for delaying the visitation tawaf from its time. Al-Razi understood from this that the second tawaf is valid and that the first has been dissolved. Al-Karkhi held that the first is considered in the chapter of violation just as in the chapter of hadath by agreement; the author of al-Idah affirmed this since there is no doubt that the first occurred validly such that women became permissible by it. And he adduced evidence...
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a critical discourse on the nature of repetition (i'adah) when one performs tawaf in a state of impurity. The author explains that the base text's 'wa ya'id' (and he repeats) implies an alternative: either the blood sacrifice or the repetition. The repetition is recommended for minor impurity and obligatory for major impurity according to al-Hidayah. If one repeats within the days of sacrifice, no further compensation is needed. However, if one repeats after the days of sacrifice, Abu Hanifa rules that a blood sacrifice is required for the delay. The passage then delves into a famous ikhtilaf between al-Razi and al-Karkhi: al-Razi held that the second tawaf (the repetition) completely replaces the first, while al-Karkhi argued that the first tawaf remains valid and the repetition is merely a supplement. The author sides with al-Karkhi, noting that the first tawaf has already permitted intercourse with women, so it cannot be invalidated. Supporting arguments from al-Idah and others are cited. The discussion concludes with a note about a different opinion requiring charity per shawt.

Key Terms
إعادة (i‘adah): Repeating the tawaf after having performed it in a state of impurity
انفسخ (infasakha): Dissolved, voided; al-Razi's term for the status of the first tawaf
معتد به (mu‘tad bihi): Considered valid; al-Karkhi's term that the first tawaf is counted

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Bahr al-Raiq, what is the status of the first tawaf after repetition in janabah?
A) It is dissolved and invalid
B) It remains valid and the repetition is complementary
C) It is partially valid but requires additional expiation
D) It is valid only if repeated within the days of sacrifice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided on whether the first tawaf is valid after i'adah; the preferred view (al-Karkhi) holds it remains valid, simplifying expiation rules.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah While Junub After the Days of Nahr
Ruling on compensation for tawaf al-ziyarah performed in janabah after its time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two alternative obligations for a pilgrim who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub after the Days of Nahr and explain the Hanafi reasoning for preferring repetition versus sending blood.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub after its time incurs either a dam or repetition; the waw means 'or'.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common question in Hajj: what happens if a pilgrim performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) and after the designated days of Nahr? Abu Hanifa clarifies that two obligations arise: either a sacrificial sheep (dam) or a repetition of the tawaf. The text also explores which option is preferable depending on whether the pilgrim is still in Makkah or has returned home, and highlights a difference between the authors of al-Hidayah and al-Muhit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling according to Abu Hanifa
The act is performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub after the Days of Nahr. According to Abu Hanifa, this obligates either a dam (sheep) or a repetition (i'ada) of the tawaf. Note that the waw in the phrase 'لزمه دم للتأخير' actually means 'or', indicating two alternatives.
The ruling is from Abu Hanifa; the text does not specify fard or wajib but uses 'lazim' (obligatory).
2
Understand the preference while still in Makkah
As long as the pilgrim remains in Makkah, repetition (i'ada) is considered the original and better option. This is because the compensator (the repetition) is of the same genus as the compensated (the tawaf), thus restoring the act fully.
The principle: 'al-jabir min jins al-majbur' (the compensator should be of the same type as the deficiency).
3
Analyze the situation when the pilgrim has returned home
For minor impurity (hadath asghar), there is consensus that sending a sheep is better than returning. For major impurity (janabah), there is a difference: al-Hidayah holds that returning for repetition is better, while al-Muhit holds that sending the blood is better because the first tawaf is considered valid and the blood benefits the poor.
The difference hinges on whether the first tawaf is considered valid (sahih) despite the janabah. If valid, repetition is not needed; if invalid, repetition is required.
4
Consider the procedure if the pilgrim returns for repetition
If the pilgrim chooses to return, he must do so with a new ihram because his previous ihram was invalidated by the first tawaf (which made him halal for women). He must enter Makkah with a new ihram for Hajj or Umrah, and then perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah anew. Additionally, a dam becomes obligatory for the delay (ta'khir) of the tawaf beyond its time.
The dam for delay is in addition to any other obligations; it is not a substitute for the repetition.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) and that performing it in a state of janabah invalidates the tawaf entirely, requiring repetition without the option of dam. The Hanafi position, as stated, provides alternatives.
This ikhtilaf affects the practical ruling for a Shafi'i pilgrim: they must repeat the tawaf regardless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعيد) طاف جنباً بعد أيام النحر لزمه دم للتأخير عند أبي حنيفة. وبهذا علم أن الواو في قوله بمعنى «أو» لأن الواجب بمعنى شيئين إما لزوم الشاة أو الإعادة والإعادة هي الأصل ما دام بمكة ليكون الجابر من جنس المجبور فهي أفضل من الدم، وأما إذا رجع إلى أهله ففي الحدث الأصغر اتفقوا أن بعث الشاة أفضل من الرجوع واختلفوا في الحدث الأكبر فاختار في الهداية أن العود إلى الإعادة أفضل لماذكرنا ، واختار في المحيط أن بعث الدم أفضل لأن الطواف الأول معتداً . وقع به وفيه منفعة للفقراء، وإذا عاد للأول يرجع بإحرام جديد بناء على أنه حل في حق النساء بطواف الزيارة جنباً وهو آفاقي يريد مكة فلا بد له من إحرام بحج أو عمرة، فإذا أحرم بعمرة يبدأ بها، فإذا فرغ منها يطوف للزيارة ويلزمه دم لتأخير طواف الزيارة عن وقته
He repeats. One who performed tawaf while junub after the Days of Nahr is obligated a blood (sheep) for delay according to Abu Hanifa. By this it is known that the waw in his statement means 'or', because the obligatory is two things: either the obligation of a sheep or repetition. Repetition is the original as long as he is in Makkah so that the compensator is of the same genus as the compensated; thus it is better than blood. As for when he returns to his family, regarding minor impurity they agreed that sending a sheep is better than returning. They differed regarding major impurity: al-Hidayah chose that returning for repetition is better for what we mentioned; al-Muhit chose that sending blood is better because the first tawaf is valid, done as such, and it benefits the poor. If he returns for the first, he returns with a new ihram based on that he had become halal in terms of women due to Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, and he is an afaqi intending Makkah, so he must make an ihram for Hajj or Umrah. If he enters ihram for Umrah, he begins with it. When he finishes it, he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and a blood (sheep) becomes obligatory for delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah from its time.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Abu Hanifa regarding Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) after the Days of Nahr. The text explains that the waw in the phrase 'طاف جنباً بعد أيام النحر لزمه دم للتأخير' actually means 'or', indicating two alternative obligations: either sacrificing a sheep (dam) or repeating the tawaf. Repetition is considered the original and better option while still in Makkah because the compensating act (i'ada) matches the nature of the deficient act (tawaf). When the pilgrim has returned home, there is consensus that for minor impurity (hadath asghar), sending a sheep is better than returning. For major impurity (janabah), there is disagreement: al-Hidayah favors returning for repetition, while al-Muhit favors sending a sheep on the grounds that the first tawaf was valid and benefits the poor. If the pilgrim returns, he must do so with a new ihram because he had become halal regarding women due to the first tawaf, even though it was invalid due to janabah. He then performs Umrah first, then Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and incurs an additional blood (dam) for delaying the tawaf.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed after standing at Arafah during Hajj, also called tawaf al-ifadah.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of the tawaf after having performed it in an invalid state.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep) offered as expiation for a deficiency in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is correct regarding Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed while junub after the Days of Nahr?
A) The only obligation is a sheep (dam).
B) The pilgrim must return to Makkah to repeat the tawaf.
C) The pilgrim may either sacrifice a sheep or repeat the tawaf.
D) The pilgrim must fast three days as expiation.

Key Takeaway
A pilgrim who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub after the Days of Nahr has two alternative obligations: a sheep or repetition; preference depends on location and scholarly interpretation.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does the Second Tawaf Replace the First?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of the first tawaf when repeated by a junub.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two positions within the Hanafi school regarding the repeated tawaf for a junub and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The khilaf between al-Razi and al-Karkhi on the repeated tawaf is lafzi—both agree blood is wajib, so no practical difference.

Al-Marghinani presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person who performs tawaf while in a state of major impurity must repeat it, and if so, whether the second tawaf nullifies the first. Two prominent Hanafi scholars, Fakhr al-Islam al-Razi and Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, offer different analyses, yet the text concludes the disagreement is purely verbal. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish real from apparent ikhtilaf within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify which scholar holds that the first tawaf is rescinded (munfasikh) and which holds it remains valid (mu'tad bihi).
Al-Razi: second tawaf replaces the first. Al-Karkhi: first remains valid; second is compensatory.
2
Identify the proof for al-Karkhi's view
Analyze the case from al-Asl: a person performing Umrah tawaf while impure in Ramadan who performs Hajj that year is not a mutamatti' even if he repeats the tawaf in Shawwal.
This shows the first tawaf is valid for tahallul, so it is considered legally effective.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence. The text states blood is wajib by agreement, so the khilaf is lafzi.
A theoretical difference about sa'y may exist, but the main outcome is the same obligation of blood.
4
Determine the tarjih
Identify which view the text prefers. The author of al-I'dah corrects al-Karkhi's view, and Fath al-Qadir strengthens it.
The mufta bihi is al-Karkhi's position that the first tawaf is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفهم الرازي من ذلك أن الطواف الثاني معتد به وأن الأول قد انفسخ، وذهب الكرخي إلى أن الأول معتبر في فصل الجناية كما في فصل الحدث اتفاقاً، وصححه صاحب الإيضاح إذ لا شك في وقع الأول معتداً به حتى حل به النساء، واستدل له بما في الأصل: لو طاف لعمرته محدثاً أو جنباً في رمضان وحج من عامه لم يكن متمتعاً إن أعاده في شوال أو لم يعده، وقواه في فتح القدير. وإنما وجب الدم لترك الواجب لأن الواجب الإعادة في أيام النحر فإذا مضت ترك واجباً، والظاهر أن الخلف لفظي لا ثمرة له لأن الدم واجب اتفاقاً وإن اختلف التخريج
Al-Razi understood from this that the second tawaf is valid and the first has been rescinded. Al-Karkhi held that the first is considered valid in the chapter of violations, as in the chapter of minor impurity by agreement. The author of al-I'dah corrected this, since there is no doubt that the first occurred validly such that women became permissible through it. He argued with what is in al-Asl: if one performed tawaf for his Umrah while in minor or major impurity in Ramadan and performed Hajj that same year, he would not be a mutamatti' whether he repeated it in Shawwal or not. This was strengthened in Fath al-Qadir. The blood (dam) is only obligatory for leaving an obligation, because the obligation is repetition during the Days of Nahr; when they pass, he has left an obligation. Apparently the disagreement is verbal, with no practical consequence, because blood is obligatory by agreement even if the analytical reasoning differs.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between two scholars, Fakhr al-Islam al-Razi and Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, concerning the status of a repeated tawaf. Al-Razi, citing the wording of the earlier text, argues that when a junub repeats his tawaf, the second tawaf is the valid one and the first is rescinded (munfasikh). Al-Karkhi, supported by the author of al-I'dah, counters that the first tawaf remains valid; the second is merely a compensatory act (jabir) to make up for the deficiency of impurity. The evidence from al-Asl (a foundational text) shows that a person who performs Umrah tawaf while impure and later performs Hajj that same year is not considered a mutamatti' (performing Umrah first and then Hajj) even if he repeats the tawaf in Shawwal, implying the first tawaf is considered for the purpose of determining the type of Hajj. This strengthens al-Karkhi's view. However, the text concludes that the dispute is lafzi (verbal) because in both cases a blood sacrifice is obligatory anyway, so there is no practical difference.

Key Terms
انفسخ (infasakha): The first tawaf is rescinded or nullified and becomes void.
معتد به (mu'tad bihi): Considered valid and legally effective; the opposite of munfasikh.
خلف لفظي (khulf lafzi): A disagreement that is merely verbal without real practical consequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence of the dispute between al-Razi and al-Karkhi?
A) Obligation of blood differs.
B) Whether sa'y must be repeated after the second tawaf.
C) Whether the pilgrim becomes halal for women.
D) There is no practical consequence; both agree blood is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between al-Razi and al-Karkhi is lafzi; the relied-upon view holds the first tawaf valid, and blood is wajib in both views.

Compensation for Sunnah and Wajib Tawafs in Impurity
Details the compensation for sunnah and wajib tawafs performed in impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required compensation for Tawaf al-Qudum (sunnah) and Tawaf al-Sadr (wajib) when performed in minor or major impurity, and explain the underlying rationale and intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Sunnah and wajib tawafs without purification require charity for minor impurity, repetition and blood for major.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi rulings on Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf, sunnah) and Tawaf al-Sadr (the farewell tawaf, wajib) when performed without proper purification. It details the graduated compensation depending on the severity of impurity and the rank of the tawaf, addressing both internal Hanafi differences and the refutation of a minority view claiming no compensation is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tawaf and its category
Determine whether the tawaf is sunnah (Tawaf al-Qudum) or wajib (Tawaf al-Sadr). The ruling for both is identical despite different original categories.
Both are lower in rank than Tawaf al-Ziyarah (fard).
2
Classify the impurity type
Distinguish between minor impurity (hadath, e.g., without wudu) and major impurity (janabah). The compensation differs.
The text emphasizes this qayd (restriction).
3
Apply the compensation for minor impurity
For hadath in a sunnah/wajib tawaf, the compensation is a charity (sadaqah). The deficiency is slight.
Sadaqah is less than a blood sacrifice.
4
Apply the compensation for major impurity
For janabah, repetition (i'ada) is obligatory; if not repeated, a blood sacrifice (dam) is due. The deficiency is aggravated.
Repetition is precautionary.
5
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Imam Muhammad holds that for Tawaf al-Tahiyya (sunnah), i'ada is not obligatory but better. Al-Asbijabi's view of no compensation is rejected as false.
The relied-upon position is compensation as described.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول : ( وصدقة لو محدثاً للقدوم) أي يجب عليه صدقة لو طاف للقدوم . محدثاً لأنه دخله نقص بترك الطهارة فينجبر بالصدقة إظهاراً لدنو رتبته عن الواجب بإيجاب الله تعالى وهو طواف الزيارة، وأشار إلى أن كل طواف هو تطوع فهو كذلك. وقيد بالحدث لأنه لو طاف للقدوم جنباً لزمه الإعادة ودم إن لم يعد لأن النقص فيه متغلظ فتلزمه الإعادة احتياطاً. وقال محمد : ليس عليه أن يعيد طواف التحية لأنه سنة وإن أعاد فهو أفضل. كذا في المحيط وبهذا ظهر بطلان ما في غاية البيان معزياً إلى الأسبيجابي من أنه لا شيء عليه لو طاف للقاء محدثاً أو جنباً لأنه يقتضي عدم وجوب الطهارة للطواف ولأن طواف التطوع إذا شرع فيه صار واجباً بالشروع ثم يدخله النقص بترك الطهارة فيه، غاية الأمر أن وجوبه ليس بإيجابه تعالى ابتداء فأظهرنا التفاوت في الحط من الدم إلى الصدقة فيما إذا طافه محدثاً، ومن البدنة إلى الشاة فيما إذا طافه جنباً. وظاهر كلامهم يقتضي وجوب الشاة فيما إذا طاف للتطوع جنباً، وذكر في غاية البيان أنه إن طاف للقدوم محدثاً ورمل عقبه فهو جائز والأفضل أن يعيدهما عقيب طواف الزيارة، وإن طاف له جنباً ورمل عقبه فإنه لا يعتد به ويجب عليه السعي عقب طواف الزيارة ويرمل فيه . قوله : (والصدر) بالجر عطف على القدوم فتجب صدقة لو طاف محدثاً، ودم لو جنباً، فقد سووا بين طواف القدوم وبين طواف الصدر مع أن الأول سنة والثانية واجب. وأجاب عنه في الهداية بأن طواف الصدر دون طواف الزيارة وإن كان واجباً فلا بد من إظهار التفاوت
His saying: 'And a charity if he performed tawaf while in minor impurity for al-Qudum' meaning he owes a charity if he performed tawaf for al-Qudum while in minor impurity, because it has been affected by deficiency by omitting purification; so it is compensated by charity, showing its rank is lower than the wajib by Allah's obligation, which is Tawaf al-Ziyarah. He indicated that every tawaf that is supererogatory is like this. He restricted it to minor impurity because if he performed tawaf for al-Qudum while junub, repetition and blood are obligatory if he does not repeat, because the deficiency is aggravated, so repetition is obligatory as a precaution. Muhammad said: He does not have to repeat the Tahiyya tawaf because it is sunnah, though repeating is better. Thus in al-Muhit. By this the falsehood of what is in Ghayat al-Bayan attributed to al-Asbijabi becomes apparent, namely that nothing is due upon him if he performs tawaf for meeting while in minor or major impurity, because it would entail that purification is not obligatory for tawaf, and because a supererogatory tawaf when started becomes obligatory by starting; then deficiency enters it by omitting purification. The only difference is that its obligation is not from Allah initially, so we show the variation from blood to charity when he performs it in minor impurity, and from badanah to sheep when he performs it in major impurity. The apparent meaning of their words necessitates the obligation of a sheep when he performs supererogatory tawaf while junub. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that if he performs tawaf for al-Qudum in minor impurity and then performs raml after it, it is permissible and better to repeat both after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If he performed it junub and performed raml after it, then it is not valid, and he must perform Sa'y after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and perform raml therein. His saying: 'and al-Sadr' is in the genitive, conjoined with al-Qudum. So a charity is obligatory if he performed it in minor impurity, and blood if in major impurity. They equated between Tawaf al-Qudum and Tawaf al-Sadr, even though the first is sunnah and the second is wajib. The answer to this is given in al-Hidayah that Tawaf al-Sadr is lower than Tawaf al-Ziyarah, even though it is wajib; thus it is necessary to show variation.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage details the compensation required for Tawaf al-Qudum (the tawaf performed when first entering Makkah, a sunnah) and Tawaf al-Sadr (the farewell tawaf, considered wajib in the Hanafi school) when performed in a state of impurity. For minor impurity (hadath asghar), a charity (sadaqah) is required because the deficiency is slight and the tawaf's rank is lower than the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah. For major impurity (janabah), repetition (i'ada) is required, and if not repeated, a blood (sheep) is due. Imam Muhammad adds that for the sunnah Tawaf al-Tahiyya, repetition is not obligatory but better. The text refutes the view of al-Asbijabi who claimed nothing is due, arguing that omitting purification causes deficiency in a tawaf that has become obligatory by initiation. The ruling for Tawaf al-Sadr is identical to that for Tawaf al-Qudum despite the latter being sunnah and the former wajib. Al-Hidayah explains this by noting that Tawaf al-Sadr, though wajib, is still of a lower rank than Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so a similar compensation applies.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The sunnah tawaf performed upon first arriving in Makkah for Hajj or Umrah.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah; considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable gift, here meaning a small amount of food or money given as compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required compensation for Tawaf al-Qudum performed while in minor impurity (hadath)?
A) A blood sacrifice (dam).
B) A charity (sadaqah).
C) Repetition of the tawaf plus a blood sacrifice.
D) Nothing, as it is a sunnah tawaf.

Key Takeaway
For sunnah and wajib tawafs, compensation is graduated: sadaqah for minor impurity, repetition and dam for major impurity.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Rulings on Omitting Circuits from Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Explains Hanafi rulings on omitting circuits from Tawaf al-Ziyarah and the principle of majority equivalence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting 1-3 vs 4+ circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the legal principle of 'al-akthar muqam al-kull' derived from the hadith of Arafah.

Core Idea
Leaving 1-3 circuits requires a dam; leaving 4+ invalidates tahallul, based on the principle that the majority stands for the whole.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine the rulings for partial omission of the obligatory tawaf (Tawaf al-Ziyarah). The author details the required penalties—dam for up to three circuits, remaining in ihram for four or more—and then grounds this in the broader Hanafi principle that in Hajj, the majority of an act can stand for the whole, citing the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete' and the consensus that shaving most of the head effects tahallul. We will also consider a critical objection from Fath al-Qadir and how the Hanafi school responds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Leaving one, two, or three circuits requires a dam (blood sacrifice). Leaving four circuits means the person remains in ihram (cannot have marital relations).
The ruling distinguishes between majority and minority omissions.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete' and the consensus that shaving most of the head effects tahallul. These establish the principle that majority can substitute for the whole.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Understand the qiyas
The Hanafis apply the principle to tawaf because tawaf is one of the two causes of tahallul (along with shaving). Qiyas extends the ruling from shaving to tawaf.
This qiyas is of the khafi type.
4
Analyze the critique
Fath al-Qadir objects that the principle only applies to the entire Hajj, not to its parts. The commentator acknowledges the criticism but maintains the ruling based on school practice.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the strength of the qiyas.

طواف الركن ولو ترك أكثره بقي محرماً أو ترك أكثر الصدر أو طافه حنباً وصدقة بترك السبعة يوجب عنه في الهداية بأن طواف القدوم يصير واجباً أيضاً بالشروع وأقره الشارحون وقد يقال: إن ما وجب ابتداء قبل الشروع أقوى مما وجب بالشروع فينبغي عدم المساواة. قيد بترك الطهارة للطواف لأن السعي محدثاً أو جنباً لا شيء، سواء كان عمرة أو حج، لأنه عبادة سعي تؤدى لا في المسجد الحرام والأصل أن كل عبادة تؤدى لا في المسجد في أحكام المناسك فالطهارة ليست بواجبة لها كالسعي والوقوف بعرفة والمزدلفة ورمي الجمار بخلاف الطواف فإنه عبادة تؤدى في المسجد فكانت الطهارة واجبة فيه كذا في الفتاوى الظهيرية. قوله : (أو ترك أقل طواف الركن
