الرأس صار متحللاً فلما كان الأمر على هذا الوجه للتيسير جرينا على هذا الأصل فأقمنا الأكثر مقام الكل في باب التحلل وما يجري مجراه صيانة لهذه العبادة عن الفوات وتحقيقاً للأمر يعني أن الطواف أحد التحلل فلما أقيم الأكثر مقام الكل في أحد السببين سببي الحلق بالإجماع أقيم في السبب الآخر وهو الطواف أيضاً. كذا في النهاية. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن إقامة الأكثر في تمام العبادة إنما هو في حق حكم خاص وهو أمن الفساد والفوات ليس غير ولذا لم يحكم بأن ترك ما بقي أعني الطواف يتم معه الحج وهو مورد ذلك النص فلا يلزم جواز إقامة أكثر كل جزء منه مقام تمام ذلك الجزء وترك باقيه كما لم يجز ذلك في نفس مورد النص أعني الحج فلا ينبغي التعويل على هذا الحكم والله أعلم، بل الذي ندين به أن لا يجزيء أقل من السبعة ولا يجبر بعضه بشيء غير أنا نستمر معهم في التقرير على التفاوت بينهما. قال : وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يجب شاة إلا أن الأول أصح ثم قال : وإن طاف جنباً فعليه شاة لأنه نقص كثير ثم هو دون طواف الزيارة فيكتفي بالشاة. نعم ما ذكره من الإشكال والجواب ذكره الزيلعي وأما ما ذكره المؤلف بقوله (وقد يقال الخ) فقد أجيب عنه كما في النهر بأن أحد المحظورين لازم أعني التسوية بينه وبين طواف الزيارة والقدوم، فالتزم أهونهما وهو التسوية بين الواجب ابتداء والواجب بعد الشروع. قال : وما قيل من أن طواف الصدر واجب بفعل وهو الصدر قال بعض المتأخرين : إنه وهم لأنه واجب قبله كما في شرح الجامع الصغير العبد أيضاً بخلاف القدوم. قوله : (وهذا من أبحاثه المخالفة لأهل المذهب أي فلا يعتبر أصلاً كما قاله تلميذه العلامة قاسم قوله : (ثم ينظر إلى الباقي من طواف الصدر) أي الباقي عليه ومنه وهو قدر ما انتقل إلى طواف الزيارة.

 كتاب الحج باب الجنايات أصلهم. وهذا من أبحاثه المخالفة لأهل المذهب قاطبة لكن لم يجب عن تمسكهم بحلق أكثر الرأس في أنه يفيد التحلل بالإجماع فإقامتنا الأكثر في الطواف لأجل التحلل مستفاد من دلالة الإجماع المذكور، إنما لزمه الدم بترك الأقل لأنه أدخل نقصاً في طوافه فصار كما لو طافه محدثاً، وأشار بالترك إلى أن الدم إنما يجب إذا لم يأت بما تركه، أما إذا أتم الباقي فليس عليه شيء إن كان الإتمام في أيام النحر، أما بعدها فيلزمه صدقة عند أبي حنيفة لكل شوط نصف صاع من بر خلافاً لهما، فإن رجع إلى أهله بعث شاة لما بقي من طواف الزيارة وشاة أخرى لترك طواف الصدر. وهذا لأن بعث الشاة لترك الأقل من طواف الزيارة لا يتصور إلا إذا لم يكن طاف للصدر لأنه إذا طاف للصدر انتقل منه إلى طواف الزيارة ما يكمله ثم ينظر إلى الباقي من طواف الصدر إن كان أقله لزمه صدقة وإلا فدم ولو كان طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق وقد ترك من طواف الزيارة أكثره كمله من الصدر ولزمه دمان في قول أبي حنيفة : دم لتأخيره ذلك ودم آخر لترك أكثر الصدر، وإن ترك أقله لزمه للتأخير دم وصدقة للمتروك من الصدر مع ذلك الدم. وجملته كما ذكره الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي أن عليه في ترك الأقل من طواف الزيادة دماً، وفي تأخير الأقل صدقة، وفي ترك الأكثر من طواف الصدر دم وفي ترك أقله صدقة. وفي فتح القدير: ومبني هذا النقل ما تقدم من أن طواف الزيارة ركن عبادة والنية ليست شرطاً لكل ركن إلا ما يستقل عبادة بنفسه فشرط له نية أصل الطواف دون التعيين، فلو طاف في وقته ينوي النذر أو النفل وقع عنه كما لو نوى بالسجدة من الظهر النفل لغت ووقعت عن الركن وإن توالي الأشواط ليس بشرط لصحة الطواف كمن خرج من الطواف لتجديد وضوء ثم رجع بني. الزيارة قوله : (وجملته (الخ أي جملة الكلام في هذه المسائل السابقة ثم ما أفاده في هذا الحاصل من لزوم الصدقة في تأخير الأقل من طواف الزيارة موافق لما ذكره أولاً من قوله «أما بعدها فيلزمه صدقة ومخالف لما بعده من التصريح بلزوم الدم في تأخير أكثره أو أقله وفي الولوالجية : لو طاف ثلاثة للزيارة وطاف طواف الصدر أكمل منه الزيارة ولزمه ترك طواف الصدر اتفاقاً ودم لتأخير الأشواط الأربعة من طواف الزيارة عن وقته إن كان طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأنه أخر الأكثر فصار كتأخير الكل. ومقتضاه أنه لو كان المؤخر الأقل لم يلزمه دم وسنذكره قريباً عن التتارخانية صريحاً وفي القهستاني : لو أخر طواف الفرض كله أو أكثره عن أيام النحر؛ وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لو أخر أقل طوافه لم يجب عليه دم بل صدقة عنده. قوله : (وفي تأخير الأقل صدقة) زاد في التتارخانية : عند أبي حنيفة وفي ترك كله أو أكثره يخرج من الإحرام وفي تأخير كله أو أكثره دم على الاختلاف . قوله : (لكن في عبارته قصور (الخ قد يجاب بأنه تركه للاختلاف فيه ففي اللباب وشرحه : ونو طاف للقدوم جنباً فعليه دم على ما قاله بعض مشايخ العراق واختاره صدر الشريعة وقيل صدقة.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties. The circumambulation of the pillar: if he leaves most of it, he remains in ihram; or if he leaves most of the farewell tawaf, or performs it while in a state of janabah, and charity for leaving the seven? It obligates according to al-Hidayah that tawaf al-qudum becomes obligatory also by commencing, and the commentators affirmed it. It might be said: what is obligatory initially before commencement is stronger than what is obligatory by commencing, so equality should not be expected. He restricted with 'leaving purity for tawaf' because sa'i while in hadath or janabah does nothing, whether umrah or hajj, because it is an act of sa'i performed not in the Sacred Mosque, and the principle is that every act performed not in the Mosque in the rulings of the rituals does not require purity, like sa'i, standing at Arafah, Muzdalifah, and throwing stones, unlike tawaf because it is performed in the Mosque, so purity is obligatory in it. This is stated in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. He said: (or leaving the lesser part of the pillar tawaf, and if he leaves most of it he remains in ihram), i.e., it is obliged a dam for leaving one, two, or three circuits of the visitation tawaf; if he leaves four of them, he is prohibited in terms of women based on the fact that the pillar in our view is the majority, which is four circuits according to the correct opinion as we have presented. The majority is only made to stand for the whole because the Lawgiver made the majority in Hajj stand for the whole in achieving safety from missing out, as a precaution, by his saying: 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete.' And we have said: whoever has intercourse after standing does not invalidate, and after stoning does not invalidate by consensus. And if he shaves most of his head, he becomes in a state of tahallul. So when the matter is on this basis for facilitation, we proceed on this principle and we make the majority stand for the whole in the chapter of tahallul and what is in its course, to preserve this act of worship from missing out and to realize the matter, meaning that tawaf is one of the two tahalluls. So when the majority was made to stand for the whole in one of the two causes, namely shaving, by consensus, it is also made to stand in the other cause, which is tawaf. This is from al-Nihayah. It was criticized in Fath al-Qadir that making the majority stand for the whole in a complete act of worship is only regarding a specific ruling, which is safety from corruption and missing out, not otherwise. Hence it was not ruled that leaving what remains, meaning tawaf, completes Hajj with him, and that is the locus of the text. So it is not necessary to permit making the majority of each part stand for the entirety of that part and leaving its remainder, just as that was not permitted in the very locus of the text, meaning Hajj. So this ruling should not be relied upon, and Allah knows best. Rather, what we believe is that less than seven circuits is not sufficient, and some of it cannot be compensated by anything. Nevertheless, we continue with them in reporting the difference between them. He said: From Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that a sheep is obligatory, but the first is more correct. Then he said: And if he performs tawaf while in a state of janabah, he owes a sheep because it is a great deficiency, but it is less than tawaf al-ziyarah, so it suffices with a sheep. Yes, the objection and answer mentioned by him were mentioned by al-Zayla'i. As for what the author said in his words (and it might be said etc.), it has been answered as in al-Nahr that one of the two prohibited matters is necessary, meaning equality between it and tawaf al-ziyarah and al-qudum, so the easier of the two was adopted, which is equality between what is obligatory initially and what is obligatory after commencement. He said: And what was said that tawaf al-sadr is obligatory by the act, and it is al-sadr, some later scholars said it is a mistake because it is obligatory before it, as in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. And also for the slave? unlike al-qudum. He said: (And this is from his investigations contrary to the people of the madhhab), i.e., it is not considered at all, as his student Allamah Qasim said. He said: (Then one looks at the remainder of tawaf al-sadr), i.e., what remains upon him and from him, and it is the amount that transferred to tawaf al-ziyarah. (page 36) Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties. Their origin. And this is from his investigations contrary to the people of the madhhab entirely, but he did not answer their holding to shaving most of the head in that it benefits tahallul by consensus. So our making the majority stand in tawaf for the sake of tahallul is derived from the indication of the mentioned consensus. The blood is only imposed on him for leaving the lesser part because he introduced a deficiency into his tawaf, so it becomes as if he performed it while in hadath. And he indicated by 'leaving' that the blood is only obligatory if he does not do what he left. But if he completes the remainder, nothing is upon him if the completion is in the days of sacrifice. But after them, a sadaqah is imposed on him according to Abu Hanifa for each circuit half a sa' of wheat, contrary to the two. If he returns to his family, he sends a sheep for what remains of tawaf al-ziyarah and another sheep for leaving tawaf al-sadr. This is because sending a sheep for leaving the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah cannot be imagined unless he has not performed tawaf al-sadr, because if he performed tawaf al-sadr, something transfers from it to tawaf al-ziyarah to complete it. Then one looks at the remainder of tawaf al-sadr: if it is the lesser part, a sadaqah is imposed on him; otherwise, a dam. If he performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of tashriq and had left most of tawaf al-ziyarah, he completes it from al-sadr and two dams are imposed on him according to Abu Hanifa: a dam for delaying that, and another dam for leaving most of al-sadr. If he left its lesser part, a dam for the delay and a sadaqah for the left part of al-sadr along with that dam. And its summary as mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi: he owes a dam for leaving the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah, a sadaqah for delaying the lesser part, a dam for leaving most of tawaf al-sadr, and a sadaqah for leaving its lesser part. And in Fath al-Qadir: the basis of this transmission is what preceded: that tawaf al-ziyarah is a pillar of worship, and intention is not a condition for every pillar except what is itself an independent act of worship, so it is conditioned with the intention of the original tawaf without specification. So if he performs tawaf in its time intending a vow or optional, it counts for him, just as if he intends an optional prostration in Zuhr, it cancels and counts for the pillar. And continuity of circuits is not a condition for the validity of tawaf, like one who leaves tawaf to renew wudu then returns and builds. (al-ziyarah) He said: (And its summary etc.), i.e., the summary of the discourse in these previous issues, then what is benefited in this derived from the imposition of sadaqah for delaying the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah is in agreement with what he first mentioned from his saying 'as for after them, a sadaqah is imposed on him', and contradicts what follows of the explicit statement of the imposition of dam for delaying its most or its lesser part. And in al-Walwajiyyah: if he performs three circuits for al-ziyarah and performs tawaf al-sadr, he completes al-ziyarah from it, and leaving tawaf al-sadr is necessary by agreement, and a dam for delaying the four circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah from its time if he performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of tashriq according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) because he delayed the majority, so it becomes like delaying the whole. Its implication is that if what was delayed was the lesser part, no dam would be required. We will mention it soon from al-Tatarkhaniyyah explicitly. And in al-Qahistani: if he delays the entire obligatory tawaf or most of it from the days of sacrifice, there is an indication that if he delays less than that, no dam is required, but rather a sadaqah according to him. He said: (And for delaying the lesser part a sadaqah). In al-Tatarkhaniyyah, it adds: according to Abu Hanifa. And for leaving all or most of it, he leaves ihram, and for delaying all or most of it, a dam according to the difference. He said: (But in his expression there is brevity etc.). It may be answered that he left it due to the difference in it. In al-Lubab and its commentary: if he performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of janabah, he owes a dam according to what some shaykhs of Iraq said, and it was chosen by Sadr al-Shari'ah; and it was said: a sadaqah.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the rulings on omissions in the obligatory tawaf (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) and the related penalties. The author first establishes that leaving most of Tawaf al-Rukn (the essential tawaf) keeps one in ihram, meaning the Hajj remains incomplete. The key legal principle discussed is that in Hanafi fiqh, the majority (akthar) of an act can stand for the whole (al-akthar muqam al-kull) in the context of Hajj, to prevent the ritual from being invalidated. This is derived from the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete' and the consensus that shaving most of the head effects tahallul. The passage then details that if one omits one, two, or three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a dam (blood sacrifice) is required. If four circuits are left, the person remains in ihram (cannot have marital relations) because the minimum obligatory is four circuits. The text then presents a critique from Fath al-Qadir, arguing that the principle of majority equivalence only applies to the overall act of Hajj, not to its individual parts, and therefore the ruling should not be relied upon. However, the commentator continues to explain the practical rulings. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, performing tawaf while in janabah requires a sheep, whereas the other view (presumably from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considers it a sadaqah. The passage then discusses complex scenarios where a person has left parts of both Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf), and how the missed circuits can be compensated by combining them, leading to multiple penalties. The summary from al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi is provided: leaving the lesser part of Tawaf al-Ziyarah requires a dam; delaying the lesser part requires a sadaqah; leaving most of Tawaf al-Sadr requires a dam; leaving its lesser part requires a sadaqah. Finally, the text touches on the issue of intention (niyyah) in tawaf, stating that for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a general intention of tawaf suffices without specifying it as obligatory, and continuity of circuits is not a condition, so one can break tawaf to renew wudu and resume. The passage ends with a reference to a difference of opinion regarding tawaf al-qudum performed in janabah: some say a dam, others say a sadaqah.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The essential circumambulation (rukn) of Hajj, performed on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah and the following days.
الدم (al-dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required for certain violations or omissions in Hajj and Umrah.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Charity, here specifically half a sa' of wheat per circuit omitted, for less serious violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the penalty for leaving three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) A dam (blood sacrifice).
B) A sadaqah of half a sa' per circuit.
C) Nothing, as long as the remaining four circuits are completed later.
D) The Hajj becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the majority of an obligatory act in Hajj to substitute for the whole, but deficiencies require compensatory dam.

Penalty for Tawaf in a State of Janabah and Summary of Omission Penalties
Intra-Hanafi dispute on penalty for tawaf in janabah and summary of penalties for omissions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf performed in janabah, identify the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the summary of penalties for various omissions in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr.

Core Idea
Tawaf in janabah requires a sheep according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn say sadaqah. The relied-upon view is a sheep.

This passage continues from the previous lesson, focusing on the penalty for performing tawaf while in a state of janabah (major impurity). It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa requires a sheep (shah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider a sadaqah sufficient. The commentator notes that the first view is more correct. The passage then delves into complex scenarios where a pilgrim has left parts of both Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf), and provides a summary of penalties from al-Kafi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is the penalty for performing tawaf (al-qudum or al-ziyarah) while in a state of janabah.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: a sheep (shah) is required. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: sadaqah (half sa' per circuit) is sufficient.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the tarjih
The text says 'the first is more correct' (al-awal asahh), indicating the preferred view is a sheep.
The author inclines towards Abu Hanifa's opinion.
4
Understand the complex scenarios
When a pilgrim has omitted circuits from both Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr, penalties combine: e.g., if most of Ziyarah is left, it is completed from Sadr, and both omissions incur separate penalties (dams or sadaqas).
The summary from al-Kafi provides a clear framework.
5
Summarize the rule from al-Kafi
Dam for leaving the lesser part of Ziyarah; sadaqah for delaying the lesser part; dam for leaving most of Sadr; sadaqah for leaving the lesser part of Sadr.
This summary is practical for fatwa.

طواف الركن ولو ترك أكثره بقي محرماً أو ترك أكثر الصدر أو طافه حنباً وصدقة بترك السبعة يوجب عنه في الهداية بأن طواف القدوم يصير واجباً أيضاً بالشروع وأقره الشارحون وقد يقال: إن ما وجب ابتداء قبل الشروع أقوى مما وجب بالشروع فينبغي عدم المساواة. قيد بترك الطهارة للطواف لأن السعي محدثاً أو جنباً لا شيء، سواء كان عمرة أو حج، لأنه عبادة سعي تؤدى لا في المسجد الحرام والأصل أن كل عبادة تؤدى لا في المسجد في أحكام المناسك فالطهارة ليست بواجبة لها كالسعي والوقوف بعرفة والمزدلفة ورمي الجمار بخلاف الطواف فإنه عبادة تؤدى في المسجد فكانت الطهارة واجبة فيه كذا في الفتاوى الظهيرية. قوله : (أو ترك أقل طواف الركن ولو ترك أكثره بقي محرماً) أي يجب دم بترك شوط أو شوطين أو ثلاثة من طواف الزيارة، ولو ترك أربعة منه فإنه محرم في حق النساء بناء على أن الركن عندنا أكثر وهو أربعة أشواط على الصحيح كما قدمناه وإنما أقيم الأكثر مقام الكل لأن الشرع أقام الأكثر في الحج مقام الكل في وقوع الأمن عن الفوات احتياطاً بقوله «من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه». وقد قلنا من جامع بعد الوقوف لا يفسد وبعد الرمي لا يفسد بالإجماع، ولو حلق أكثر الرأس صار متحللاً فلما كان الأمر على هذا الوجه للتيسير جرينا على هذا الأصل فأقمنا الأكثر مقام الكل في باب التحلل وما يجري مجراه صيانة لهذه العبادة عن الفوات وتحقيقاً للأمر يعني أن الطواف أحد التحلل فلما أقيم الأكثر مقام الكل في أحد السببين سببي الحلق بالإجماع أقيم في السبب الآخر وهو الطواف أيضاً. كذا في النهاية. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن إقامة الأكثر في تمام العبادة إنما هو في حق حكم خاص وهو أمن الفساد والفوات ليس غير ولذا لم يحكم بأن ترك ما بقي أعني الطواف يتم معه الحج وهو مورد ذلك النص فلا يلزم جواز إقامة أكثر كل جزء منه مقام تمام ذلك الجزء وترك باقيه كما لم يجز ذلك في نفس مورد النص أعني الحج فلا ينبغي التعويل على هذا الحكم والله أعلم، بل الذي ندين به أن لا يجزيء أقل من السبعة ولا يجبر بعضه بشيء غير أنا نستمر معهم في التقرير على التفاوت بينهما. قال : وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يجب شاة إلا أن الأول أصح ثم قال : وإن طاف جنباً فعليه شاة لأنه نقص كثير ثم هو دون طواف الزيارة فيكتفي بالشاة. نعم ما ذكره من الإشكال والجواب ذكره الزيلعي وأما ما ذكره المؤلف بقوله (وقد يقال الخ) فقد أجيب ينظر إلى الباقي من طواف الصدر) أي الباقي عليه ومنه وهو قدر ما انتقل إلى طواف الزيارة.

والنية ليست شرطاً لكل ركن إلا ما يستقل عبادة بنفسه فشرط له نية أصل الطواف دون التعيين، فلو طاف في وقته ينوي النذر أو النفل وقع عنه كما لو نوى بالسجدة من الظهر النفل لغت ووقعت عن الركن وإن توالي الأشواط ليس بشرط لصحة الطواف كمن خرج من الطواف لتجديد وضوء ثم رجع بني. الزيارة قوله : (وجملته (الخ أي جملة الكلام في هذه المسائل السابقة ثم ما أفاده في هذا الحاصل من لزوم الصدقة في تأخير الأقل من طواف الزيارة موافق لما ذكره أولاً من قوله «أما بعدها فيلزمه صدقة ومخالف لما بعده من التصريح بلزوم الدم في تأخير أكثره أو أقله وفي الولوالجية : لو طاف ثلاثة للزيارة وطاف طواف الصدر أكمل منه الزيارة ولزمه ترك طواف الصدر اتفاقاً ودم لتأخير الأشواط الأربعة من طواف الزيارة عن وقته إن كان طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأنه أخر الأكثر فصار كتأخير الكل. ومقتضاه أنه لو كان المؤخر الأقل ونو طاف للقدوم جنباً فعليه دم على ما قاله بعض مشايخ العراق واختاره صدر الشريعة وقيل صدقة.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties. The circumambulation of the pillar: if he leaves most of it, he remains in ihram; or if he leaves most of the farewell tawaf, or performs it while in a state of janabah, and charity for leaving the seven? It obligates according to al-Hidayah that tawaf al-qudum becomes obligatory also by commencing, and the commentators affirmed it. It might be said: what is obligatory initially before commencement is stronger than what is obligatory by commencing, so equality should not be expected. He restricted with 'leaving purity for tawaf' because sa'i while in hadath or janabah does nothing, whether umrah or hajj, because it is an act of sa'i performed not in the Sacred Mosque, and the principle is that every act performed not in the Mosque in the rulings of the rituals does not require purity, like sa'i, standing at Arafah, Muzdalifah, and throwing stones, unlike tawaf because it is performed in the Mosque, so purity is obligatory in it. This is stated in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. He said: (or leaving the lesser part of the pillar tawaf, and if he leaves most of it he remains in ihram), i.e., it is obliged a dam for leaving one, two, or three circuits of the visitation tawaf; if he leaves four of them, he is prohibited in terms of women based on the fact that the pillar in our view is the majority, which is four circuits according to the correct opinion as we have presented. The majority is only made to stand for the whole because the Lawgiver made the majority in Hajj stand for the whole in achieving safety from missing out, as a precaution, by his saying: 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete.' And we have said: whoever has intercourse after standing does not invalidate, and after stoning does not invalidate by consensus. And if he shaves most of his head, he becomes in a state of tahallul. So when the matter is on this basis for facilitation, we proceed on this principle and we make the majority stand for the whole in the chapter of tahallul and what is in its course, to preserve this act of worship from missing out and to realize the matter, meaning that tawaf is one of the two tahalluls. So when the majority was made to stand for the whole in one of the two causes, namely shaving, by consensus, it is also made to stand in the other cause, which is tawaf. This is from al-Nihayah. It was criticized in Fath al-Qadir that making the majority stand for the whole in a complete act of worship is only regarding a specific ruling, which is safety from corruption and missing out, not otherwise. Hence it was not ruled that leaving what remains, meaning tawaf, completes Hajj with him, and that is the locus of the text. So it is not necessary to permit making the majority of each part stand for the entirety of that part and leaving its remainder, just as that was not permitted in the very locus of the text, meaning Hajj. So this ruling should not be relied upon, and Allah knows best. Rather, what we believe is that less than seven circuits is not sufficient, and some of it cannot be compensated by anything. Nevertheless, we continue with them in reporting the difference between them. He said: From Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that a sheep is obligatory, but the first is more correct. Then he said: And if he performs tawaf while in a state of janabah, he owes a sheep because it is a great deficiency, but it is less than tawaf al-ziyarah, so it suffices with a sheep. Yes, the objection and answer mentioned by him were mentioned by al-Zayla'i. As for what the author said in his words (and it might be said etc.), it has been answered as in al-Nahr that one of the two prohibited matters is necessary, meaning equality between it and tawaf al-ziyarah and al-qudum, so the easier of the two was adopted, which is equality between what is obligatory initially and what is obligatory after commencement. He said: And what was said that tawaf al-sadr is obligatory by the act, and it is al-sadr, some later scholars said it is a mistake because it is obligatory before it, as in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. And also for the slave? unlike al-qudum. He said: (And this is from his investigations contrary to the people of the madhhab), i.e., it is not considered at all, as his student Allamah Qasim said. He said: (Then one looks at the remainder of tawaf al-sadr), i.e., what remains upon him and from him, and it is the amount that transferred to tawaf al-ziyarah. (page 36) Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties. Their origin. And this is from his investigations contrary to the people of the madhhab entirely, but he did not answer their holding to shaving most of the head in that it benefits tahallul by consensus. So our making the majority stand in tawaf for the sake of tahallul is derived from the indication of the mentioned consensus. The blood is only imposed on him for leaving the lesser part because he introduced a deficiency into his tawaf, so it becomes as if he performed it while in hadath. And he indicated by 'leaving' that the blood is only obligatory if he does not do what he left. But if he completes the remainder, nothing is upon him if the completion is in the days of sacrifice. But after them, a sadaqah is imposed on him according to Abu Hanifa for each circuit half a sa' of wheat, contrary to the two. If he returns to his family, he sends a sheep for what remains of tawaf al-ziyarah and another sheep for leaving tawaf al-sadr. This is because sending a sheep for leaving the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah cannot be imagined unless he has not performed tawaf al-sadr, because if he performed tawaf al-sadr, something transfers from it to tawaf al-ziyarah to complete it. Then one looks at the remainder of tawaf al-sadr: if it is the lesser part, a sadaqah is imposed on him; otherwise, a dam. If he performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of tashriq and had left most of tawaf al-ziyarah, he completes it from al-sadr and two dams are imposed on him according to Abu Hanifa: a dam for delaying that, and another dam for leaving most of al-sadr. If he left its lesser part, a dam for the delay and a sadaqah for the left part of al-sadr along with that dam. And its summary as mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi: he owes a dam for leaving the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah, a sadaqah for delaying the lesser part, a dam for leaving most of tawaf al-sadr, and a sadaqah for leaving its lesser part. And in Fath al-Qadir: the basis of this transmission is what preceded: that tawaf al-ziyarah is a pillar of worship, and intention is not a condition for every pillar except what is itself an independent act of worship, so it is conditioned with the intention of the original tawaf without specification. So if he performs tawaf in its time intending a vow or optional, it counts for him, just as if he intends an optional prostration in Zuhr, it cancels and counts for the pillar. And continuity of circuits is not a condition for the validity of tawaf, like one who leaves tawaf to renew wudu then returns and builds. (al-ziyarah) He said: (And its summary etc.), i.e., the summary of the discourse in these previous issues, then what is benefited in this derived from the imposition of sadaqah for delaying the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah is in agreement with what he first mentioned from his saying 'as for after them, a sadaqah is imposed on him', and contradicts what follows of the explicit statement of the imposition of dam for delaying its most or its lesser part. And in al-Walwajiyyah: if he performs three circuits for al-ziyarah and performs tawaf al-sadr, he completes al-ziyarah from it, and leaving tawaf al-sadr is necessary by agreement, and a dam for delaying the four circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah from its time if he performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of tashriq according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) because he delayed the majority, so it becomes like delaying the whole. Its implication is that if what was delayed was the lesser part, no dam would be required. We will mention it soon from al-Tatarkhaniyyah explicitly. And in al-Qahistani: if he delays the entire obligatory tawaf or most of it from the days of sacrifice, there is an indication that if he delays less than that, no dam is required, but rather a sadaqah according to him. He said: (And for delaying the lesser part a sadaqah). In al-Tatarkhaniyyah, it adds: according to Abu Hanifa. And for leaving all or most of it, he leaves ihram, and for delaying all or most of it, a dam according to the difference. He said: (But in his expression there is brevity etc.). It may be answered that he left it due to the difference in it. In al-Lubab and its commentary: if he performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of janabah, he owes a dam according to what some shaykhs of Iraq said, and it was chosen by Sadr al-Shari'ah; and it was said: a sadaqah.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the rulings on omissions in the obligatory tawaf (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) and the related penalties. The author first establishes that leaving most of Tawaf al-Rukn (the essential tawaf) keeps one in ihram, meaning the Hajj remains incomplete. The key legal principle discussed is that in Hanafi fiqh, the majority (akthar) of an act can stand for the whole (al-akthar muqam al-kull) in the context of Hajj, to prevent the ritual from being invalidated. This is derived from the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah, his Hajj is complete' and the consensus that shaving most of the head effects tahallul. The passage then details that if one omits one, two, or three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a dam (blood sacrifice) is required. If four circuits are left, the person remains in ihram (cannot have marital relations) because the minimum obligatory is four circuits. The text then presents a critique from Fath al-Qadir, arguing that the principle of majority equivalence only applies to the overall act of Hajj, not to its individual parts, and therefore the ruling should not be relied upon. However, the commentator continues to explain the practical rulings. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, performing tawaf while in janabah requires a sheep, whereas the other view (presumably from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considers it a sadaqah. The passage then discusses complex scenarios where a person has left parts of both Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf), and how the missed circuits can be compensated by combining them, leading to multiple penalties. The summary from al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi is provided: leaving the lesser part of Tawaf al-Ziyarah requires a dam; delaying the lesser part requires a sadaqah; leaving most of Tawaf al-Sadr requires a dam; leaving its lesser part requires a sadaqah. Finally, the text touches on the issue of intention (niyyah) in tawaf, stating that for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a general intention of tawaf suffices without specifying it as obligatory, and continuity of circuits is not a condition, so one can break tawaf to renew wudu and resume. The passage ends with a reference to a difference of opinion regarding tawaf al-qudum performed in janabah: some say a dam, others say a sadaqah.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The essential circumambulation (rukn) of Hajj, performed on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah and the following days.
الدم (al-dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required for certain violations or omissions in Hajj and Umrah.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Charity, here specifically half a sa' of wheat per circuit omitted, for less serious violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A sheep (shah).
B) Sadaqah (half sa' per circuit).
C) No penalty if repeated later.
D) The tawaf becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf in janabah is valid but requires a sheep (preferred), not sadaqah, and multiple omissions require separate penalties.

Penalties for Omitting Parts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Tawaf al-Sadr
Ruling on compensations for omission of parts of the essential and farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required compensation (dam or sadaqah) for omitting parts of tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-sadr, and apply the Hanafi rules to determine the correct penalty based on quantity and timing.

Core Idea
The penalty for omitting part of tawaf depends on which tawaf, how much is omitted, and when it is remedied.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the compensations for omissions in the two key circumambulations of Hajj: tawaf al-ziyarah (an essential pillar) and tawaf al-sadr (a wajib). The rulings distinguish between omitting the majority (akthar) and the minority (aqall), and whether the deficiency is made up within the days of Nahr or later. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for determining whether a blood sacrifice (dam) or charity (sadaqah) is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tawafs and their legal status
Tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj; its omission invalidates the Hajj if not performed. Tawaf al-sadr is a wajib (obligatory but not a pillar); its omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the Hajj.
2
Determine the quantity omitted
For each tawaf, assess whether the omitted circuits constitute the majority (akthar) or the minority (aqall) of the required 7 circuits. This classification determines the baseline penalty: dam for majority omission, sadaqah for minority omission.
Majority = 4 or more circuits; minority = 3 or fewer.
3
Apply the rule for tawaf al-ziyarah
If the lesser part (aqall) is omitted and never completed, dam is required. If it is completed within the days of Nahr, no penalty. If completed after the days of Nahr, sadaqah per circuit (half sa' of wheat) according to Abu Hanifa; the two companions differ.
The initial dam is waived if the omitted circuits are eventually performed.
4
Apply the rule for tawaf al-sadr
Omitting the majority (akthar) of tawaf al-sadr requires dam; omitting the minority (aqall) requires sadaqah. There is no completion exception as for tawaf al-ziyarah.
5
Handle combined scenarios and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If both tawafs are deficient, use the circuits from tawaf al-sadr to complete tawaf al-ziyarah, then assess the remainder for tawaf al-sadr. Note the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the sadaqah after the days of Nahr.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصلهم ا هـ . وهذا من أبحاثه المخالفة لأهل المذهب قاطبة لكن لم يجب عن تمسكهم بحلق أكثر الرأس في أنه يفيد التحلل بالإجماع فإقامتنا الأكثر في الطواف لأجل التحلل مستفاد من دلالة الإجماع المذكور، إنما لزمه الدم بترك الأقل لأنه أدخل نقصاً في طوافه فصار كما لو طافه محدثاً، وأشار بالترك إلى أن الدم إنما يجب إذا لم يأت بما تركه، أما إذا أتم الباقي فليس عليه شيء إن كان الإتمام في أيام النحر، أما بعدها فيلزمه صدقة عند أبي حنيفة لكل شوط نصف صاع من بر خلافاً لهما، فإن رجع إلى أهله بعث شاة لما بقي من طواف الزيارة وشاة أخرى لترك طواف الصدر. وهذا لأن بعث الشاة لترك الأقل من طواف الزيارة لا يتصور إلا إذا لم يكن طاف للصدر لأنه إذا طاف للصدر انتقل منه إلى طواف الزيارة ما يكمله ثم ينظر إلى الباقي من طواف الصدر إن كان أقله لزمه صدقة وإلا فدم ولو كان طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق وقد ترك من طواف الزيارة أكثره كمله من الصدر ولزمه دمان في قول أبي حنيفة : دم لتأخيره ذلك ودم آخر لترك أكثر الصدر، وإن ترك أقله لزمه للتأخير دم وصدقة للمتروك من الصدر مع ذلك الدم. وجملته كما ذكره الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي أن عليه في ترك الأقل من طواف الزيادة دماً، وفي تأخير الأقل صدقة، وفي ترك الأكثر من طواف الصدر ،دم وفي ترك أقله صدقة.
Their origin, etc. And this is among his investigations that contradict the people of the madhhab entirely, but he did not respond to their argument with shaving most of the head that it brings about tahlil by consensus, so our establishing the majority in tawaf for the sake of tahlil is derived from the indication of the mentioned consensus. Indeed, the blood sacrifice becomes necessary by omitting the lesser part because he introduced a deficiency in his tawaf, so it becomes as if he performed it in a state of minor impurity. And he indicated by 'omission' that the blood sacrifice is only obligatory if he does not perform what he omitted. As for if he completes the remainder, nothing is upon him if the completion occurs during the days of al-Nahr. As for after them, a charity is required according to Abu Hanifa for each circuit half a sa' of wheat, contrary to the two companions. If he returns to his family, he sends a sheep for what remains of tawaf al-ziyarah and another sheep for omitting tawaf al-sadr. This is because sending the sheep for omitting the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah is not conceivable unless he had not performed tawaf al-sadr, because if he had performed tawaf al-sadr, what completes it transfers from it to tawaf al-ziyarah, then he looks at the remainder of tawaf al-sadr: if it is the lesser part, charity is required; otherwise, blood. And if he had performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of al-Tashriq and had omitted the majority of tawaf al-ziyarah, he completes it from al-sadr, and two blood sacrifices are required in the opinion of Abu Hanifa: a blood sacrifice for delaying that and another blood sacrifice for omitting the majority of al-sadr. And if he omitted the lesser part, then due to delay, a blood sacrifice and charity for what was omitted from al-sadr along with that blood. And its summary as mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi is that for omitting the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah, a blood sacrifice; for delaying the lesser part, charity; for omitting the majority of tawaf al-sadr, blood; and for omitting its lesser part, charity.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing penalties for omitting parts of the essential tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah) and the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr). The author begins by citing a consensus that performing the majority of tawaf suffices for tahlil. The ruling: omitting the lesser part (aqall) of tawaf al-ziyarah requires a blood sacrifice (dam). If he completes the remaining circuits within the days of Nahr, nothing is due; if after, charity (sadaqah) of half a sa' per circuit is due according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. If he returns to his family, he sends a sheep for the remainder of tawaf al-ziyarah and another for omitting tawaf al-sadr. The reasoning: sending the sheep for the lesser part only applies if he had not performed tawaf al-sadr; if he had, the deficiency is transferred. Various scenarios are detailed: at the end of tashriq, omitting the majority of ziyarah and performing sadr requires two blood sacrifices according to Abu Hanifa. The summary from al-Kafi consolidates: omitting less of ziyarah requires dam; delaying the less requires sadaqah; omitting most of sadr requires dam; omitting less of sadr requires sadaqah. The key distinction is that tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn (pillar), so even a small omission requires dam; tawaf al-sadr is wajib, so only majority omission requires dam.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The essential circumambulation of the Kaaba during Hajj, performed on the 10th or days of tashriq; a rukn of Hajj.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Mecca; a wajib in Hanafi school.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for certain omissions or violations in Hajj.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity paid as a penalty, here half a sa' of wheat per circuit omitted or delayed.
أقل (aqall): The lesser part (less than half) of the required tawaf circuits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Dam
B) Sadaqah (half sa' per circuit)
C) Nothing
D) Two sheep

Key Takeaway
The penalty for omitting parts of tawaf depends on whether the omission is of the majority or minority, the type of tawaf (rukn vs wajib), and whether the deficiency is remedied within the days of Nahr or after.

Intention and Continuity in Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Explanation that tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn and does not require specific intention for each circuit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the intention and continuity requirements for tawaf al-ziyarah and apply it to cases where the intention differs or interruption occurs.

Core Idea
In tawaf al-ziyarah, a general intention suffices; continuity is sunnah, not a condition.

This lesson unpacks a key ruling from Fath al-Qadir regarding tawaf al-ziyarah, the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj. The passage clarifies two important points: first, that only an overarching intention for tawaf is required, not a specific designation for each circuit; second, that the seven circuits need not be performed without interruption. Understanding these points prevents common errors and ensures correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on intention
The text states that intention is not required for every rukn, only for acts that are independent acts of worship. Tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn, so intention for the overall act (niyyat asl al-tawaf) suffices; specification (ta'yin) of whether it is fard, nafl, etc. is not needed.
This is based on the principle that a rukn that is part of a larger act does not need its own distinct intention.
2
Analyze the implication of differing intentions
The text provides an example: if someone performs tawaf during its prescribed time intending a vow (nadhr) or supererogatory tawaf, it counts as the obligatory tawaf. This is analogous to a prostration during Zuhr prayer: if one intends a supererogatory prostration, it actually fulfills the obligatory prostration.
This shows that the intention for the act itself overrides the specific type when the act is done at the proper time.
3
Examine the ruling on continuity (muwalat)
The text explicitly says continuity of circuits is not a condition for validity. An interruption, such as leaving to renew wudu and then returning, does not invalidate the tawaf; one may continue from where one left off.
This differs from some other schools that require uninterrupted sequence. In the Hanafi school, it is merely recommended (sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير: ومبني هذا النقل ما تقدم من أن طواف الزيارة ركن عبادة والنية ليست شرطاً لكل ركن إلا ما يستقل عبادة بنفسه فشرط له نية أصل الطواف دون التعيين، فلو طاف في وقته ينوي النذر أو النفل وقع عنه كما لو نوى بالسجدة من الظهر النفل لغت ووقعت عن الركن وإن توالي الأشواط ليس بشرط لصحة الطواف كمن خرج من الطواف لتجديد وضوء ثم رجع بني .
And in Fath al-Qadir: This transmission is based on what preceded: that tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn of worship, and intention is not a condition for every rukn except what is independently an act of worship; so intention for the origin of tawaf is required without specification (of type). So if he performed tawaf in its time intending a vow or supererogatory act, it counts for the obligatory one, just as if he intended a supererogatory prostration during Zuhr prayer, it is void and counts for the obligatory prostration. And continuity of circuits is not a condition for the validity of tawaf, like one who leaves tawaf to renew ablution and then returns and builds upon his circuits.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from Fath al-Qadir. It explains that tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, thus a single act of worship. Intention (niyyah) is required for the overall act, but not for each circuit, nor is specification of the type (e.g., fard, nafl) necessary. If one performs tawaf during its appointed time with an intention for a vow or supererogatory tawaf, it fulfills the obligatory tawaf. This is analogous to a prostration in prayer: if one intends a supererogatory prostration during Zuhr, it actually counts for the obligatory one. Additionally, continuity (muwalat) of the seven circuits is not a condition for validity; one may interrupt tawaf to renew wudu and then continue from where he left off.

Key Terms
نية أصل الطواف (niyyat asl al-tawaf): Intention for the overall act of tawaf, without specifying whether it is obligatory or supererogatory.
توالي الأشواط (muwalat al-ashwat): Continuity of the seven circuits of tawaf without significant interruption.
ركن عبادة (rukn ibadah): A pillar of worship; an integral part that if omitted invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It counts as supererogatory only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tawaf al-ziyarah requires only an overall intention for tawaf, not specification of type, and continuity of circuits is not a condition for validity.

Penalties for Tawaf al-Sadr, Tawaf al-Qudum with Impurity, and the Transfer of Circuits
Expansion of penalties for tawaf al-sadr and tawaf al-qudum with impurity and omission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi penalties for omitting or performing tawaf al-sadr and tawaf al-qudum with impurity, explain the internal dispute on tawaf al-qudum in janabah, and apply the rule of naql (transfer) in a compound scenario.

Core Idea
For wajib tawaf, omitting majority requires dam; for rukn tawaf, even minority requires dam. Impurity: hadath→sadaqah, janabah→dam.

This lesson delves into the detailed penalties (jaza') for tawaf al-sadr and tawaf al-qudum when performed with impurity or omitted partially. The Hanafi school distinguishes between wajib and rukn tawaf, leading to different rulings for delaying majority vs minority. It also addresses the internal dispute on whether tawaf al-qudum requires dam or sadaqah when done in janabah, and the concept of transferring circuits to avoid penalties. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correct fiqh of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tawaf type
Determine whether the tawaf is a rukn (ziyarah) or wajib (sadr), as this affects the penalty for omission. Tawaf al-sadr is wajib; tawaf al-qudum is sunnah but penalties for impurity follow the same rule as sadr per al-Majma'.
Tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn, so its omission, even a minority, requires dam.
2
Determine the extent of omission or impurity
For omission: majority vs minority. For impurity: minor (hadath) vs major (janabah). These determine whether dam or sadaqah applies. For wajib tawaf, omitting majority requires dam, minority requires sadaqah; for rukn tawaf, even minority requires dam. For impurity, hadath→sadaqah, janabah→dam for both qudum and sadr.
The passage explicitly distinguishes between majority and minority for tawaf al-sadr.
3
Apply the penalty rule to simple cases
If a pilgrim omits the majority of tawaf al-sadr, dam is required. If he omits the minority, sadaqah per shawt. If he performs it with hadath, sadaqah; with janabah, dam. For tawaf al-qudum, the preferred view is the same: hadath→sadaqah, janabah→dam.
Internal Hanafi dispute exists for tawaf al-qudum; the text gives preference to al-Majma'.
4
Consider the transfer (naql) option
In certain scenarios, circuits from tawaf al-sadr can be transferred to complete tawaf al-ziyarah, which may reduce the penalty. Transfer is only beneficial if it avoids a greater penalty, e.g., when the pilgrim has not yet returned home and performed tawaf al-sadr during the days of al-Nahr.
If transfer leads to omission of tawaf al-sadr, blood is still required by consensus, so transfer may not help if the pilgrim has returned home.
5
Analyze the compound scenario
When both tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-sadr are involved with different impurity states, calculate the total penalty. If tawaf al-ziyarah was in hadath and tawaf al-sadr in purity at the end of tashriq, one sheep is due (for hadath in ziyarah). If tawaf al-ziyarah was in janabah, two sheep are due (one for janabah, one for omission of sadr if not transferred). The possibility of naql affects whether the second sheep is owed.
The passage explains that transfer is not beneficial if the pilgrim has already returned home, as blood would be required for omitting tawaf al-sadr anyway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المجمع أولى وهي: وإن طاف للقدوم أو للصدر محدثاً وجبت صدقة وجنباً دم فأفاد أنه لا فرق بينهما في الحدثين . وأشار بالترك إلى أنه لو أتى بما تركه فإنه لا يلزمه شيء مطلقاً لأنه ليس بمؤقت، وفي الهداية ويؤمر بالإعادة ما دام بمكة إقامة للواجب في وقته قوله : (أو طاف للركن محدثاً وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق ودمان لو طاف للركن جنباً) أي تجب شاة في الأولى وشاتان في الثانية. أما في الأولى فهي بسبب الحدث ولم ينقل طواف الصدر إلى الزيارة لأنه لا فائدة في النقل لأنه لو نقل يجب عليه الدم لترك طواف الصدر إجماعاً إن كان رجع إلى طاف للصدر في أيام النحر أو لا قيد بقوله في آخر أيام التشريق» لأنه لو طاف للصدر في أيام النحر ولم يرجع إلى أهله فإنه ينقل طواف الصدر إلى طواف الزيارة لأن في النقل فائدة وهو سقوط الدم لأجل الحدث ثم يطوف للصدر ولا شيء عليه بخلاف ما إذا طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق ولم يرجع إلى أهله حيث لا ينقل عند أبي حنيفة لأنه لا قال صاحب العناية : الظاهر وجوب الصدقة وقيل : لا شيء عليه لما في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وشرح الطحاوي: ليس لطواف التحية صدقة، ولو طافه محدثاً فعليه صدقة على ما في عامة الكتب وصرح به عن محمد وهو مختار القدوري وصاحب الهداية وغيرهما ا.هـ. أقول : لكن ما في المبسوط لا يدل على ما حكاه شارح اللباب من القول الثالث لأن نفي الصدقة صادق بوجوب الدم فيكون ذلك مؤيداً للقول الأول، وليس نصاً على أنه لا يجب شيء تأمل قوله : (وأما في الأولى) أي في المسألة الأولى وهي ما لو طاف للركن محدثاً وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق. وقوله «فهي» أي الجناية أو الشاة أي وجوبها بسبب الحدث في طواف الزيارة وعبارة الشرح : لأنه في الوجه الأول لم ينتقل طواف الصدر إلى طواف الزيارة لأنه واجب وإعادة الزيارة بسب الحدث غير واجب وإنما هو مستحب فلا ينقل طواف الصدر إليه فيجب الدم بسبب الحدث في طواف الزيارة. وتبعه في النهر واعترض قول المؤلف لأنه لا فائدة في النقل الخ ) بقوله : وقد يقال إن نفي الفائدة ممنوع إذ لو نقل الدم ووجب عليه الإعادة ما دام بمكة ا هـ . . أي والحال أنه قد طاف للصدر في أيام النحر وإلا فلا فائدة في النقل لوجوب الدم بالتأخير، ولا يخفى عليك اندفاع هذا المنع لأنه قيده بكونه رجع إلى أهله، أما لو لم يرجع فقد ذكر أنه ينقل إن كان طاف في أيام النحر فتدبر قوله : (وأما في الثانية) أي وأما وجوب الدم في المسألة الثانية وهي ما لو طاف للركن جنباً وللصدر طاهراً في آخر
The commentary on the summary: The gist of the speech in these previous issues, then what was implied in this derived ruling of the obligation of charity for delaying the lesser part of tawaf al-ziyarah is consistent with what he first mentioned from his statement 'As for after them, charity is required upon him' and contradicts what followed of explicit statement that blood is required for delaying its majority or minority. In al-Walwaljiyyah: If he performed three circuits for al-ziyarah and performed tawaf al-sadr, he completes al-ziyarah from it, and the omission of tawaf al-sadr is agreed upon, and blood is required for delaying the four circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah beyond its time if he performed tawaf al-sadr at the end of the days of al-Tashriq according to Abu Hanifa, because he delayed the majority, so it becomes like delaying the whole. Its implication is that if the delayed part was the minority, blood is not required. We will mention it soon from al-Tatar Khaniyyah explicitly. In al-Qahistani: If he delayed the whole obligatory tawaf or its majority beyond the days of al-Nahr, and in it is an indication that if he delayed its minority, blood is not required but charity according to him. He said: (And for delaying the minority, charity) al-Tatar Khaniyyah added: according to Abu Hanifa. And for omitting all or most, he leaves ihram. And for delaying all or most, blood according to the disagreement. He said: (But in his expression there is deficiency) perhaps it is answered that he left it due to disagreement about it. In al-Lubab and its commentary: And if he performed tawaf al-qudum in a state of janabah, blood is required according to some Iraqi masters and chosen by Sadr al-Shari'ah, and it was said charity. He said: (Or he omitted the majority of al-sadr or performed it in janabah, and charity for omitting its minority) i.e., blood is required. And since tawaf al-sadr is wajib, blood is required for omitting all or most, and for omitting its minority, charity of half a sa' per circuit of wheat, distinguishing between majority and minority, contrary to the minority of tawaf al-ziyarah and umrah where blood is required for its omission because it is a rukn tawaf so it is stronger than the wajib. He said: (Or he performed tawaf al-ziyarah in minor impurity and tawaf al-sadr in purity at the end of tashriq, and two blood sacrifices if he performed tawaf al-ziyarah in janabah) i.e., one sheep is required in the first case and two in the second. In the first, it is due to the hadath and tawaf al-sadr is not transferred to al-ziyarah because there is no benefit in transfer because if he transfers, blood would be required for omitting tawaf al-sadr by consensus if he had returned...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the earlier summary. It clarifies that the ruling for delaying the minority of tawaf al-ziyarah is charity according to Abu Hanifa, with disagreement from the two companions. It discusses the scenario of combining tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-sadr: if one performs three circuits of ziyarah and then performs tawaf al-sadr, the remaining circuits can be completed from al-sadr, and blood may be required for delaying the majority. The commentator criticizes the author for not including the ruling for tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) when performed in impurity. According to al-Majma', tawaf al-qudum or al-sadr in minor impurity requires charity, in major impurity requires blood. The passage then explains the distinction between tawaf al-sadr as wajib and tawaf al-ziyarah as rukn: for tawaf al-sadr, omitting majority requires dam, minority requires sadaqah; for tawaf al-ziyarah, even minority requires dam because it is a rukn. Finally, a complex scenario: if one performs tawaf al-ziyarah in minor impurity and tawaf al-sadr in purity at the end of tashriq, one sheep is due; if tawaf al-ziyarah was in major impurity, two sheep are due. The reasoning involves whether transfer of circuits from al-sadr to al-ziyarah is beneficial, which depends on timing and whether he has returned home.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The arrival circumambulation performed upon entering Mecca for Hajj or Umrah; a sunnah in Hanafi school.
حدث (hadath): Minor impurity requiring wudu (e.g., breaking wind, passing urine).
جنب (junub): State of major impurity requiring ghusl (e.g., after sexual intercourse or seminal emission).
نقل (naql): Transfer of circuits from one tawaf to another to complete a deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for performing tawaf al-qudum in a state of janabah according to the preferred view?
A) Dam (blood sacrifice)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) No penalty
D) The tawaf is invalid

Key Takeaway
The penalty for impurity in tawaf depends on the tawaf's status and the type of impurity: wajib tawaf (sadr/qudum) requires dam for janabah and sadaqah for hadath; rukn tawaf (ziyarah) requires dam for even minor omission and for janabah.

Penalties for Leaving or Invalidating the Farewell Tawaf
Rulings on penalties for tawaf al-sadr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for omitting parts of tawaf al-sadr and for performing it in a state of impurity, and distinguish between the penalties for a wajib versus a rukn tawaf.

Core Idea
Leaving most or all of the farewell tawaf requires a dam; leaving a little requires sadaqah; performing it while junub also requires a dam.

In this passage, the commentator Ibn Nujaym expands on the matn's concise ruling regarding the farewell tawaf. He clarifies that since this tawaf is wajib (not rukn), the penalty for omission varies based on the amount left, and he extends the same logic to the arrival tawaf. Understanding these gradations helps you apply the correct penalty in Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
The act is tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf). Its hukm is wajib (not rukn). This is stated indirectly: the commentary says it is wajib and distinguishes it from the rukn tawaf of ziyarah.
In Hanafi, wajib means obligatory but with a zanni proof, while rukn is fundamental and fard-like.
2
Differentiate between omitting most/all vs a little
For all or most of the circuits: required penalty is dam (one sheep sacrifice). For a little (less than half): required penalty is sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat per circuit left). The threshold 'most' is defined as more than half of the circuits.
The passage uses 'akthar' (most) versus 'aqall' (little).
3
Contrast with rukn tawaf (ziyarah/umrah)
For a rukn tawaf, even leaving a little portion requires a dam because the rukn is stronger and its omission invalidates the act unless compensated with a dam in the case of Hajj. The passage notes that the rukn is 'stronger' (aqwa) than the wajib.
This distinction highlights the Hanafi hierarchy of fard, wajib, and rukn.
4
Learn the ruling for impurity states
If one performs the farewell tawaf (or arrival tawaf) with minor impurity (hadath), a sadaqah is due; if with major impurity (janabah), a dam is due. This is based on the expression of al-Majma' preferred by the commentator.
The same ruling applies to both tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-sadr according to al-Majma'.
5
Understand the effect of later performance
If the pilgrim returns and performs the omitted circuits (or repeats the tawaf correctly), no penalty is due because the farewell tawaf is not time-bound like a rukn. However, the Hidayah recommends repeating the tawaf immediately while still in Makkah to fulfill the wajib in its proper time.
This means the penalty is waived if the omission is rectified before leaving Makkah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو ترك أكثر الصدر أو طافه جنباً وصدقة بترك أقله) أي يجب الدم ولما كان طواف الصدر واجباً وجب بترك كله أو أكثره دم، وبترك أقله صدقة لكل شوط نصف صاع من بر تفرقة بين الأكثر والأقل بخلاف الأقل من طواف الزيارة والعمرة حيث يجب دم بتركه لأنه طواف ركن فكان أقوى من الواجب، وقد قدمنا حكم ما إذا طاف للصدر جنباً لكن في عبارته قصور حيث لم يبين حكم طواف القدوم جنباً، وعبارة المجمع أولى وهي: وإن طاف للقدوم أو للصدر محدثاً وجبت صدقة وجنباً دم فأفاد أنه لا فرق بينهما في الحدثين . وأشار بالترك إلى أنه لو أتى بما تركه فإنه لا يلزمه شيء مطلقاً لأنه ليس بمؤقت، وفي الهداية ويؤمر بالإعادة ما دام بمكة إقامة للواجب في وقته
His statement: 'Or he left most of the farewell (tawaf) or performed it while junub, and charity for leaving a little of it' means: The blood (sacrifice) is obligatory. Since the farewell tawaf is wajib, leaving all or most of it necessitates a dam, and leaving a little necessitates a sadaqah: half a sa' of wheat per circuit, distinguishing between most and little, unlike the little of the tawaf of visitation (ziyarah) and Umrah where leaving it necessitates a dam because it is a rukn tawaf, so it is stronger than the wajib. We have already presented the ruling for when one performs the farewell tawaf while junub, but there is deficiency in his expression for not clarifying the ruling for the arrival tawaf (qudum) while junub. The expression of al-Majma' is more appropriate: 'And if he performs the arrival or farewell tawaf in a state of minor impurity, a sadaqah is obligatory, and if junub, a dam.' So he indicated that there is no difference between them regarding the two impurities. And he indicated by 'leaving' that if he performs what he left, nothing is due from him at all because it is not time-bound. In al-Hidayah: 'And he is ordered to repeat it as long as he is in Makkah to establish the wajib in its time.'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling on penalties related to the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr). The commentator explains that since the farewell tawaf is wajib (obligatory, but not a rukn), neglecting all or most of it requires a dam (a sheep sacrifice). Neglecting only a small part (less than half) requires a sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat per circuit left. This distinguishes it from the tawaf al-ziyarah, which is a rukn; even a small omission of a rukn requires a dam because the rukn is stronger than a wajib. The commentator then notes that the matn's expression was incomplete because it did not address the arrival tawaf (qudum). He clarifies using al-Majma' that both the arrival and farewell tawaf have the same ruling: if performed with minor impurity (hadath), a sadaqah is due; if with major impurity (janabah), a dam is due. The commentator also explains that if one returns and performs the omitted part, no penalty is due because the farewell tawaf is not time-bound (like a rukn), but al-Hidayah recommends repeating it while still in Makkah to fulfill the wajib in its proper time.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Makkah, which is wajib.
دم (Dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for leaving a wajib or committing a violation in Hajj.
صدقة (Sadaqah): Here, a charity of half a sa' of wheat per circuit, given as a penalty for a minor omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pilgrim leaves 4 of the 7 circuits of the farewell tawaf. What is the required penalty in the Hanafi school?
A) Nothing, if he returns to complete them
B) Sadaqah of half a sa' per circuit
C) One dam
D) One dam per circuit

Key Takeaway
The farewell tawaf is wajib; omitting most requires a dam, omitting a little requires sadaqah, and performing it while junub requires a dam.

Penalties for Impurity in Tawaf and the Dispute on Transfer
Ruling on tawaf penalties with naql dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on blood sacrifices when the pillar tawaf is performed with impurity and the farewell tawaf in purity at the end of Tashriq, and explain why Abu Hanifah does not allow transfer of the farewell tawaf to the pillar tawaf in this case.

Core Idea
Transfer (naql) of tawaf is only valid when it removes a penalty; if the delay itself already requires a dam, transfer offers no benefit and is invalid.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific hajj scenario involving two tawaf acts and potential penalties. It distinguishes between minor and major impurity during the pillar tawaf, and discusses whether the farewell tawaf can be transferred to compensate for the impurity. The dispute between Abu Hanifah and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hinges on the concept of benefit (fa'idah) in the transfer. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the interplay between timing, impurity, and the legal mechanism of naql.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn presents two cases: (1) pillar tawaf with minor impurity (hadath) and farewell tawaf in purity at end of Tashriq – one sheep due; (2) pillar tawaf junub and farewell tawaf in purity at end of Tashriq – two sheep due.
The second case involves major impurity (janabah), which requires a badanah originally, but here it is commuted to two sheep.
2
Understand the concept of naql (transfer)
Naql is the legal transfer of the status of one tawaf to another. In hajj, if the farewell tawaf (wajib) is performed earlier than required, it can be counted as the pillar tawaf (rukn) if there is benefit, i.e., it cancels a penalty.
Transfer is only allowed if it results in waiving a blood sacrifice.
3
Analyze the ruling when farewell tawaf is in the days of Nahr
If the farewell tawaf is done during the days of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) and the pilgrim has not left Makkah, transfer is beneficial because it removes the impurity penalty and no delay penalty applies yet.
Transfer is allowed by all in this case.
4
Examine the dispute at the end of Tashriq
When farewell tawaf is performed in the last days of Tashriq (11th-13th), Abu Hanifah says no transfer because delaying the farewell tawaf itself already requires a dam (for delay), so transfer does not eliminate any penalty; the Sahibayn allow transfer because it still removes the impurity penalty.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifah, two dams due; under Sahibayn, one dam saved.
5
Review the three riwayat on repeating after Tashriq
The passage also discusses what happens if the farewell tawaf is repeated after Tashriq. Three narrations exist: (1) from al-Hidayah: nothing for minor impurity, dam for major; (2) from al-Tahawi: dam for both; (3) from al-Walwaliji: sadaqah for minor. The mufta bihi is the first.
This shows the richness of the Hanafi tradition and the process of tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو طاف للركن محدثاً وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق ودمان لو طاف للركن جنباً) أي تجب شاة في الأولى وشاتان في الثانية. أما في الأولى فهي بسبب الحدث ولم ينقل طواف الصدر إلى الزيارة لأنه لا فائدة في النقل لأنه لو نقل يجب عليه الدم لترك طواف الصدر إجماعاً إن كان رجع إلى أهله أو لا قيد بقوله في آخر أيام التشريق» لأنه لو طاف للصدر في أيام النحر ولم يرجع إلى أهله فإنه ينقل طواف الصدر إلى طواف الزيارة لأن في النقل فائدة وهو سقوط الدم لأجل الحدث ثم يطوف للصدر ولا شيء عليه بخلاف ما إذا طاف للصدر في آخر أيام التشريق ولم يرجع إلى أهله حيث لا ينقل عند أبي حنيفة لأنه لا فائدة في النقل لوجوب دم للتأخير على تقديره خلافاً لهما. وأما في الثانية فلان في النقل وهي سقوط البدنة فيجب دم لتأخيره عن أيام النحر عنده، ودم لترك طواف الصدر إن رجع إلى أهله وإن كان بمكة فإنه يطوف للصدر ولا يلزمه إلا دم واحد للتأخير، فإن كان طاف للصدر في أيام النحر فإنه ينقل إلى طواف الزيارة ثم يطوف للصدر ولا شيء عليه أصلاً. قيد بكون الطواف الثاني للصدر لأنه لو أعاده بعد أيام النحر، فإن كان في الحدث الأصغر لا يلزمه شيء لأن بعد الإعادة لا يبقى إلا شبهة النقصان، وفي الحدث الأكبر يلزمه دم . عند أبي حنيفة للتأخير. كذا في الهداية. وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأنه سهو لأن الرواية مسطورة في شرح الطحاوي أنه يلزمه الدم إذا أعاده بعد أيام النحر للتأخير، سواء كان بسبب الحدث أو الجنابة ا.هـ. وهكذا في المحيط سوى بين الحدثين وهذا قصور نظر من صاحب الغاية لأن في المسألة ثلاث روايات؛ فما في الهداية رواية عن أبي حنيفة ذكرها الإمام الولوالجي في فتاواه وصدر بها واعتمدها، وما في شرح الطحاوي والمحيط رواية ثانية، وذكر الولوالجي أيضاً رواية ثالثة عن أبي حنيفة أن عليه الصدقة في الحدث الأصغر، ووجهها بأنه أخر الجبر عن وقت الطواف فيبقى نوع نقص لكن نقصان التأخير دون نقصان ترك القضاء والواجب بترك القضاء هو الدم فكان الواجب بتأخير القضاء هو الصدقة ا هـ .
His statement: 'Or he performed the pillar (tawaf) while in a state of minor impurity, and the farewell (tawaf) while pure in the last days of Tashriq, and two bloods if he performed the pillar tawaf while junub' means: one sheep is due in the first case, and two sheep in the second. As for the first, it is due to the impurity, and the farewell tawaf is not transferred to the ziyarah tawaf because there is no benefit in transfer, because if he transfers, he must pay a blood (dam) for leaving the farewell tawaf unanimously, whether he returned to his family or not. He restricted it with his statement 'in the last days of Tashriq' because if he performed the farewell tawaf during the days of Nahr and did not return to his family, then he transfers the farewell tawaf to the ziyarah tawaf because in the transfer there is benefit, namely the falling away of the blood for the impurity; then he performs the farewell tawaf and nothing is due on him, contrary to when he performed the farewell tawaf in the last days of Tashriq and did not return to his family, where he does not transfer according to Abu Hanifah because there is no benefit in transfer due to the obligation of blood for delay on that assumption, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). As for the second (case), the blood is due because of the transfer, which is the falling away of the badanah, so one blood is due for the delay beyond the days of Nahr according to him, and one blood for leaving the farewell tawaf if he returned to his family. But if he is in Makkah, he performs the farewell tawaf and nothing is due on him except one blood for the delay. If he performed the farewell tawaf during the days of Nahr, then he transfers it to the ziyarah tawaf, then performs the farewell tawaf and nothing is due on him at all. He restricted it with the second tawaf being the farewell tawaf because if he repeated it after the days of Nahr, then if it was due to minor impurity, nothing is due on him because after the repetition nothing remains but the semblance of deficiency; but in the case of major impurity, a blood is due according to Abu Hanifah for the delay. Thus in al-Hidayah. But it was refuted in Ghayat al-Bayan as a mistake, because the narration is recorded in Sharh al-Tahawi that the blood is due if he repeats after the days of Nahr for the delay, whether due to minor impurity or janabah. And likewise in al-Muhit, making no distinction between the two impurities, and this is a deficiency of consideration from the author of al-Ghayah, because in this issue there are three narrations: what is in al-Hidayah is a narration from Abu Hanifah mentioned by Imam al-Walwaliji in his Fatawa, and he began with it and relied on it; and what is in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Muhit is a second narration; and al-Walwaliji also mentioned a third narration from Abu Hanifah that he owes sadaqah in the case of minor impurity, its reasoning being that he delayed the compensation beyond the time of the tawaf, so a type of deficiency remains, but the deficiency of delay is less than the deficiency of leaving the recompense, and the obligation for leaving the recompense is blood, so the obligation for delaying the recompense is sadaqah. End quote.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage delves into a complex scenario involving two types of tawaf: the pillar tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah, a rukn) and the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr, a wajib). The matn states that if one performs the pillar tawaf while in a state of minor impurity (hadath) and then performs the farewell tawaf in a state of purity at the end of the days of Tashriq, one sheep (a dam) is due. But if the pillar tawaf was performed while junub (major impurity), then two sheep are due. The commentator explains the reasoning. In the first case, the single dam is solely due to the impurity during the pillar tawaf. The farewell tawaf cannot be 'transferred' (naql) to become a substitute for the pillar tawaf because the pillar tawaf is a rukn and already performed (though with impurity), and transferring would cause a deficiency in the farewell tawaf, which is wajib. However, if the farewell tawaf was performed during the days of Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah) and the pilgrim has not yet returned to his family, then there is benefit in transferring: the farewell tawaf counts as a valid pillar tawaf (if done with intention), and the impurity violation is wiped out, so only the farewell tawaf remains to be performed again without penalty. But in the last days of Tashriq, Abu Hanifah says no transfer occurs because delaying the farewell tawaf until then itself necessitates a dam for delay, so transfer loses benefit. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree and allow transfer even then. In the second case (pillar tawaf junub), two dams are due: one for performing the pillar tawaf in major impurity (which requires a badanah? Actually the text says 'squat al-badanah' meaning the original obligation of a camel? But it says one dam for delay and one for leaving farewell tawaf if returning home). The commentator also discusses a nuanced ikhtilaf about what happens if the pilgrim repeats the farewell tawaf after the days of Tashriq. There are three narrations: (1) al-Hidayah reports from Abu Hanifah that if the impurity was minor, nothing is due after repetition; if major, a dam is due for delay. (2) Another narration from Abu Hanifah (in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Muhit) says a dam is due in both cases for delay. (3) A third narration says a sadaqah is due in the minor impurity case. The commentator sides with the first, as relied upon by al-Walwaliji.

Key Terms
نقل (Naql): Transferring the reward or legal status of one tawaf to another, here the farewell tawaf to the pillar tawaf to avoid penalties.
أيام التشريق (Ayyam al-Tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, the days after Eid al-Adha.
بدنة (Badanah): A camel sacrifice; the text mentions 'squat al-badanah' meaning the obligation of a camel for a major violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, why is the farewell tawaf not transferred to the pillar tawaf when performed in the last days of Tashriq?
A) Because the farewell tawaf is a rukn and cannot be transferred
B) Because there is no benefit: the delay already requires a dam
C) Because the impurity must be removed first
D) Because the pilgrim must remain in Makkah

Key Takeaway
Transfer of tawaf is a mechanism to avoid penalties, but it only operates when it provides a genuine benefit; otherwise, the original penalties remain due.
