The Penalty for Tawaf and Sa'y in Impurity Without Repetition
Explains the penalty for performing both tawaf and sa'y of Umrah in impurity without repetition, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on repeating tawaf only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing tawaf and sa'y of Umrah in impurity without repetition, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on repeating only tawaf.

Core Idea
Performing tawaf and sa'y in impurity without repetition requires a dam; repeating tawaf alone may or may not void the penalty.

In Hanafi fiqh, purity is a necessary condition (wajib) for tawaf, and sa'y must follow a valid tawaf. If a pilgrim performs both in a state of minor impurity and does not repeat them, a dam is due. However, if he repeats the tawaf while pure, the deficiency may be removed, but scholars differ on whether the sa'y performed before the repeated tawaf is still valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition omitted
The act is performing tawaf and sa'y for Umrah while in hadath (minor impurity). The omitted condition is purity (taharah), which is wajib for tawaf and for the sa'y to follow the tawaf in purity.
Purity for tawaf is a condition according to the sahih view; for sa'y, it is wajib to perform after a pure tawaf.
2
State the base ruling
If both tawaf and sa'y are done in impurity and the pilgrim does not repeat them, a dam (one sheep) is wajib for leaving the wajib.
This is the default ruling in the passage.
3
Introduce the exception and the dispute
If the pilgrim repeats the tawaf (while pure) but not the sa'y, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: some say no dam is due; others say a dam is still due.
The passage examines both views and resolves in favour of no dam.
4
Understand the reasoning behind each view
View 1 (Shams al-A'imma, al-Hidayah): No dam because the repeated tawaf serves as a jabir (compensatory act) removing the deficiency. View 2 (many mashayikh): Dam because the repetition nullifies the first tawaf, making the sa'y precede a valid tawaf, violating the order (sa'y must be after tawaf).
The concept of jabir is key in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The preferred view adopted by al-Hidayah, al-Nahr, and the author of al-Kanz is that no dam is due when only tawaf is repeated.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو طاف لعمرته وسعى محدثاً ولم يعد أي تجب شاة لتركه الواجب وهو الطهارة. قيد بقوله ولم يعد لأنه لو أعاد الطواف ظاهراً فإنه لا يلزمه شيء لارتفاع النقصان أيام التشريق قوله : (لأنه لو أعاده أي أعاد الركن قوله : (قيد بقوله ولم يعد) مقتضى جعله ذلك قيداً أن الواو فيه للحال كما هو ظاهر كلام الزيلعي و به صرح مسكين ثم قال: وإن أعادهما لا شيء، وإن أعاد الطواف ولم يعد السعي قيل لا شيء عليه في الصحيح، وقيل عليه دما واختار الأول شمس الأئمة كما ذكره الزيلعي تبعاً لتصحيح الهداية لكن قال في غاية البيان: وأكثر مشايخنا في شروح الجامع الصغير على خلاف ما ذهب إليه صاحب الهداية حيث قالوا : إذا أعاد الطواف ولم يعد السعي كان عليه لأن الإعادة تجعل المؤدى كأن لم يكن من وجه فيبقى السعي قبل الطواف وذلك خلاف المشروع لأن المشروع في السعي أن يكون بعد الطواف ا هـ. قال في النهر : والأصح عدم وجوبه ولا نسلم انتقاض المؤدي بل معتد به والثاني يعتد به جابراً للدم، ولما كان جعل الواو للحال كما هو ظاهر ما في الشرح يلزم عليه المشي على مرجوح عدل العيني عنه فقال: أي ليس عليه إعادتهما لما علمت من أنها مندوبة فقط، وعندي أن هذا الحل أجل ا هـ. وحيث مشى المؤلف على ما في الهداية فالمناسب أن يجعل قوله ولم يعد كلاماً مستأنفاً كما في العيني
His statement: 'Or he performed tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y while in a state of minor impurity and did not repeat' means: a sheep is due for his leaving the wajib, which is purity. He restricted it with his statement 'and did not repeat' because if he repeats the tawaf apparently, nothing is due from him due to the removal of the deficiency... The implication of making it a condition is that the waw is for the state (hal) as is apparent from the statement of al-Zayla'i, and Muskin explicitly stated it. Then he said: 'And if he repeats both, nothing is due. And if he repeats the tawaf but not the sa'y, it is said: nothing is due on him according to the sahih; and it is said: a dam is due on him.' Shams al-A'imma chose the first, as al-Zayla'i mentioned following the tashih of al-Hidayah. But it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'Most of our mashayikh in the commentaries of al-Jami' al-Saghir are contrary to what the author of al-Hidayah held, for they said: If he repeats the tawaf but not the sa'y, a dam is due, because the repetition makes the performed (tawaf) as if it never existed in one sense, so the sa'y remains before the tawaf, and that is contrary to the legislated order (sa'y after tawaf).' Al-Nahr said: 'The more correct is that nothing is due, and we do not accept that the performed (tawaf) is nullified; rather it is valid, and the second (tawaf) is valid as a reparatory (jabir) for the blood.' And since making the waw for the state as apparent in the sharh would require acting upon a weak opinion, al-Ayni departed from it and said: 'It means he is not required to repeat both, as you know that they are only recommended.' And in my view this solution is more excellent. End quote. Since the author proceeded according to what is in al-Hidayah, it is appropriate to make his statement 'and did not repeat' a new clause (musta'naf) as in al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific violation in Umrah: performing both the tawaf and sa'y while in a state of minor impurity (hadath) and not repeating them afterwards. The ruling is that a dam (one sheep) is due because the pilgrim omitted the wajib of purity during both acts. However, the commentator restricts this to the case where he does not repeat the tawaf; if he does repeat it (while in purity), the deficiency is removed and no penalty is due. The discussion then turns to what happens if he repeats only the tawaf but not the sa'y. There is an ikhtilaf: the preferred view (sahih) according to Shams al-A'imma and al-Hidayah is that nothing is due, because the repeated tawaf compensates for the impurity. But many other Hanafi scholars (from commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir) hold that a dam is still due because the repetition effectively cancels the first tawaf, making the sa'y (which was performed after an impure tawaf) come before the valid tawaf, which is against the proper order (sa'y should be after tawaf). The commentator notes that al-Nahr considers the first tawaf still valid and the second as a reparatory act, so nothing extra is due. Al-Ayni resolves the issue by reinterpreting the phrase 'and did not repeat' as an independent statement meaning he is not required to repeat both (the tawaf and sa'y) because repeating them is only recommended, not obligatory. The commentator concludes that the author follows al-Hidayah, and thus the wording should be understood as a new clause.

Key Terms
سعي (Sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah, which is a rukn of Hajj and Umrah.
جابر (Jabir): A reparatory act that compensates for a deficiency; here the repeated tawaf serves as a jabir for the impurity blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Hidayah, if a pilgrim repeats the tawaf of Umrah (performed earlier in impurity) but does not repeat the sa'y, what is the ruling?
A) A dam is due for the sa'y performed before a valid tawaf
B) Nothing is due because the repeated tawaf repairs the deficiency
C) He must repeat the sa'y as well
D) He must sacrifice a camel

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, purity is wajib for tawaf; if both tawaf and sa'y are done in impurity, a dam is due unless the tawaf is repeated, in which case the preferred view absolves the penalty.

Three Narrations on Dam for Delay in Tawaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam for delaying tawaf compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrations from Abu Hanifa on dam for delaying tawaf compensation and identify which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Three narrations, one ruling: Abu Hanifa's students preserved variant views on dam for delay; the mufta bihi requires dam only for major impurity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about the penalty for delaying the compensation (jabr) of a tawaf performed in impurity. The text presents three narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa that differ on whether a dam (blood sacrifice) or sadaqah (charity) is required, and whether the severity of impurity matters. Understanding these narrations is essential for correctly issuing fatwa in Hajj-related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
What is the act that triggers a potential penalty? It is delaying the compensation tawaf (performed after impurity) beyond the days of sacrifice.
The compensation tawaf is a wajib act that must be performed after a tawaf done in impurity.
2
State the Three Narrations
According to the passage, there are three narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) dam for major impurity only, (2) dam for both impurities, (3) sadaqah for minor impurity.
These narrations are preserved by later scholars like al-Walwalji.
3
Understand the Rationale
The justification for each narration is based on the degree of deficiency: major impurity is more severe, so it requires a heavier penalty.
Sadaqah is lighter than dam because delay is a lesser deficiency than complete omission.
4
Identify the Mufta Bihi
Imam al-Walwalji relied on the narration from al-Hidayah (dam only for major impurity) as the operative position.
This is the preferred ruling for fatwa.
5
Note the Practical Consequence
In practice, a person who repeats the tawaf after the days of sacrifice and was in minor impurity owes nothing; if in major impurity, a dam is required.
This distinguishes between the severity of the two states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

A benefit regarding the transmission for the obligation of a blood (penalty) for delay, based on his estimation, contrary to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). As for the second, it is because in the transmission, it is that the camel is dropped, so a blood (penalty) is obligatory for delaying it beyond the days of sacrifice according to him, and a blood (penalty) for leaving the farewell tawaf if he returns to his family; but if he is in Makkah, he performs tawaf for farewell and nothing is required except one blood (penalty) for delay. If he performed the farewell tawaf during the days of sacrifice, then it is transferred to the tawaf of visitation, then he performs the farewell tawaf and nothing is required at all. It is restricted to the second tawaf being for farewell because if he repeats it after the days of sacrifice, then if he was in minor impurity, nothing is required because after repetition only a semblance of deficiency remains, and in major impurity, a blood (penalty) is required according to Abu Hanifa for delay. Thus in al-Hidayah. It was critiqued in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is a mistake because the narration is recorded in Sharh al-Tahawi that the blood (penalty) is required if he repeats after the days of sacrifice for delay, whether due to minor or major impurity. End quote. Similarly, in al-Muhit it equates the two impurities, and this is a lack of insight from the author of al-Ghayah because there are three narrations in the issue. What is in al-Hidayah is a narration from Abu Hanifa mentioned by Imam al-Walwalji in his Fatawa, and he began with it and relied on it. What is in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Muhit is a second narration. Al-Walwalji also mentioned a third narration from Abu Hanifa that he must give charity in minor impurity, and its justification is that he delayed the compensation beyond the time of tawaf, so a type of deficiency remains, but the deficiency of delay is less than the deficiency of not repeating or leaving sa'i or departing from Arafat before leaving the duty; the duty for leaving the duty is blood, so the duty for delaying the duty is charity. End quote.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the penalty (dam) for delaying the compensation (jabr) of a tawaf performed in a state of impurity. The text begins by stating a ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa: if one delays the compensation beyond the days of sacrifice, a dam is obligatory. It then contrasts this with the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), who hold a different view. The author explains that according to one narration (from al-Hidayah), if one repeats the tawaf after the days of sacrifice, no penalty is required for minor impurity because repetition removes the deficiency, but for major impurity a dam is still required. However, this is contested by Ghayat al-Bayan, which claims it is a mistake, citing a narration from Sharh al-Tahawi that requires a dam regardless of the type of impurity. Al-Muhit also equates the two. The passage then clarifies that there are actually three narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) as in al-Hidayah (dam only for major impurity), (2) as in Sharh al-Tahawi (dam for both), and (3) that sadaqah (charity) is required for minor impurity. The justification for sadaqah is that delaying the compensation is a lesser deficiency than omitting it entirely. The author concludes by stating that the duty for leaving the duty is blood, but for delay it is charity. This reflects the Hanafi principle of distinguishing between different levels of deficiency.

Key Terms
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (penalty) required for specific violations in Hajj/Umrah.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charitable payment as a penalty for minor deficiencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing
B) A dam
C) Sadaqah
D) A camel

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi ruling is that delaying compensation after major impurity requires a dam; after minor impurity and repetition, no penalty.

Penalty for Umrah Tawaf in Impurity and the Effect of Repeating
Commentary on the ruling for performing Umrah tawaf in impurity and the effect of repeating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi penalty for performing Umrah tawaf in a state of impurity and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether repeating the tawaf removes the penalty.

Core Idea
A shah is wajib for Umrah tawaf in impurity; repeating the tawaf may remove it, but the sa'i order is critical.

This lesson examines the penalty for performing Umrah tawaf without purity. The Hanafi school holds that purity is a wajib of tawaf, and leaving it incurs a shah. However, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on whether repeating the tawaf (with or without sa'i) eliminates the penalty. We will trace the reasoning from al-Hidayah and later commentaries, and also see how major impurity (janabah) is treated by istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for impurity in Umrah tawaf
The matn states that if one performs Umrah tawaf in minor impurity (hadath) and does not repeat, a shah is wajib because purity is a wajib.
2
Understand the condition 'and did not repeat'
The restriction shows that if one repeats the tawaf, the penalty is lifted because the deficiency is removed.
This is the key to the dispute.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on repeating only tawaf
The preferred view (al-Hidayah) says no penalty remains; but many later scholars (Ghayat al-Bayan) argue that a penalty is still due because the repetition nullifies the original tawaf, making sa'i precede tawaf.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether a shah is due.
4
Examine the application of istihsan for major impurity
By analogy (qiyas), janabah would require a camel, but istihsan allows a shah because Umrah tawaf is less important than tawaf al-ziyarah.
Two factors: importance of tawaf and severity of janabah.
5
Differentiate the qarin's case
A qarin who performs tawaf in impurity before the day of sacrifice can repeat the Umrah tawaf without penalty; after that, a dam is due. For janabah, if not repeated, a dam for sa'i is due.
The qarin cannot repeat tawaf after standing at Arafat.

وقيل عليه دما واختار الأول شمس الأئمة كما ذكره الزيلعي تبعاً لتصحيح الهداية لكن قال في غاية البيان: وأكثر مشايخنا في شروح الجامع الصغير على خلاف ما ذهب إليه صاحب الهداية حيث قالوا : إذا أعاد الطواف طواف التحية كما قدمناه مصرحاً به عن الولوالجية قوله : (لأنه لو طاف أقله محدثاً الخ) ذكر مثله في السراج لكنه دم بالإعادة، ولا يؤمر بالعود إذا رجع إلى أهله لوقوع التحلل بأداء الركن مع الحلق والنقصان يسير، وما دام بمكة يعيد الطواف لأنه الأصل والأفضل أن يعيد السعي لأنه تبع للطواف ، وإن لم يعده فلا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح لأن الطهارة ليست بشرط في السعي وقد وقع عقب طواف معتد به وإعادته لجبر النقصان كوجوب الدم لا لانفساخ الأول. ولو قال المصنف محدثاً أو جنباً لكان أولى لأنه لا فرق بين الحدثين في طواف العمرة كما في المحيط من فلا شيء وغيره، والقياس أنه لا يكتفي بالشاة فيما إذا طاف لعمرته جنباً لأن حكم الجناية أغلظ الحدث كما في طواف الزيارة لكن اكتفى بها استحساناً لأن طواف الزيارة فوق طواف العمرة. وإيجاب أغلظ الدماء وهو البدنة في طواف الزيارة كان لمعنيين: وكادة الطواف وغلظ أمر الجنابة، فإذا وجد أحد المعنيين دون الثاني تعذر إيجاب أغلظ الدماء فاقتصرنا على الشاة. كذا في غاية البيان. وفي المحيط ولو طاف القارن طوافين وسعى سعيين محدثاً أعاد طواف العمرة قبل يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه للجبر بجنسه في وقته فإن لم يعد حتى طلع فجر يوم النحر لزمه دم لطواف العمرة محدثاً وقد فات وقت القضاء ويرمل في طواف الزيارة يوم النحر ويسعى بعده استحباباً ليحصل الرمل والسعي عقب طواف كامل، وإن لم يعد عليه لأنه سعی عقب طواف معتد به إذ الحدث الأصغر لا يمنع الاعتداد، وفي الجنابة إن لم يعد فعليه للسعي وكذا الحائض ا هـ . فالحاصل أن قولهم إن المعتمر يعيد الطواف» محله ما إذا لم يكن قارناً، أما في القارن إذا دخل يوم النحر فلا إعادة، وعلل له محمد كما نقله ابن بدار في شرح الجامع الصغير بأنه لو أعاده لانتقضت عمرته لأنه يصير رافضاً لها بالوقوف وقد تأكدت فلا يمكن استدراك النقص بجنسه فيجبر بالدم. قال ابن سماعة فقلت لمحمد : إنك قلت في الأصل إن القارن لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط وسعى ولم يطف لحجته حتى وقف إنه يتم طواف العمرة يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه فقد أوجبت الإتمام وما أوجبت الدم. قال محمد: لأن هناك قدم شيئاً على شيء، وهنا الفساد وجد في جميع الطواف فإن لم نجوز وأبطلنا طوافه لرفضنا عمرته بمنزلة من لم يطف ا هـ .
His saying: (or he performed tawaf for his Umrah and performed sa'i while in a state of minor impurity and did not repeat) i.e. a sheep is obligatory because he left the obligatory act, which is purity. He restricted it by saying 'and did not repeat' because if he repeats the tawaf apparently, then nothing is required of him because the deficiency is removed during the days of tashreeq. His saying: (because if he repeats it, i.e. repeats the pillar) His saying: (restricted by his saying 'and did not repeat') the implication of making that a restriction is that the waw is for the state (hal), as is apparent from the words of al-Zaylai and Maskeen explicitly stated it. Then he said: If he repeats both, nothing; if he repeats the tawaf but not the sa'i, it was said nothing is upon him according to the correct view, and it was said a dam is upon him, and Shams al-Aimmah chose the first as al-Zaylai mentioned following the verification of al-Hidayah. But in Ghayat al-Bayan, most of our teachers in the commentaries of al-Jami' al-Saghir are contrary to what the author of al-Hidayah held, for they said: if he repeats the tawaf but not the sa'i, a penalty is upon him because the repetition makes the performed act as if it had not occurred from one perspective, so the sa'i remains before the tawaf, and that is contrary to what is legislated because what is legislated for sa'i is that it occurs after the tawaf. End quote. It was said in al-Nahr: the more correct is that it is not obligatory, and we do not concede that the performed act is rescinded; rather it is valid, and the second is considered a compensation for the dam. And when making the waw for the state, as is apparent in the commentary, it necessitates following a weak view, so al-Ayni deviated from it and said: i.e., it is not upon him to repeat both, because you know that they are (the repetition) only recommended. And according to me, this solution is more appropriate. End quote. And since the author followed what is in al-Hidayah, it is more appropriate to make his words 'and did not repeat' a separate statement, as in al-Ayni. His saying: (and he performs ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah...) this statement with its reasoning indicates that the qarin performs ramal in the greeting tawaf, as we previously stated explicitly from al-Walwaljiyyah. His saying: (because if he performed its minimum while in minor impurity...) a similar example is mentioned in al-Siraj, but it is a blood (penalty) with repetition. And he is not commanded to return if he has returned to his family because the tahlul occurs by performing the pillar with shaving, and the deficiency is minor. And as long as he is in Makkah, he repeats the tawaf because it is the original, and it is better that he repeats the sa'i because it is a follower of the tawaf, and if he does not repeat it, nothing is upon him, and this is the correct view because purity is not a condition in sa'i, and it occurred after a valid tawaf, and its repetition is to compensate the deficiency like the obligation of blood, not to nullify the first. And if the author had said 'minor impurity or major impurity' it would have been better because there is no difference between the two impurities in Umrah tawaf, as in al-Muhit: 'from nothing else'. And by analogy, it is not sufficient to suffice with a sheep (shah) when he performs tawaf for his Umrah in a state of major impurity because the ruling of janabah is more severe than that of minor impurity, as in tawaf al-ziyarah, but it is sufficient by istihsan because tawaf al-ziyarah is superior to Umrah tawaf. And the obligation of the more severe blood (the camel) in tawaf al-ziyarah was for two reasons: the importance of the tawaf and the severity of janabah. So when one of the two reasons exists without the other, it is not possible to obligate the more severe blood, so we limited it to the shah. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Muhit: If the qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is in minor impurity, he repeats the Umrah tawaf before the day of sacrifice and nothing is upon him because the compensation is of the same kind within its time. If he does not repeat until the dawn of the day of sacrifice, a dam becomes obligatory for the Umrah tawaf performed in minor impurity because the time for replacement has passed. And he performs ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah on the day of sacrifice and performs sa'i after it as a recommendation to achieve ramal and sa'i after a complete tawaf. And if he does not repeat, it is upon him because he performed sa'i after a valid tawaf, since minor impurity does not prevent validity. And in the case of major impurity, if he does not repeat, a dam is upon him for the sa'i, and similarly for a menstruating woman. End quote. So the conclusion is that their saying 'the mutamir repeats the tawaf' applies only if he is not a qarin. As for the qarin when the day of sacrifice enters, there is no repetition. And Muhammad gave the reason for it, as related by Ibn Badar in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, that if he were to repeat it, his Umrah would be nullified because he becomes rejecting it by standing at Arafat, and it has become confirmed, so it is not possible to make up for the deficiency by its like; thus it is compensated by blood. Ibn Sama'ah said: I said to Muhammad: You said in al-Asl that if the qarin performs four circuits of tawaf and sa'i and does not perform tawaf for his Hajj until he stands at Arafat, that he completes the Umrah tawaf on the day of sacrifice and nothing is upon him. You obliged completion and did not oblige blood. Muhammad said: Because there, he performed something before something else, and here, the corruption occurred in the entire tawaf. If we do not validate and we nullify his tawaf, we would be rejecting his Umrah, and he becomes like one who did not perform tawaf. End quote.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling for someone who performs Umrah tawaf in a state of minor impurity (hadath) and does not repeat the tawaf. The author begins by explaining the matn: a sheep (shah) is obligatory because purity is a wajib condition. The restriction 'and did not repeat' indicates that if one repeats the tawaf, the penalty is lifted because the deficiency is removed. There is a discussion on whether repeating only the tawaf (not the sa'i) suffices. The preferred view (from al-Hidayah) is that no penalty remains, but many later Hanafi scholars (in Ghayat al-Bayan) hold that a penalty is still required because the repetition effectively nullifies the original tawaf, making the sa'i precede the tawaf, contrary to the prescribed order. Al-Ayni suggests that repetition is only recommended, so no penalty is due. The passage then extends the ruling to major impurity (janabah), stating that the same shah applies by istihsan, even though analogy would require a camel (as in tawaf al-ziyarah). The reasoning is that tawaf al-ziyarah has two factors (importance of the tawaf and severity of janabah), while Umrah tawaf lacks the first factor, so only a shah is due. The case of a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) is also discussed: if he performs both tawafs and sa'is in impurity, he may repeat only the Umrah tawaf before the day of sacrifice without penalty; after that, a dam is required. For janabah, if he does not repeat, a dam is due for the sa'i. The passage ends with a dialogue between Ibn Sama'ah and Imam Muhammad clarifying why a qarin cannot repeat tawaf after standing at Arafat.

Key Terms
شاة (shah): A sheep (or goat) required as a penalty for certain Hajj/Umrah violations.
قارن (qarin): A person performing Hajj and Umrah together (qiran).
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of minor impurity (hadath) requiring wudu.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Hidayah, what is the penalty for someone who performs Umrah tawaf in a state of minor impurity and does not repeat the tawaf?
A) A camel
B) A shah (sheep)
C) Sadaqah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A mutamir who performs Umrah tawaf in impurity owes a shah, but repeating the tawaf (and possibly sa'i) may cancel the penalty according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Penalties for Impurity and Omitted Shawts in Umrah Tawaf
Ruling on impurity and missing a shawt in Umrah tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalty for performing any part of Umrah tawaf in impurity and for leaving a shawt, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the minimum amount.

Core Idea
For Umrah tawaf, any impurity incurs a shah; leaving even one shawt incurs a dam.

This passage examines the penalties for performing Umrah tawaf while impure, focusing on whether the amount of tawaf or type of impurity affects the obligation. The author compares earlier views from al-Muhit with the unified position of al-Lubab, settling on a shah for any impurity and a dam for any missing shawt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and conditions
Determine what the ruling applies to: Umrah tawaf performed in a state of impurity (minor or major) or with a missing shawt.
The key distinction is between impurity during tawaf and omission of a shawt.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
Separate the ruling for impurity while performing tawaf (any amount) from the ruling for leaving a shawt (performing fewer than seven).
The penalty for impurity is a shah; for a missing shawt it's a dam.
3
Compare the intra-Hanafi views on minimum in minor impurity
Examine the earlier position (al-Muhit) that requires half a sa' per shawt if the minimum is performed in minor impurity, versus al-Lubab's unified view that requires a shah regardless of amount or type.
Al-Lubab's view is the mufta bihi.
4
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
Conclude that for any amount of Umrah tawaf (even one shawt) in any impurity, a shah is obligatory; for leaving a shawt, a dam is obligatory, but it drops if the shawt is repeated.
This simplifies the earlier distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بكون طواف العمرة كله محدثاً والأكثر كالكل لأنه لو طاف أقله محدثاً وجب عليه لكل شوط نصف صاع من حنطة إلا إذا بلغت قيمته دماً فينقص منه ما شاء، ولو طاف أقله جنباً وجب عليه دم وتجب الإعادة في مخالف لما في الفتح عن المحيط ونصه : لو طاف للعمرة جنباً أو محدثاً فعليه شاة، ولو ترك من طواف العمرة شوطاً فعليه دم لأنه لا مدخل للصدقة في العمرة ا هـ . وفي اللباب : ولو طاف للعمرة كله أو أكثره أو أقله ولو شوطاً جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء أو محدثاً فعليه شاة، لا فرق فيه بين الكثير والقليل والجنب والمحدث لأنه لا مدخل في طواف العمرة للبدنة ولا للصدقة بخلاف طواف الزيارة، وكذا لو ترك منه أي من طواف العمرة أقله ولو شوطاً فعليه دم وإن أعاده سقط عنه الدم ا هـ.
And it is restricted that the entire Umrah tawaf is in minor impurity, and the majority is like the whole because if he performs its minimum in minor impurity, for each shawt half a sa' of wheat is obligatory unless its value reaches a dam, then he may deduct from it as he wishes. And if he performs its minimum in major impurity, a dam is obligatory upon him, and repetition is obligatory contrary to what is in al-Fath from al-Muhit, and its text: If he performs tawaf for Umrah in major impurity or minor impurity, upon him is a shah, and if he leaves one shawt of Umrah tawaf, upon him is a dam because there is no room for sadaqah in Umrah. End quote. And in al-Lubab: If he performs tawaf for Umrah entirely, or most of it, or the minimum of it, even one shawt, in major impurity or menstruation or post-childbirth or minor impurity, upon him is a shah; there is no difference between much and little, major impurity and minor impurity because there is no room in Umrah tawaf for a camel nor for sadaqah, contrary to tawaf al-ziyarah. Similarly, if he leaves from it, i.e., from Umrah tawaf, the minimum of it, even one shawt, upon him is a dam, and if he repeats it, the dam is dropped. End quote.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage clarifies the penalty for performing only part of the Umrah tawaf (less than the full seven circuits) while in a state of impurity. The author first states a restriction: the ruling that a shah is obligatory applies only if the entire tawaf is done in impurity; the majority (more than half) is treated like the whole. If one performs the minimum (less than a full tawaf) in minor impurity, the penalty is half a sa' of wheat per shawt, unless the total value reaches that of a dam, in which case one may deduct. If the minimum is performed in major impurity, a dam is obligatory, and repetition is required. However, the author notes a contrary view from al-Fath and al-Muhit, which hold that whether the impurity is minor or major, a shah is obligatory for the entire tawaf (or any part), and if one leaves a shawt (i.e., performs less than seven), the penalty is a dam because sadaqah does not apply in Umrah. The passage then cites al-Lubab, which unifies the ruling: for any amount of tawaf (even one shawt) performed in any impurity (minor, major, menstruation, postnatal), a shah is obligatory; there is no distinction because neither a camel (badanah) nor sadaqah applies to Umrah tawaf, unlike tawaf al-ziyarah. Additionally, if one leaves a shawt (i.e., performs only six or fewer), a dam is obligatory, but if one repeats the missing shawt, the dam is dropped.

Key Terms
شوط (shawt): One circuit of tawaf around the Ka'bah; seven shawts complete one tawaf.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or large animal used as a sacrifice in Hajj; a heavier penalty than shah.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required as expiation for certain violations in Hajj/Umrah.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat offered as sacrifice; a lighter penalty than dam?

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Lubab, what is the penalty for someone who performs three shawts (out of seven) of Umrah tawaf in a state of minor impurity?
A) Half a sa' of wheat
B) A shah (sheep)
C) A dam (blood)
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Umrah tawaf, any impurity (minor or major) in any portion requires a shah; leaving a shawt requires a dam, which drops if the shawt is repeated.

Tawaf al-Umrah with Impurity: Validity and Expiation
Explains the ruling and istihsan for tawaf al-umrah in impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for tawaf al-umrah performed while in a state of minor or major impurity, and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in determining the required expiation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-umrah with impurity is valid but requires a sheep, not a camel, due to lower emphasis.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi hajj jurisprudence: the difference between tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-umrah regarding expiation for impurity. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how the school uses istihsan to arrive at a lenient ruling for 'Umrah, acknowledging its lesser status compared to the Hajj tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is performing tawaf of 'Umrah while in a state of hadath (minor or major impurity). The Hanafi ruling: the tawaf is valid (sahih) but requires a blood expiation.
The expiation is a sheep (shah) for the entire tawaf, regardless of the type of impurity.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
By strict analogy (qiyas), janabah in any tawaf would require a camel (badanah) because janabah is a severe impurity, similar to tawaf al-ziyarah where a camel is due.
This would be the ruling if qiyas were applied without modification.
3
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to rule that a sheep suffices. The reason is that tawaf al-ziyarah has two elements: the strong emphasis (wukadah) of the tawaf and the severity of janabah. Tawaf al-umrah lacks the wukadah, so only one element is present, making a lesser expiation appropriate.
Istihsan is a primary source in Hanafi usul, often overriding qiyas when there is a stronger indication.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a sheep is due for tawaf al-umrah performed in any state of impurity (junub, muhdith, ha'id, nufasa'). This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as stated in al-Lubab.
There is no distinction between much or little impurity; a sheep covers all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الجنايات
بالإعادة، ولا يؤمر بالعود إذا رجع إلى أهله لوقوع التحلل بأداء الركن مع الحلق والنقصان يسير، وما دام بمكة يعيد الطواف لأنه الأصل والأفضل أن يعيد السعي لأنه تبع للطواف ، وإن لم يعده فلا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح لأن الطهارة ليست بشرط في السعي وقد وقع عقب طواف معتد به وإعادته لجبر النقصان كوجوب الدم لا لانفساخ الأول. ولو قال المصنف محدثاً أو جنباً لكان أولى لأنه لا فرق بين الحدثين في طواف العمرة كما في المحيط وغيره، والقياس أنه لا يكتفي بالشاة فيما إذا طاف لعمرته جنباً لأن حكم الجناية أغلظ الحدث كما في طواف الزيارة لكن اكتفى بها استحساناً لأن طواف الزيارة فوق طواف العمرة. وإيجاب أغلظ الدماء وهو البدنة في طواف الزيارة كان لمعنيين: وكادة الطواف وغلظ أمر الجنابة، فإذا وجد أحد المعنيين دون الثاني تعذر إيجاب أغلظ الدماء فاقتصرنا على الشاة. كذا في غاية البيان. وفي المحيط ولو طاف القارن طوافين وسعى سعيين محدثاً أعاد طواف العمرة قبل يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه للجبر بجنسه في وقته فإن لم يعد حتى طلع فجر يوم النحر لزمه دم لطواف العمرة محدثاً وقد فات وقت القضاء ويرمل في طواف الزيارة يوم النحر ويسعى بعده استحباباً ليحصل الرمل والسعي عقب طواف كامل، وإن لم يعد عليه لأنه سعی عقب طواف معتد به إذ الحدث الأصغر لا يمنع الاعتداد، وفي الجنابة إن لم يعد فعليه للسعي وكذا الحائض ا هـ . فالحاصل أن قولهم إن المعتمر يعيد الطواف» محله ما إذا لم يكن قارناً، أما في القارن إذا دخل يوم النحر فلا إعادة، وعلل له محمد كما نقله ابن بدار في شرح الجامع الصغير بأنه لو أعاده لانتقضت عمرته لأنه يصير رافضاً لها بالوقوف وقد تأكدت فلا يمكن استدراك النقص بجنسه فيجبر بالدم. قال ابن سماعة فقلت لمحمد : إنك قلت في الأصل إن القارن لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط وسعى ولم يطف لحجته حتى وقف إنه يتم طواف العمرة يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه فقد أوجبت الإتمام وما أوجبت الدم. قال محمد: لأن هناك قدم شيئاً على شيء، وهنا الفساد وجد في جميع الطواف فإن لم نجوز وأبطلنا طوافه لرفضنا عمرته بمنزلة من لم يطف ا هـ . وقيد بكون طواف العمرة كله محدثاً والأكثر كالكل لأنه لو طاف أقله محدثاً وجب عليه لكل شوط نصف صاع من حنطة إلا إذا بلغت قيمته دماً فينقص منه ما شاء، ولو طاف أقله جنباً وجب عليه دم وتجب الإعادة في
مخالف لما في الفتح عن المحيط ونصه : لو طاف للعمرة جنباً أو محدثاً فعليه شاة، ولو ترك من طواف العمرة شوطاً فعليه دم لأنه لا مدخل للصدقة في العمرة ا هـ . وفي اللباب : ولو طاف للعمرة كله أو أكثره أو أقله ولو شوطاً جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء أو محدثاً فعليه شاة، لا فرق فيه بين الكثير والقليل والجنب والمحدث لأنه لا مدخل في طواف العمرة للبدنة ولا للصدقة بخلاف طواف الزيارة، وكذا لو ترك منه أي من طواف العمرة أقله ولو شوطاً فعليه دم وإن أعاده سقط عنه الدم ا
هـ. 
الإمام أو ترك الوقوف بمزدلفة أو رمي الجمار كلها أو رمى يوم أو أخر الحلق أو
أن
الحدثين كما في الظهيرية. وينبغي أن يكون هذا على الضعيف، أما على الصحيح من الإعادة فيما إذا طاف للركن محدثاً، إنما هي مستحبة، ففي طواف العمرة أولى. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم ما إذا ترك الأقل من طواف العمرة وصرح في الظهيرية بلزوم الدم، ولهذا لو طاف للعمرة في جوف الحجر ولم يعد حتى رجع إلى أهله لزمه دم لأنه ترك من الطواف ربعه لأن الحجر ربع البيت، وإذا كان ذلك في طواف العمرة ففي طواف الفرض أولى. وأما في الطواف الواجب إذا دخل في جوف الحجر فإنه ينبغي أن تجب فيه الصدقة. كذا ذكر الشارح. ولا ينبغي التعبير بـ«ينبغي لأن المصنف في المختصر قد صرح بلزوم الصدقة بترك الأقل من طواف الصدر، وينبغي أن لا فرق بين الطواف الواجب والتطوع في لزوم الصدقة لما أن الطواف وراء الحطيم واجب في كل طواف.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses. With repetition, and he is not commanded to return if he has gone back to his family because the tahlul occurred by performing the rukn with shaving and the deficiency is minor. As long as he is in Makkah, he repeats the tawaf because it is the original, and it is better to repeat the sa'y because it is subsidiary to tawaf. If he does not repeat it, there is nothing upon him, and that is the correct view because purity is not a condition in sa'y, and it occurred after a valid tawaf. Its repetition is to compensate for the deficiency like the obligation of blood, not because the first is invalidated. If the author had said 'muhdith or junub' it would be better because there is no difference between the two hadaths in tawaf al-umrah as in al-Muhit and others. By qiyas, he is not content with a sheep when he performed tawaf for his umrah while junub because the ruling of the offense is more severe due to the hadath as in tawaf al-ziyarah, but he was content with it by istihsan because tawaf al-ziyarah is above tawaf al-umrah. Obliging the severer blood (camel) in tawaf al-ziyarah was for two meanings: the insistence of the tawaf and the severity of janabah. When one of the two meanings is found without the second, obliging the severer blood is impossible, so we restrict to the sheep. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. In al-Muhit: If a qarin performed two tawafs and two sa'ys while muhdith, he repeats the tawaf of umrah before the day of Nahr, and nothing upon him due to compensation by its like in its time. If he does not repeat until dawn of the day of Nahr, then a blood (sheep) is due for the tawaf of umrah muhdith and the time for qada' has passed. He performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah on the day of Nahr and sa'y after it as a recommendation so that raml and sa'y occur after a complete tawaf. If he does not repeat, nothing upon him because sa'y occurred after a valid tawaf, since minor hadath does not prevent validity. In janabah, if he does not repeat, there is (a sheep) for the sa'y, and similarly for menstruating woman. End. So the conclusion is that their statement 'the mutamir repeats the tawaf' applies when he is not a qarin. As for the qarin, if the day of Nahr enters, there is no repetition. Muhammad explained as narrated by Ibn Badar in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: that if he repeated, his umrah would be invalidated because he would be rejecting her by staying, and it is confirmed, so redress by its like is not possible, so it is compensated by blood. Ibn Sama'ah said: I said to Muhammad: You said in al-Asl that if the qarin performed tawaf for her four circuits and sa'y and did not perform tawaf for his hajj until he stood, then he completes tawaf al-umrah on the day of Nahr and nothing upon him; you obligated completion and not blood. Muhammad said: because there he preceded something over something; here the corruption is found in all of the tawaf; if we do not allow and nullify his tawaf, we reject his umrah, like one who did not perform tawaf. End. It is conditioned that all of tawaf al-umrah is muhdith, and the majority is like all because if he performs the minimum (part) muhdith, for each circuit half a sa' of wheat is due upon him, unless its value reaches blood, then he deducts from it what he wishes. If he performs the minimum junub, blood is due upon him and repetition is obligatory. Contrary to what is in al-Fath from al-Muhit: its text: If he performed tawaf for umrah junub or muhdith, upon him a sheep; if he left one circuit of tawaf al-umrah, upon him blood because there is no room for charity in umrah. End. In al-Lubab: If he performed tawaf for umrah all of it or most of it or part of it even one circuit while junub, menstruating, postpartum, or muhdith, upon him a sheep; no difference between much and little, junub and muhdith because there is no room for camel or charity in tawaf al-umrah, unlike tawaf al-ziyarah. Similarly, if he left of it (i.e., of tawaf al-umrah) the minimum even one circuit, upon him blood; if he repeats, the blood drops from him. End. The imam or leaving standing at Muzdalifah or throwing all the stones or throwing on one day or delaying shaving or the two hadaths as in al-Zahiriyyah. It should be that this is upon the weak (view). As for the correct view regarding the repetition when he performed tawaf for the rukn muhdith, it is merely recommended; so in tawaf al-umrah it is more appropriate. The author did not mention the ruling of leaving the minimum of tawaf al-umrah, but it is stated in al-Zahiriyyah that blood is due. Therefore, if he performed tawaf for umrah inside the Hijr and did not repeat until he returned to his family, blood is due upon him because he left a quarter of the tawaf, as the Hijr is a quarter of the House. If that is in tawaf al-umrah, then in tawaf al-fard it is more appropriate. As for the obligatory tawaf, if he enters the Hijr, then it should be that charity is due. Thus the commentator mentioned. One should not express it with 'should' because the author in al-Mukhtasar stated explicitly that charity is due for leaving the minimum of tawaf al-sadr, and should be no difference between obligatory and voluntary tawaf in the obligation of charity because the tawaf behind al-Hatim is obligatory in every tawaf.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the rulings for a person who performs tawaf for 'Umrah while in a state of impurity (minor or major). The text begins by discussing the ruling on repetition: if the person returns to his family, he is not commanded to go back because the tawaf is valid (the deficiency is minor). But if he is still in Makkah, he should repeat the tawaf (and it is recommended to repeat the sa'y). The correct view is that if he does not repeat the sa'y, nothing is due because purity is not a condition for sa'y. The author notes that the matn's phrase 'junub or muhdith' would be better because both are the same for 'Umrah tawaf. Then, the text presents a qiyas and its override by istihsan: by analogy (qiyas), one would not suffice with a sheep (shah) for janabah, because the penalty for janabah is more severe in tawaf al-ziyarah (where a camel is due), but in 'Umrah tawaf, a sheep suffices by istihsan. The reason given is that tawaf al-ziyarah is more emphasized (wukadah) and the severity of janabah combines; for 'Umrah tawaf, only one meaning (severity of janabah) is present, so a full camel is not required. The passage then discusses the case of a qarin (performer of Qiran) who performed multiple tawafs and sa'ys while muhdith. According to Muhammad, if he does not repeat the 'Umrah tawaf until the day of Nahr, a sheep is due. Muhammad also clarifies a distinction between a case where someone did partial tawaf and then stood at 'Arafah, versus someone who did all the tawaf impure. The text also addresses the ruling for performing tawaf in the Hijr: if one does not repeat, a sheep is due because a quarter of the tawaf is missed. Finally, there is a mention that the correct view (sahih) is that repeating tawaf for the rukn when muhdith is recommended, not obligatory, so for 'Umrah it is more so. The passage emphasizes that in 'Umrah tawaf, there is no room for camel (badanah) or charity (sadaqah) — only a sheep for the entire tawaf done in impurity, and blood for leaving some circuits.

Key Terms
شاة (shāh): A sheep (or goat) that is the minimum expiation for certain violations in Hajj.
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or large animal) offered as a sacrifice or expiation, required for major violations like tawaf al-ziyarah done in janabah.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) due to stronger evidence or custom.
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim performing Qiran (combining Hajj and 'Umrah with one ihrām).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the expiation for performing the entire tawaf of 'Umrah while junub?
A) A camel (badanah)
B) A sheep (shāh)
C) Half a sa' of wheat per circuit
D) Nothing, because janabah does not affect tawaf al-umrah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-umrah performed in a state of impurity is valid but requires a sheep (shah) as expiation by istihsan, overriding the qiyas that would have required a camel.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
The Qarin's Tawaf with Impurity
Explains the qarin's ruling for tawaf al-umrah with hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a qarin who performs tawaf al-umrah in a state of impurity, and distinguish between the case where partial tawaf is completed later and where the entire tawaf is impure.

Core Idea
A qarin who performs tawaf al-umrah impure cannot repeat it after standing at Arafah; a sheep becomes due.

This lesson focuses on the special case of a qarin (pilgrim performing Qiran) who performs tawaf for 'Umrah while in a state of impurity. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq relates a dialogue between Muhammad al-Shaybani and Ibn Sama'ah, clarifying when a sheep is due and when the tawaf can be completed without expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and key actors
The scenario: a qarin performed two tawafs and two sa'ys while muhdith. The text distinguishes between before the Day of Nahr and after Fajr of the Day of Nahr.
A qarin combines Hajj and 'Umrah with one ihram. He must perform tawaf al-umrah and sa'y for 'Umrah, then tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'y for Hajj.
2
Trace the ruling before the Day of Nahr
If he repeats the tawaf al-umrah before the Day of Nahr, nothing is due because the deficiency is compensated by the repetition in its time.
This is analogous to the earlier ruling for a non-qarin: repetition removes the obligation of blood.
3
Understand the ruling if time passes
If he does not repeat until dawn of the Day of Nahr, a sheep is due for the tawaf al-umrah done muhdith. He cannot repeat because the time for qada' has passed.
The sa'y for 'Umrah is still considered valid after a complete tawaf (if the tawaf is muhdith but not junub).
4
Analyze Muhammad's distinction
Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishes between two cases: (1) a qarin who performed only four circuits of tawaf al-umrah and sa'y, then stood at Arafah—he completes the tawaf on the Day of Nahr with no blood. (2) a qarin who performed all tawaf impure—here the impurity affected the entire tawaf, so repetition is not possible, and blood is due.
The key is whether the impurity pervaded the entire tawaf or only part of it.

بالإعادة، ولا يؤمر بالعود إذا رجع إلى أهله لوقوع التحلل بأداء الركن مع الحلق والنقصان يسير، وما دام بمكة يعيد الطواف لأنه الأصل والأفضل أن يعيد السعي لأنه تبع للطواف ، وإن لم يعده فلا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح لأن الطهارة ليست بشرط في السعي وقد وقع عقب طواف معتد به وإعادته لجبر النقصان كوجوب الدم لا لانفساخ الأول. ولو قال المصنف محدثاً أو جنباً لكان أولى لأنه لا فرق بين الحدثين في طواف العمرة كما في المحيط وغيره، والقياس أنه لا يكتفي بالشاة فيما إذا طاف لعمرته جنباً لأن حكم الجناية أغلظ الحدث كما في طواف الزيارة لكن اكتفى بها استحساناً لأن طواف الزيارة فوق طواف العمرة. وإيجاب أغلظ الدماء وهو البدنة في طواف الزيارة كان لمعنيين: وكادة الطواف وغلظ أمر الجنابة، فإذا وجد أحد المعنيين دون الثاني تعذر إيجاب أغلظ الدماء فاقتصرنا على الشاة. كذا في غاية البيان. وفي المحيط ولو طاف القارن طوافين وسعى سعيين محدثاً أعاد طواف العمرة قبل يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه للجبر بجنسه في وقته فإن لم يعد حتى طلع فجر يوم النحر لزمه دم لطواف العمرة محدثاً وقد فات وقت القضاء ويرمل في طواف الزيارة يوم النحر ويسعى بعده استحباباً ليحصل الرمل والسعي عقب طواف كامل، وإن لم يعد عليه لأنه سعی عقب طواف معتد به إذ الحدث الأصغر لا يمنع الاعتداد، وفي الجنابة إن لم يعد فعليه للسعي وكذا الحائض ا هـ . فالحاصل أن قولهم إن المعتمر يعيد الطواف» محله ما إذا لم يكن قارناً، أما في القارن إذا دخل يوم النحر فلا إعادة، وعلل له محمد كما نقله ابن بدار في شرح الجامع الصغير بأنه لو أعاده لانتقضت عمرته لأنه يصير رافضاً لها بالوقوف وقد تأكدت فلا يمكن استدراك النقص بجنسه فيجبر بالدم. قال ابن سماعة فقلت لمحمد : إنك قلت في الأصل إن القارن لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط وسعى ولم يطف لحجته حتى وقف إنه يتم طواف العمرة يوم النحر ولا شيء عليه فقد أوجبت الإتمام وما أوجبت الدم. قال محمد: لأن هناك قدم شيئاً على شيء، وهنا الفساد وجد في جميع الطواف فإن لم نجوز وأبطلنا طوافه لرفضنا عمرته بمنزلة من لم يطف ا هـ . وقيد بكون طواف العمرة كله محدثاً والأكثر كالكل لأنه لو طاف أقله محدثاً وجب عليه لكل شوط نصف صاع من حنطة إلا إذا بلغت قيمته دماً فينقص منه ما شاء، ولو طاف أقله جنباً وجب عليه دم وتجب الإعادة في

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the rulings for a person who performs tawaf for 'Umrah while in a state of impurity (minor or major). The text begins by discussing the ruling on repetition: if the person returns to his family, he is not commanded to go back because the tawaf is valid (the deficiency is minor). But if he is still in Makkah, he should repeat the tawaf (and it is recommended to repeat the sa'y). The correct view is that if he does not repeat the sa'y, nothing is due because purity is not a condition for sa'y. The author notes that the matn's phrase 'junub or muhdith' would be better because both are the same for 'Umrah tawaf. Then, the text presents a qiyas and its override by istihsan: by analogy (qiyas), one would not suffice with a sheep (shah) for janabah, because the penalty for janabah is more severe in tawaf al-ziyarah (where a camel is due), but in 'Umrah tawaf, a sheep suffices by istihsan. The reason given is that tawaf al-ziyarah is more emphasized (wukadah) and the severity of janabah combines; for 'Umrah tawaf, only one meaning (severity of janabah) is present, so a full camel is not required. The passage then discusses the case of a qarin (performer of Qiran) who performed multiple tawafs and sa'ys while muhdith. According to Muhammad, if he does not repeat the 'Umrah tawaf until the day of Nahr, a sheep is due. Muhammad also clarifies a distinction between a case where someone did partial tawaf and then stood at 'Arafah, versus someone who did all the tawaf impure. The text also addresses the ruling for performing tawaf in the Hijr: if one does not repeat, a sheep is due because a quarter of the tawaf is missed. Finally, there is a mention that the correct view (sahih) is that repeating tawaf for the rukn when muhdith is recommended, not obligatory, so for 'Umrah it is more so. The passage emphasizes that in 'Umrah tawaf, there is no room for camel (badanah) or charity (sadaqah) — only a sheep for the entire tawaf done in impurity, and blood for leaving some circuits.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim performing Qiran (combining Hajj and 'Umrah with one ihrām).
نحر (Nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the Day of Sacrifice.
وقوف (wuqūf): Standing at Arafah, the essential rite of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A qarin performs the entire tawaf of 'Umrah while muhdith and does not repeat it until after the Day of Nahr. What is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the tawaf on the Day of Nahr.
B) He owes a camel (badanah).
C) He owes a sheep (shah).
D) He owes nothing because the tawaf is valid.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who performs tawaf al-umrah impure must repeat before the Day of Nahr; otherwise a sheep is due, and repetition after wuquf is not permitted.

Leaving Circuits and Tawaf in the Hijr
Explains expiation for missing circuits and Hijr tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the expiation for leaving circuits of tawaf al-umrah and for performing tawaf inside the Hijr, and distinguish between the correct (sahih) and weak views on repetition.

Core Idea
Leaving even one circuit of tawaf al-umrah requires a dam (sheep); tawaf inside the Hijr misses a quarter of the House.

This lesson covers two additional sub-rulings: the expiation for omitting part of tawaf al-umrah (e.g., leaving one circuit) and the ruling for performing tawaf inside the Hijr (the semi-circular wall). The passage also clarifies that the correct view is that repetition of tawaf when muhdith is recommended, not obligatory, for tawaf al-umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving a part of tawaf al-umrah (even one circuit) or performing tawaf inside the Hijr (which is considered leaving a quarter of the tawaf because the Hijr is part of the Ka'bah).
For leaving circuits, a dam (sheep) is due. For tawaf inside the Hijr, also a dam because a quarter of the tawaf is missed.
2
Distinguish between types of impurity
If the tawaf was done entirely in impurity (junub or muhdith), a sheep is due. If only part was done impure (e.g., part of circuits), the expiation varies: for minor impurity, half a sa' per circuit unless it reaches a dam; for major impurity, a dam.
The text from al-Lubab says there is no difference between much and little for impurity; but the earlier part mentions per-circuit expiation for partial impurity.
3
Understand the Hijr ruling
Performing tawaf inside the Hijr means the pilgrim walks inside the semi-circular wall. The Hijr is considered part of the Ka'bah, so the tawaf is incomplete. The expiation is a dam if not repeated before leaving Makkah.
This is analogous to leaving a fourth of the circuits.
4
Note the correct view on repetition
The passage concludes that the correct (sahih) view is that repetition for tawaf al-umrah done impure is merely recommended (mustahabb), not wajib. This is the weaker view compared to what was earlier stated. The stronger view (from al-Lubab) is that repetition is wajib while in Makkah.
The text mentions that in al-Zahiriyyah, it is considered weak; the correct view is that repetition is mustahabb. However, the mufta bihi seems to be the stronger view from al-Lubab.

With repetition, and he is not commanded to return if he has gone back to his family because the tahlul occurred by performing the rukn with shaving and the deficiency is minor. As long as he is in Makkah, he repeats the tawaf because it is the original, and it is better to repeat the sa'y because it is subsidiary to tawaf. If he does not repeat it, there is nothing upon him, and that is the correct view because purity is not a condition in sa'y, and it occurred after a valid tawaf. Its repetition is to compensate for the deficiency like the obligation of blood, not because the first is invalidated. If the author had said 'muhdith or junub' it would be better because there is no difference between the two hadaths in tawaf al-umrah as in al-Muhit and others. By qiyas, he is not content with a sheep when he performed tawaf for his umrah while junub because the ruling of the offense is more severe due to the hadath as in tawaf al-ziyarah, but he was content with it by istihsan because tawaf al-ziyarah is above tawaf al-umrah. Obliging the severer blood (camel) in tawaf al-ziyarah was for two meanings: the insistence of the tawaf and the severity of janabah. When one of the two meanings is found without the second, obliging the severer blood is impossible, so we restrict to the sheep. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. In al-Muhit: If a qarin performed two tawafs and two sa'ys while muhdith, he repeats the tawaf of umrah before the day of Nahr, and nothing upon him due to compensation by its like in its time. If he does not repeat until dawn of the day of Nahr, then a blood (sheep) is due for the tawaf of umrah muhdith and the time for qada' has passed. He performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah on the day of Nahr and sa'y after it as a recommendation so that raml and sa'y occur after a complete tawaf. If he does not repeat, nothing upon him because sa'y occurred after a valid tawaf, since minor hadath does not prevent validity. In janabah, if he does not repeat, there is (a sheep) for the sa'y, and similarly for menstruating woman. End. So the conclusion is that their statement 'the mutamir repeats the tawaf' applies when he is not a qarin. As for the qarin, if the day of Nahr enters, there is no repetition. Muhammad explained as narrated by Ibn Badar in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: that if he repeated, his umrah would be invalidated because he would be rejecting her by staying, and it is confirmed, so redress by its like is not possible, so it is compensated by blood. Ibn Sama'ah said: I said to Muhammad: You said in al-Asl that if the qarin performed tawaf for her four circuits and sa'y and did not perform tawaf for his hajj until he stood, then he completes tawaf al-umrah on the day of Nahr and nothing upon him; you obligated completion and not blood. Muhammad said: because there he preceded something over something; here the corruption is found in all of the tawaf; if we do not allow and nullify his tawaf, we reject his umrah, like one who did not perform tawaf. End. It is conditioned that all of tawaf al-umrah is muhdith, and the majority is like all because if he performs the minimum (part) muhdith, for each circuit half a sa' of wheat is due upon him, unless its value reaches blood, then he deducts from it what he wishes. If he performs the minimum junub, blood is due upon him and repetition is obligatory. Contrary to what is in al-Fath from al-Muhit: its text: If he performed tawaf for umrah junub or muhdith, upon him a sheep; if he left one circuit of tawaf al-umrah, upon him blood because there is no room for charity in umrah. End. In al-Lubab: If he performed tawaf for umrah all of it or most of it or part of it even one circuit while junub, menstruating, postpartum, or muhdith, upon him a sheep; no difference between much and little, junub and muhdith because there is no room for camel or charity in tawaf al-umrah, unlike tawaf al-ziyarah. Similarly, if he left of it (i.e., of tawaf al-umrah) the minimum even one circuit, upon him blood; if he repeats, the blood drops from him. End. The imam or leaving standing at Muzdalifah or throwing all the stones or throwing on one day or delaying shaving or the two hadaths as in al-Zahiriyyah. It should be that this is upon the weak (view). As for the correct view regarding the repetition when he performed tawaf for the rukn muhdith, it is merely recommended; so in tawaf al-umrah it is more appropriate. The author did not mention the ruling of leaving the minimum of tawaf al-umrah, but it is stated in al-Zahiriyyah that blood is due. Therefore, if he performed tawaf for umrah inside the Hijr and did not repeat until he returned to his family, blood is due upon him because he left a quarter of the tawaf, as the Hijr is a quarter of the House. If that is in tawaf al-umrah, then in tawaf al-fard it is more appropriate. As for the obligatory tawaf, if he enters the Hijr, then it should be that charity is due. Thus the commentator mentioned. One should not express it with 'should' because the author in al-Mukhtasar stated explicitly that charity is due for leaving the minimum of tawaf al-sadr, and should be no difference between obligatory and voluntary tawaf in the obligation of charity because the tawaf behind al-Hatim is obligatory in every tawaf.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the rulings for a person who performs tawaf for 'Umrah while in a state of impurity (minor or major). The text begins by discussing the ruling on repetition: if the person returns to his family, he is not commanded to go back because the tawaf is valid (the deficiency is minor). But if he is still in Makkah, he should repeat the tawaf (and it is recommended to repeat the sa'y). The correct view is that if he does not repeat the sa'y, nothing is due because purity is not a condition for sa'y. The author notes that the matn's phrase 'junub or muhdith' would be better because both are the same for 'Umrah tawaf. Then, the text presents a qiyas and its override by istihsan: by analogy (qiyas), one would not suffice with a sheep (shah) for janabah, because the penalty for janabah is more severe in tawaf al-ziyarah (where a camel is due), but in 'Umrah tawaf, a sheep suffices by istihsan. The reason given is that tawaf al-ziyarah is more emphasized (wukadah) and the severity of janabah combines; for 'Umrah tawaf, only one meaning (severity of janabah) is present, so a full camel is not required. The passage then discusses the case of a qarin (performer of Qiran) who performed multiple tawafs and sa'ys while muhdith. According to Muhammad, if he does not repeat the 'Umrah tawaf until the day of Nahr, a sheep is due. Muhammad also clarifies a distinction between a case where someone did partial tawaf and then stood at 'Arafah, versus someone who did all the tawaf impure. The text also addresses the ruling for performing tawaf in the Hijr: if one does not repeat, a sheep is due because a quarter of the tawaf is missed. Finally, there is a mention that the correct view (sahih) is that repeating tawaf for the rukn when muhdith is recommended, not obligatory, so for 'Umrah it is more so. The passage emphasizes that in 'Umrah tawaf, there is no room for camel (badanah) or charity (sadaqah) — only a sheep for the entire tawaf done in impurity, and blood for leaving some circuits.

Key Terms
الحجر (al-Hijr): The semi-circular wall adjacent to the Ka'bah; considered part of the original foundation of the Ka'bah by Ibrahim.
شوط (shawṭ): One circuit of tawaf (around the Ka'bah).
صاع (ṣāʿ): A unit of volume (approx. 3-4 liters) used for charity expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Leaving circuits of tawaf al-umrah or performing tawaf inside the Hijr requires a dam (sheep); the correct view is that repetition of impure tawaf is wajib while in Makkah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Ruling on Leaving Wajibat of Hajj: With and Without Excuse
States ruling on leaving wajibat with/without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving a wajib of Hajj and identify when a valid excuse exempts the pilgrim from the expiation (dam).

Core Idea
Leaving a wajib without excuse requires a sheep; with excuse, nothing is due.

In Hajj, not all obligatory acts are pillars (arkan). Some are wajibat, whose omission does not invalidate Hajj but requires an expiation (dam). However, if the pilgrim has a valid excuse, the obligation of dam is dropped. This lesson clarifies the conditions and consequences based on the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
Determine what is being discussed: leaving a wajib of Hajj (e.g., sa'y, standing at Muzdalifah, throwing stones).
2
Distinguish between leaving with and without excuse
The ruling hinges on whether the pilgrim had a valid excuse (udhr). If no excuse, dam is due; if excuse, nothing is owed.
The passage explicitly states this distinction.
3
Locate the evidence
The principle is derived from the hadith that tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf) is dropped for a menstruating woman. By analogy, other wajibat are dropped for valid excuses.
This is a qiyas from a known exception.
4
Apply the ruling to examples
Consider specific cases: leaving sa'y, standing at Muzdalifah, or throwing stones. The same rule applies—dam if without excuse, nothing if with excuse.
Partial omission of sa'y (e.g., three circuits) requires feeding half a sa' per circuit, unless it reaches the value of blood.
5
Note the partial omission rule
If only part of a wajib is left (e.g., three circuits of sa'y), the expiation is proportional: half a sa' per circuit, with a cap at the value of a sheep.
Leaving most of a wajib is treated like leaving all of it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو ترك السعي أو أفاض من عرفات قيل الإمام أو ترك الوقوف بمزدلفة أو الجمار كلها أو رمى يوم أي تجب شاة بترك واجب من واجبات الحج وقد ذكرناها كلها في أول الكتاب. أراد بالترك الترك لغير عذر، أما إذا ترك واجباً لعذر فإنه لا شيء عليه كما صرح به في البدائع في ترك السعي أنه إن تركه لعذر فلا شيء عليه، وإن بغير عذر لزمه دم لأن هذا حكم ترك الوجوب في هذا الباب أصله طواف الصدر حيث سقط عن الحائض بالحديث، وصرح في الهداية بأن في ترك الوقوف بمزدلفة بغير عذر رد ما لا لعذر، وصرح الولوالجي في فتاواه بأنه لو سعى راكباً من غير عذر لزمه دم إن لم يعده لأن المشي واحب وترك الواجب من غير عذر يوجب الدم، ولو أعاده بعد ما حل وجامع لم يلزمه دم لأن السعي غير مؤقت في نفسه إنما الشرط أن يأتي به بعد الطواف وقد وجد ا هـ. وكذا لو أتى به بعد ما رجع إلى أهله وعاد إلى مكة لكنه يعود بإحرام جديد كذا ذكره الأسبيجابي. وقيد بتركه لأنه لو ترك ثلاثة أشواط أطعم لكل شوط نصف صاع إلا أن يبلغ دماً فينقص منه ما شاء وترك أكثره كترك كله، وقد قدمنا أن من الواجبات في السعي الابتداء بالصفا فلو بدأ بالمروة لزمه .دم وأراد بالإفاضة قبل الإمام الدفع من عرفات قبل غروب الشمس، سواء كان الإمام أو وحده، وسواء كان الإمام أو غيره، لما أن استدامة الوقوف إلى غروب الشمس.
قوله: (أما إذا ترك واجباً لعذر فإنه لا شيء عليه الخ) قيد بالواجب لأنه لو ارتكب محذوراً لعذر فإنه لا يسقط الجزاء كما في اللباب وسيأتي ثم اعلم أن المراد بالعذر هنا ما لا يكون من جهة العباد كما حققه المؤلف آخر باب الإحصار، وذكر مثله في شرح اللباب عند قول اللباب «ولو فاته الوقوف أي بمزدلفة بإحصار فعليه دم فقال : هذا غير ظاهر لأن الإحصار من جملة الإعذار اللهم إلا أن يقال: إن هذا مانع من جانب المخلوق فلا تأثير في إسقاط دم الوجوب الألهي. ويدل عليه
His statement: (Or leaving sa'y, or departing from 'Arafat before the Imam, or leaving standing at Muzdalifah, or throwing all of the stones, or throwing one day) meaning a sheep is obligatory for leaving an obligatory act among the obligatory acts of Hajj, and we have mentioned them all in the beginning of the book. By 'leaving' he means leaving without an excuse. As for leaving an obligatory act due to an excuse, nothing is upon him, as stated in al-Bada'i' regarding leaving sa'y: if he leaves it due to an excuse, nothing upon him; if without excuse, blood is due. Because this is a ruling of leaving an obligation in this chapter; its original is tawaf al-sadr, which is dropped from the menstruating woman by hadith. In al-Hidayah, it is stated that leaving standing at Muzdalifah without excuse, he returns (?) something? [text unclear]. Al-Walwālījī stated in his fatāwā: if he performed sa'y riding without excuse, blood is due if he does not repeat it, because walking is obligatory, and leaving an obligatory act without excuse necessitates blood. If he repeats it after he has become halal (tahallul) and had intercourse, blood is not due because sa'y is not time-bound in itself; the condition is that it comes after tawaf, and that has occurred. End. Similarly, if he does it after returning to his family and comes back to Makkah, but he returns with a new ihrām, thus mentioned by al-Asbijābī. It is conditioned by his leaving (most of it) because if he leaves three circuits, he feeds half a sa' for each circuit, unless it reaches the value of blood, then he deducts from it whatever he wishes. Leaving most of it is like leaving all of it. And we have stated that among the obligatory acts in sa'y is starting from al-Safā; if he starts from al-Marwah, blood is due. And by 'departing before the Imam' he means departing from 'Arafat before sunset, whether it is the Imam or alone, and whether it is the Imam or someone else, because continuation of standing until sunset (is obligatory). His statement: (As for leaving an obligatory act due to an excuse, nothing upon him, etc.) He restricted it to obligatory (wajib) because if he commits a prohibited act due to an excuse, the penalty is not dropped, as in al-Lubab, and it will come later. Then know that the intent here by 'excuse' is what is not from the direction of the servants, as the author verified at the end of the chapter of ihsar. And he mentioned similar in Sharh al-Lubab at the statement of al-Lubab: 'If he missed standing at Muzdalifah due to ihsar, then upon him a sheep.' He said: This is not apparent because ihsar is part of excuses, unless it is said that this is a prevention from the side of the creature, so it has no effect in dropping the blood of the divine obligation. And it indicates...
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling that a sheep (shah) is due for leaving any obligatory act (wajib) of Hajj, such as sa'y, standing at Muzdalifah, throwing stones, etc. The commentator clarifies that this applies only when the act is left without a valid excuse. If there is an excuse (like illness or coercion), then no expiation is required. Evidence for this is from the principle established for tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf), which is dropped for a menstruating woman by hadith. The text also discusses details: if someone performs sa'y riding without excuse, blood is due unless he repeats it after becoming lawful (halal). Similarly, if someone performs sa'y after returning home and re-enters Makkah with a new ihrām, the same ruling applies. The commentator also notes that partially leaving sa'y (e.g., three circuits) requires charity (half sa' per circuit) unless the total value reaches the worth of blood, then one may deduct. Starting sa'y from al-Marwah instead of al-Safa also incurs blood. The passage also addresses the definition of 'excuse' (udhr): it refers to factors beyond the servant's control, such as being forced or prevented (ihsar). The commentator references al-Walwaliji and al-Asbijabi, and concludes with a discussion about the difference between leaving a wajib and committing a prohibited act with excuse.

Key Terms
واجب الحج (wājib al-ḥajj): An obligatory element of Hajj that is not a rukn; its omission requires expiation.
عذر (ʿudhr): A valid excuse such as illness, coercion, or menstruation that exempts one from the expiation for leaving a wajib.
دم (dam): Blood, specifically a sheep (shah) as expiation for violating a Hajj obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim is forced (mukrah) to miss the standing at Muzdalifah (without any fault of his own), what is the ruling?
A) He must sacrifice a sheep because he left a wajib.
B) No expiation is required because he had a valid excuse.
C) He must feed half a sa' per circuit missed.
D) His Hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A wajib of Hajj left without excuse requires a sheep; a valid excuse drops the obligation.

Penalty for Abandoning a Wajib of Hajj: General Rule and Excuse
General rule on wajib abandonment and excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that abandoning a wajib of Hajj without a valid excuse requires a dam, and identify which excuses waive the penalty.

Core Idea
Abandoning a wajib without excuse incurs a dam; with a valid excuse, no penalty.

The passage establishes a key principle: every wajib of Hajj, if omitted without a valid excuse, requires a blood penalty (dam). This lesson unpacks that rule, defines what counts as a wajib, and clarifies when an excuse—such as illness or coercion from a non-human source—waives the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage states: 'or he abandons the sa'y, or leaves Arafat before the Imam, or abandons standing at Muzdalifah, or all the stoning, or stoning one day' — meaning a sheep is obligatory for abandoning any wajib of Hajj. Note that the penalty applies only to wajibat, not to arkan or sunan.
Wajibat include sa'y, standing at Muzdalifah, stoning, halq, tawaf al-ziyarah, etc.
2
Determine the condition for the penalty
The penalty is only due if the abandonment is 'without excuse'. The passage explicitly mentions: 'As for if he abandons an obligatory act due to an excuse, then there is nothing upon him.'
An excuse is something beyond the pilgrim's control, like illness or being prevented by an enemy (specifically with illness, not enemy coercion? The text distinguishes further).
3
Identify what counts as an excuse
The commentary elaborates: excuse here means something that does not come from the servant's own doing, such as illness. Coercion by an enemy (ihsar) is not considered a valid excuse for dropping the penalty for leaving a wajib, because it is a constraint from creation, not from Allah. The author cites the principle that ihsar by enemy does not waive the penalty for violating ihram prohibitions.
Thus, only excuses that are 'from Allah' (natural causes) waive the penalty, not those caused by humans.
4
Apply the rule to an example
Consider a pilgrim who abandons sa'y entirely without any excuse: he must slaughter a sheep. If he abandons it due to severe illness, no penalty is due. If he is prevented by an enemy from completing sa'y, he still owes the dam because the enemy's coercion is not a valid excuse.
This distinction is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
